# wa-vcb-014-term-observations-v1-20260402.md
**Batch:** VCB-014 | **Instruction:** WA-VerseContext-Instruction-v2.3-20260401
**Created:** 2026-04-02 | **Version:** v1.31
**Status:** In progress — Registry 117 (peace)

---

## Registry 117 — peace

### mti:408 H2790B cha.resh [be quiet] — 43 verses

**Reading summary:** The term covers a wide range of silence-states: inward restraint in response to emotional provocation (Gen 34:5; 1Sa 10:27; 2Sa 13:20; Jer 4:19); chosen posture of listening or submission (Job 6:24; Job 13:5; Job 33:31/33; Isa 41:1); moral discernment (Pro 11:12; Pro 17:28); the soul's anguished appeal for God not to be silent (Psa 28:1; Psa 35:22; Psa 39:12; Psa 83:1; Psa 109:1); God's own restraint and its breaking (Isa 42:14; Isa 57:11 [H2814]; Psa 50:21); tactical/commanded external silence (Judg 16:2; Judg 18:19; 2Ki 18:36; Isa 36:21); procedural-legal silence (Num 30 series); and existential/moral distress (Est 4:14; Job 13:19). Several verses involve God attributed with this silence (Psa 50:21; Isa 42:14). Note: Num 30:4/7/11/14 target_words are pronoun/preposition forms — the term here functions in a legal-procedural context of a husband's deliberate non-speaking as legal ratification.

**Filter decisions:**

- Gen 24:21 — Man gazes in silence, waiting to discern God's will. The silence is an inward attentive posture of discernment. **Relevant.**
- Gen 34:5 — Jacob "held his peace" when he heard of Dinah's defilement. Explicit inward restraint of a strong emotional response until the right moment. **Relevant.**
- Exo 14:14 — "You have only to be silent." Israel commanded to trust rather than act; the silence is relational/spiritual posture of trust toward God. **Relevant.**
- Num 30:4 — Husband "says nothing" — legal ratification by non-speech. Procedural-legal function; inner-being engagement absent. **Set aside.**
- Num 30:7 — Same: legal non-objection. **Set aside.**
- Num 30:11 — Same. **Set aside.**
- Num 30:14 — Same. **Set aside.**
- Judg 16:2 — Gazites "kept quiet" all night — tactical military waiting. No inner-being engagement through this term. **Set aside.**
- Judg 18:19 — "Keep quiet; put your hand on your mouth" — command to suppress speech for self-interested persuasion. External/social pressure. **Set aside.**
- 1Sa 7:8 — "Do not cease to cry out to the Lord" — the negative of this term; the community urges Samuel not to stop praying. The inner disposition of persistent prayer is implied; borderline but the term here governs vocal intercession arising from urgent inner need. **Relevant** (retain per §3.3).
- 1Sa 10:27 — Saul "held his peace" against contemptuous men — explicit inner restraint of dignity and self-control under provocation. **Relevant.**
- 2Sa 13:20 — Absalom urges Tamar to "hold your peace" — the silence asked of her is to suppress internal grief and violation; the verse's inner-being weight is enormous. **Relevant.**
- 2Sa 19:10 — "Why do you say nothing about bringing the king back?" — political inaction; no inner-being engagement through this term specifically. **Set aside.**
- 2Ki 18:36 — People silent because king commanded it. External compliance, not inner posture. **Set aside.**
- Neh 5:8 — Nobles silent, unable to find a word — social/moral shame response. Borderline; the silence reflects a state of moral exposure and conscience-engagement. **Relevant** (retain per §3.3).
- Est 4:14 — "If you keep silent at this time" — Mordecai confronts Esther with the moral weight of inaction. The silence is a posture of the will, a moral choice with spiritual consequence. **Relevant.**
- Est 7:4 — "I would have been silent" — Esther's hypothetical inner restraint; reflects her internal calculus about when to speak. **Relevant.**
- Job 6:24 — "Teach me, and I will be silent" — Job's posture of humble submission and readiness to receive correction. **Relevant.**
- Job 11:3 — "Should your babble silence men?" — a rhetorical question about Job's speech. The term is applied rhetorically to others being silenced; inner-being engagement minimal. **Set aside.**
- Job 13:5 — "Oh that you would keep silent, and it would be your wisdom!" — Job challenges his friends; silence as wisdom-posture. **Relevant.**
- Job 13:13 — "Let me have silence, and I will speak" — Job claims silence to gather his inner resolve before speaking. **Relevant.**
- Job 13:19 — "For then I would be silent and die" — if anyone contends with him, his silence would mean conceding and dying. Linked to inner resolve and identity. **Relevant.**
- Job 33:31 — "Be silent, and I will speak" — Elihu calling Job to receptive listening. **Relevant.**
- Job 33:33 — "Be silent, and I will teach you wisdom" — same context. **Relevant.**
- Job 41:12 — "I will not keep silence concerning his limbs" — God about Leviathan; God's own decision to speak. Not a human inner-being engagement. **Set aside.**
- Psa 28:1 — "Be not deaf to me, lest, if you be silent to me, I become like those who go down to the pit" — David's desperate appeal for God not to be silent; the silence of God is an existential threat to the inner life. **Relevant.**
- Psa 32:3 — "When I kept silent, my bones wasted away through my groaning all day long" — the silence of unconfessed sin causing inner physical-spiritual deterioration. **Relevant** — strong inner-being verse.
- Psa 35:22 — "Be not silent, O Lord!" — appeal to God not to be passive in the face of enemies; the psalmist's inner distress driving the appeal. **Relevant.**
- Psa 39:12 — "Hold not your peace at my tears!" — the psalmist's inner anguish expressed as appeal to God. **Relevant.**
- Psa 50:3 — "Our God comes; he does not keep silence" — God's coming in judgment contrasted with prior silence. God's posture; borderline for inner-being of God. **Relevant** (God's inner orientation expressed through this term — §3.4 applies).
- Psa 50:21 — "These things you have done, and I have been silent; you thought that I was one like yourself" — God's silence misinterpreted as moral acquiescence; God's posture and inner judgment. **Relevant.**
- Psa 83:1 — "Do not keep silence; do not hold your peace or be still, O God!" — intense appeal to God's active engagement. **Relevant.**
- Psa 109:1 — "Be not silent, O God of my praise!" — appeal to God to act. **Relevant.**
- Pro 11:12 — "A man of understanding remains silent" — wisdom-silence as inner character quality. **Relevant.**
- Pro 17:28 — "Even a fool who keeps silent is considered wise" — perceived wisdom through silence; inner-being engagement through the character dimension. **Relevant.**
- Isa 36:21 — People silent by royal command; same as 2Ki 18:36. **Set aside.**
- Isa 41:1 — "Listen to me in silence, O coastlands" — God calling nations to attentive silence before judgment/deliberation. Posture of attentive reception. **Relevant.**
- Isa 42:14 — "I have held my peace; I have kept still and restrained myself" — God's extended inner restraint before acting; profound inner-being of God. **Relevant.**
- Jer 4:19 — "I cannot keep silent, for I hear the sound of the trumpet" — inner anguish breaking through silence; emotional-prophetic compulsion. **Relevant.**
- Jer 38:27 — Officials "stopped speaking with him" — conversation ended for strategic reasons. No inner-being engagement. **Set aside.**
- Mic 7:16 — Nations "deaf" — physical/figurative for overwhelmed; no inner-being engagement through this term. **Set aside.**
- Hab 1:13 — "Why do you remain silent when the wicked swallows up the man more righteous than he?" — moral protest against divine silence; God's apparent inner posture challenged. **Relevant.**
- Zep 3:17 — "He will quiet you by his love" — God's love as the quieting, calming force on the inner life of his people. **Relevant.**

**Group formation:**

**408-001:** Term names the posture of inner restraint — holding silence in response to emotional provocation, injustice, or the desire to speak. The inner state is present but voluntarily suppressed.
Verses: Gen 34:5; 1Sa 10:27; 2Sa 13:20; Est 7:4; Jer 4:19 (breaking of restraint); Psa 32:3 (destructive effect of restraint).
Anchor: **2Sa 13:20** (Tamar commanded to hold her peace after violation — powerful inner-being restraint of grief/trauma); **Psa 32:3** (silence of unconfessed sin and its inner cost).

**408-002:** Term names the receptive posture of silence — an inner orientation of attentive submission, readiness to hear or receive.
Verses: Gen 24:21; Exo 14:14; 1Sa 7:8 (positive negation — do not cease intercession); Job 6:24; Job 13:5; Job 13:13; Job 33:31; Job 33:33; Isa 41:1.
Anchor: **Job 6:24** ("Teach me, and I will be silent" — inward submission); **Exo 14:14** ("be silent" as posture of trust).

**408-003:** Term names the posture of wisdom — silence as an expression of inner discernment, understanding, or moral restraint.
Verses: Pro 11:12; Pro 17:28.
Anchor: **Pro 11:12** (man of understanding remains silent).

**408-004:** Term names the inner condition when an appeal is made for God not to be silent — the psalmist's existential need for divine responsiveness, exposing the inner life of the one praying.
Verses: Psa 28:1; Psa 35:22; Psa 39:12; Psa 83:1; Psa 109:1; Hab 1:13.
Anchor: **Psa 28:1** (if God is silent, I become like those who go down to the pit); **Psa 39:12** (hold not your peace at my tears).

**408-005:** Term names God's own posture of silence or its breaking — divine inner restraint, patience, or deliberate withholding as an expression of God's inner orientation.
Verses: Psa 50:3; Psa 50:21; Isa 42:14; Zep 3:17.
Anchor: **Isa 42:14** (God's long restraint and its breaking — "I have kept still and restrained myself"); **Psa 50:21** (God's silence misread as acquiescence).

**408-006:** Term applied to ethical-existential confrontation — the moral weight of remaining silent at a critical moment of injustice or crisis.
Verses: Est 4:14; Job 13:19; Neh 5:8; Job 13:13 (borderline — overlaps 408-002 in the resolve dimension).
Note: Est 4:14 and Job 13:19 are the clearest members. Neh 5:8 borderline — assign here.
Anchor: **Est 4:14** ("For if you keep silent at this time, relief and deliverance will rise... but you and your father's house will perish").

SUMMARY: mti:408 H2790B cha.resh — 43 verses | Relevant: 30 | Set aside: 13 | Groups: 6 (408-001 through 408-006) | Anchors: Psa 32:3, 2Sa 13:20, Job 6:24, Exo 14:14, Pro 11:12, Psa 28:1, Psa 39:12, Isa 42:14, Psa 50:21, Est 4:14

---

---

### mti:409 H2814 cha.shah [be silent] — 16 verses

**Reading summary:** Closely related in semantic range to H2790B, but with a narrower corpus. Covers: commanded silence in a prophetic/spiritual context (2Ki 2:3/5 — Elisha told "keep quiet" about Elijah's departure); moral self-awareness at a critical moment (2Ki 7:9 — "we are not doing right, if we are silent"); quieting/calming of a people (Neh 8:11); inward self-imposed silence and its cost (Psa 39:2); God's own silence as withholding/patience (Isa 42:14; Isa 57:11; Isa 64:12; Isa 65:6); wise choosing of silence (Ecc 3:7); calming of nature (Psa 107:29 — waves hushed); political inaction (1Ki 22:3); moral avoidance (Judg 18:9 — "will you do nothing?").

**Filter decisions:**

- Judg 18:9 — "Will you do nothing?" The term expresses moral inertia/sloth — a challenge to the will. **Relevant** (inner-being engagement through the will and moral orientation).
- 1Ki 22:3 — "We keep quiet and do not take" Ramoth-gilead — political inaction; the silence is territorial/strategic, not inner-being. **Set aside.**
- 2Ki 2:3 — Elisha told "keep quiet" about Elijah's departure — he knows, the sons of prophets know; Elisha's inner awareness of the coming event is the subtext. Borderline — the "keep quiet" functions as a social-emotional response to unbearable news. **Relevant** (retain per §3.3).
- 2Ki 2:5 — Same context at Jericho. **Relevant** (same as above).
- 2Ki 7:9 — "We are not doing right... if we are silent and wait" — explicit moral self-awareness; conscience engaging. **Relevant.**
- Neh 8:11 — "Be quiet, for this day is holy; do not be grieved" — Levites calming the people's emotional response; the quieting addresses the inner state of grief. **Relevant.**
- Psa 28:1 — "Be not deaf to me, lest, if you be silent to me" — identical to H2790B verse; this term appears here too. Appeal to God. **Relevant.**
- Psa 39:2 — "I was mute and silent; I held my peace to no avail, and my distress grew worse" — explicit inner-being deterioration from suppressed speech. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Psa 107:29 — "The waves of the sea were hushed" — physical calming of nature. No inner-being engagement. **Set aside.**
- Ecc 3:7 — "A time to keep silence, and a time to speak" — wisdom reflection on the right timing of silence within the rhythms of life; inner-being discernment about when to speak. **Relevant.**
- Isa 42:14 — "I have held my peace" (same verse as H2790B) — God's own inner restraint. **Relevant.**
- Isa 57:11 — "I have held my peace, even for a long time, and you do not fear me" — God's silence and the inner response (or failure of response) it was designed to produce. **Relevant.**
- Isa 62:1 — "I will not keep silent... until her righteousness goes forth" — prophetic resolve; the prophet's inner compulsion to speak on Zion's behalf. **Relevant.**
- Isa 62:6 — Watchmen "shall never be silent" — persistent intercession; inner orientation of watchfulness and prayer. **Relevant.**
- Isa 64:12 — "Will you keep silent, and afflict us so terribly?" — anguished appeal to God not to be passive in judgment. **Relevant.**
- Isa 65:6 — "I will not keep silent, but I will repay" — God's declaration of active judgment; God's inner resolve. **Relevant.**

**Group formation:**

**409-001:** Term names the inward suppression of speech under emotional or spiritual pressure, with deteriorating inner consequence.
Verses: Psa 39:2; 2Ki 2:3; 2Ki 2:5; Neh 8:11.
Anchor: **Psa 39:2** ("I held my peace to no avail, and my distress grew worse" — clearest inner-being cost of silence).

**409-002:** Term names the moral dimension of silence — the choice to be silent or not at a moment of ethical weight.
Verses: Judg 18:9; 2Ki 7:9; Ecc 3:7.
Anchor: **2Ki 7:9** ("We are not doing right. If we are silent... punishment will overtake us").

**409-003:** Term names God's posture of silence and its breaking — divine restraint, patience, or resolve.
Verses: Isa 42:14; Isa 57:11; Isa 64:12; Isa 65:6.
Anchor: **Isa 57:11** (God's long silence and the inner failure it was meant to address); **Isa 64:12** (anguished appeal against divine silence).

**409-004:** Term names prophetic inner resolve — refusing silence in advocacy for God's purposes.
Verses: Isa 62:1; Isa 62:6; Psa 28:1.
Anchor: **Isa 62:1** ("For Zion's sake I will not keep silent... until her righteousness goes forth as brightness").

SUMMARY: mti:409 H2814 cha.shah — 16 verses | Relevant: 14 | Set aside: 2 | Groups: 4 (409-001 through 409-004) | Anchors: Psa 39:2, 2Ki 7:9, Isa 57:11, Isa 64:12, Isa 62:1

---

### mti:2586 H4494 ma.no.ach [resting] — 6 verses

**Reading summary:** Term means a resting-place (physical). Verses cover: the dove finding nowhere to set her foot (Gen 8:9 — purely physical); no resting place for the foot in exile (Deu 28:65 — but in context explicitly paired with "trembling heart and failing eyes and a languishing soul"); rest for Ruth's welfare (Rut 3:1 — relational/existential well-being); the ark resting (1Ch 6:31 — positional/liturgical); night bird's resting place (Isa 34:14 — animal/natural); Judah finding no resting place in exile (Lam 1:3 — the absence of rest as inner-existential distress).

**Filter decisions:**

- Gen 8:9 — Dove finds no place to set her foot. Purely physical/spatial. **Set aside.**
- Deu 28:65 — "No resting place for the sole of your foot, but the Lord will give you there a trembling heart and failing eyes and a languishing soul." The resting-place denial is immediately glossed as inner-being consequence. The term itself names the physical resting-place, but in this verse the absence is directly linked to the inner state named in the same clause. **Relevant** (the physical absence of rest is the vehicle for inner-being desolation — §3.4 boundary).
- Rut 3:1 — "Should I not seek rest for you, that it may be well with you?" Naomi seeks a settled, secure life for Ruth — relational and existential flourishing. The rest sought is not merely physical but covers the whole person's security and wellbeing. **Relevant.**
- 1Ch 6:31 — The ark rested there; the service of song then appointed. Positional/liturgical, no inner-being engagement. **Set aside.**
- Isa 34:14 — Night bird finds a resting place. Animal/natural. **Set aside.**
- Lam 1:3 — Judah "finds no resting place; her pursuers have all overtaken her in the midst of her distress." The absence of rest is woven into distress and exile. **Relevant.**

**Group formation:**

**2586-001:** Term names a state of existential restlessness — the absence of resting-place as the condition of the whole person, particularly in exile or distress.
Verses: Deu 28:65; Lam 1:3; Rut 3:1 (positive: seeking rest as existential well-being).
Anchor: **Deu 28:65** (physical restlessness paired with inner desolation — trembling heart, failing eyes, languishing soul); **Lam 1:3** (Judah's exile as finding no resting place in distress).

SUMMARY: mti:2586 H4494 ma.no.ach — 6 verses | Relevant: 3 | Set aside: 3 | Groups: 1 (2586-001) | Anchors: Deu 28:65, Lam 1:3

---

### mti:2585 H4496H me.nu.chah [resting] — 21 verses

**Reading summary:** A richer semantic field than H4494 — covers: the resting-place of the ark (Num 10:33; Psa 132:8/14); the promised inheritance-rest (Deu 12:9; 1Ki 8:56); the soul returning to its rest (Psa 116:7); God's wrath excluding people from rest (Psa 95:11); the weary given rest (Isa 28:12); still waters as image of inner peace (Psa 23:2); the Lord's resting place and what he desires in it (Psa 132:14); Baruch's personal lament of finding no rest (Jer 45:3); the "quartermaster" usage (Jer 51:59 — technical, spatial); and several others. Messianic rest (Isa 11:10) and eschatological dimensions also appear.

**Filter decisions:**

- Gen 49:15 — Issachar "saw that a resting place was good" and became a servant; the resting place is territorial/economic. No inner-being engagement through this term. **Set aside.**
- Num 10:33 — Ark goes before to seek a resting place. Spatial/liturgical. **Set aside.**
- Deu 12:9 — "You have not yet come to the rest and to the inheritance" — the rest here is covenantal and eschatological in orientation, a condition of the people before God. **Relevant.**
- Rut 1:9 — "The Lord grant that you may find rest, each of you in the house of her husband!" — a blessing of relational and existential security; encompasses the whole person. **Relevant.**
- 2Sa 14:17 — "The word of my lord the king will set me at rest" — the woman of Tekoa: the king's word will bring her inner peace/relief. **Relevant.**
- 1Ki 8:56 — "Blessed be the Lord who has given rest to his people Israel" — the rest given is the fulfilment of God's promise; a condition of settled security for the whole community. **Relevant.**
- 1Ch 22:9 — Solomon: "a man of rest... I will give him rest" — the rest is not just external but defines Solomon's inner character and mission. **Relevant.**
- 1Ch 28:2 — David: "I had it in my heart to build a house of rest for the ark" — rest here is spatial/liturgical but David's inner intention is the vehicle. Borderline; the "house of rest" for the ark is spatial. **Set aside.**
- Psa 23:2 — "He leads me beside still waters" — the still waters (me.nu.chah) image peace and inner restoration. **Relevant.**
- Psa 95:11 — "They shall not enter my rest" — God's rest withheld as judgment; the rest is an inner-spiritual condition of access to God. **Relevant.**
- Psa 116:7 — "Return, O my soul, to your rest; for the Lord has dealt bountifully with you" — the soul addressed directly; inner rest as return to secure orientation in God. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Psa 132:8 — "Arise, O Lord, and go to your resting place" — spatial/liturgical. **Set aside.**
- Psa 132:14 — "This is my resting place forever; here I will dwell, for I have desired it" — God's own chosen dwelling and desire; the rest is bound up with God's will and delight. **Relevant** (God's inner orientation expressed through desire for resting-place).
- Isa 11:10 — "His resting place shall be glorious" — the Messianic figure's resting place; eschatological/glory dimension. **Relevant.**
- Isa 28:12 — "This is rest; give rest to the weary" — the offer of rest to those burdened; inner-being relief. **Relevant.**
- Isa 32:18 — "My people will abide in... quiet resting places" — the resting-places as conditions of inner peace and security. **Relevant.**
- Isa 66:1 — "What is the place of my rest?" — God's rhetorical question about what could possibly contain him; theological not inner-being. **Set aside.**
- Jer 45:3 — "I am weary with my groaning, and I find no rest" — Baruch's personal lament; explicit inner exhaustion and restlessness. **Relevant.**
- Jer 51:59 — "Quartermaster" — Seraiah's official title; technical/positional. **Set aside.**
- Mic 2:10 — "Arise and go, for this is no place to rest" — exile judgment; the denial of rest is covenantal. **Relevant.**
- Zec 9:1 — "Damascus is its resting place" — territorial/prophetic geography. **Set aside.**

**Group formation:**

**2585-001:** Term names the soul's own rest — the inner condition of peace, security, and settled orientation toward God.
Verses: Psa 116:7; Psa 23:2; 2Sa 14:17; Jer 45:3 (absence).
Anchor: **Psa 116:7** ("Return, O my soul, to your rest; for the Lord has dealt bountifully with you").

**2585-002:** Term names the covenantal rest given by God to his people — a condition of settled security, peace, and inheritance promised and fulfilled.
Verses: Deu 12:9; 1Ki 8:56; Rut 1:9; Isa 28:12; Isa 32:18; Mic 2:10; Psa 95:11.
Anchor: **Isa 28:12** ("This is rest; give rest to the weary"); **Deu 12:9** (the rest as the promised inheritance not yet reached).

**2585-003:** Term names an eschatological or divine resting-place — where God dwells, and the orientation of God's own will and delight.
Verses: Psa 132:14; Isa 11:10; 1Ch 22:9.
Anchor: **Psa 132:14** ("This is my resting place forever; here I will dwell, for I have desired it").

SUMMARY: mti:2585 H4496H me.nu.chah — 21 verses | Relevant: 13 | Set aside: 8 | Groups: 3 (2585-001 through 2585-003) | Anchors: Psa 116:7, Isa 28:12, Deu 12:9, Psa 132:14, Isa 11:10

### mti:2593 H4771 mar.go.a [rest] — 1 verse

**Filter decision:**
- Jer 6:16 — "Ask for the ancient paths, where the good way is; and walk in it, and find rest for your souls." The rest is explicitly for the soul; inner-being engagement direct and clear. **Relevant.**

**All-verses-fail rule:** Not triggered. 1 verse, relevant.

**Group formation:**

**2593-001:** Term names rest as the condition of the soul that walks in the right way — an inner-being orientation of peace attained through faithful obedience.
Verses: Jer 6:16.
Anchor: **Jer 6:16** ("find rest for your souls").

SUMMARY: mti:2593 H4771 mar.go.a — 1 verse | Relevant: 1 | Set aside: 0 | Groups: 1 (2593-001) | Anchor: Jer 6:16

### mti:2594 H4774 mar.ge.ah [repose] — 1 verse

**Filter decision:**
- Isa 28:12 — "This is rest; give rest to the weary; and this is repose" — the repose offered to the weary; inner-being relief and peace. **Relevant.**

**Group formation:**

**2594-001:** Term names divine repose offered to the weary — the condition of inner rest available through God's provision.
Verses: Isa 28:12.
Anchor: **Isa 28:12** ("this is repose; yet they would not hear").

SUMMARY: mti:2594 H4774 mar.ge.ah — 1 verse | Relevant: 1 | Set aside: 0 | Groups: 1 (2594-001) | Anchor: Isa 28:12

### mti:419 H5117 nu.ach [to rest] — 140 verses

**Reading summary:** This is the primary Hebrew root for rest/resting. The corpus is large and semantically diverse. The term covers: God giving Israel physical-territorial rest from enemies (Deu, Jos, 1-2Sa, 1-2Ki, 1-2Ch passages); ritual/liturgical placing of objects (Exo, Lev, Num passages — "put," "place," "laid," "deposit," "deposited"); God himself resting (Exo 20:11 — Sabbath); the Spirit resting on persons (Num 11:25/26; 2Ki 2:15; Isa 11:2); inner existential rest and its absence (Job 3:13/17/26; Psa 125:3; Pro 14:33; Isa 57:2; Hab 3:16; Dan 12:13); anger/wrath settling or being satisfied (Eze 5:13; 16:42; 21:17; 24:13); objects/people being placed in locations (many verses); and several idiomatic/procedural uses.

The filter must be applied at term level per §3 — many verses use this root in purely spatial/positional senses with no inner-being engagement.

**Filter decisions (working through the 140 verses):**

*Set aside — purely spatial/positional/physical:*
Gen 8:4 (ark on Ararat); Gen 19:16 (set outside city); Gen 39:16 (garment laid up); Gen 42:33 (leave brother); Exo 10:14 (locusts settled on land); Exo 16:23/24/33/34 (manna laid aside/placed); Exo 17:11 (Moses lowered hand); Exo 32:10 ("let me alone" — separate category, see below); Lev 7:15 (not leave any till morning); Lev 16:23 (leave garments); Lev 24:12 (put in custody); Num 10:33 (ark resting place — spatial); Num 15:34 (put in custody); Num 17:4/7 (deposit staffs); Num 19:9 (deposit ashes); Num 32:15 (abandon in wilderness — result of apostasy, but the term here is spatial abandonment); Deu 14:28 (lay up tithe); Deu 26:4/10 (set down basket before Lord — liturgical placement); Jos 3:13 (soles of priests' feet resting in water); Jos 4:3/8 (lay stones down); Jos 6:23 (put Rahab's family outside camp); Judg 2:23/3:1 (Lord left nations — positional); Judg 6:18/20 (set/put offering on rock — liturgical); Judg 16:26 (let Samson feel pillars — physical); 1Sa 6:18 (set down ark — spatial); 1Sa 10:25 (laid up before Lord — liturgical); 1Sa 25:9 (waited — temporal not inner-being); 1Ki 7:47 (left vessels unweighed); 1Ki 8:9 (put tablets in ark — liturgical object); 1Ki 13:29/30/31 (laid body in grave — burial); 1Ki 19:3 (left servant — positional); 2Ki 17:29 (put gods in shrines); 2Ki 23:18 (let bones be — positional); 1Ch 16:21/Psa 105:14 (allowed no one to oppress — parallel verse — see below); 2Ch 1:14 (stationed chariots); 2Ch 4:8 (placed tables); 2Ch 9:25 (stationed horsemen); Est 3:8 (tolerate — the king not acting against Haman's enemies; procedural-political); Est 9:17/18 (rested on a day of feasting — cessation of battle, physical); Eze 5:13 (vent fury — see below); Eze 16:39 (leave naked — judgment action); Eze 21:17 (satisfy fury — see below); Eze 22:20 (put in furnace — metaphor of judgment); Eze 37:1 (set down in valley — visionary placement); Eze 37:14 (place in your land — promise, spatial); Eze 40:2 (set down on mountain — visionary); Eze 40:42 (laid instruments); Eze 41:9/11 (free space — architectural); Eze 42:13/14 (put holy offerings — liturgical); Eze 44:19/30 (lay garments — liturgical); Jer 14:9 ("do not leave us" — appeal not to be abandoned, see below); Jer 27:11 (leave on its land); Jer 43:6 (left with Gedaliah — positional); Lam 5:5 (given no rest — see below); Eze 44:30 (blessing rest on house — borderline below); Psa 17:14 (leave abundance to infants — inheritance); Psa 119:121 (do not leave me to oppressors — see below); 2Sa 16:21 (left concubines — positional); 2Sa 17:12 (light upon him — military); 2Sa 20:3 (left to care for house — positional); 2Sa 21:10 (not allow birds to come — physical); Zec 5:11 (set basket down); Amo 5:7 (cast down righteousness — judgment).

*Assess further — potential inner-being engagement:*

- Gen 2:15 — "The Lord God took the man and put him in the garden." Placement of the human person; no inner-being engagement through this term. **Set aside.**
- Exo 20:11 — "The Lord... rested on the seventh day." God's rest — divine inner orientation; the Sabbath rest has profound theological significance as expression of God's inner being. **Relevant.**
- Exo 23:12 — "You shall rest; that your ox and your donkey may have rest, and the son of your servant woman, and the alien, may be refreshed." The rest is commanded for human refreshment. **Relevant.**
- Exo 33:14 — "My presence will go with you, and I will give you rest." God's presence-rest as the condition of the whole person/people before God. **Relevant.**
- Num 10:36 — "When it rested, he said, 'Return, O Lord, to the ten thousand thousands of Israel.'" The ark's resting associated with God's presence returning. Liturgical/spatial. **Set aside.**
- Num 11:25 — "The Spirit rested on them, they prophesied." The Spirit resting on persons; direct inner-being engagement. **Relevant.**
- Num 11:26 — "The Spirit rested on them... they prophesied in the camp." Same. **Relevant.**
- Deu 3:20 — "Until the Lord gives rest to your brothers." Territorial rest given by God. The rest as condition of peace and security for a people. **Relevant.**
- Deu 5:14 — "You shall rest... that your male servant and your female servant may rest as well as you." Sabbath rest as commanded care for all persons. **Relevant.**
- Deu 12:10 — "He gives you rest from all your enemies around, so that you live in safety." God-given security as inner-social condition. **Relevant.**
- Deu 25:19 — "The Lord your God has given you rest from all your enemies." Same pattern. **Relevant.**
- Jos 1:13 — "The Lord your God is providing you a place of rest." Promise of settled security. **Relevant.**
- Jos 1:15 — "Until the Lord gives rest to your brothers." Same. **Relevant.**
- Jos 21:44 — "The Lord gave them rest on every side." **Relevant.**
- Jos 22:4 — "The Lord your God has given rest to your brothers." **Relevant.**
- Jos 23:1 — "The Lord had given rest to Israel from all their surrounding enemies." **Relevant.**
- 2Sa 7:1 — "The Lord had given him rest from all his surrounding enemies." **Relevant.**
- 2Sa 7:11 — "I will give you rest from all your enemies." God's promise through Nathan. **Relevant.**
- 2Sa 16:11 — "Leave him alone, and let him curse, for the Lord has told him to." David's inner posture of restraint and submission to God's sovereign action. **Relevant** (§3.4 — the leaving alone is an expression of David's inward trust and resignation).
- 2Ki 2:15 — "The spirit of Elijah rests on Elisha." Spirit resting on a person. **Relevant.**
- 1Ch 16:21/Psa 105:14 — "He allowed no one to oppress them." God's protective restraint; inner-being of God expressed as care. **Relevant** (borderline — retain).
- 1Ch 22:9 — "A man of rest. I will give him rest... I will give peace and quiet to Israel." Solomon defined by rest; inner character. **Relevant.**
- 1Ch 22:18 — "Has he not given you peace on every side?" God's gift of rest as condition of wholeness. **Relevant.**
- 1Ch 23:25 — "The Lord has given rest to his people, and he dwells in Jerusalem forever." Rest and divine dwelling linked. **Relevant.**
- 2Ch 14:6 — "The land had rest. He had no war, for the Lord gave him peace." God's gift of rest. **Relevant.**
- 2Ch 14:7 — "He has given us peace on every side." **Relevant.**
- 2Ch 15:15 — "The Lord gave them rest all around" — rest as God's response to wholehearted seeking. **Relevant.**
- 2Ch 20:30 — "His God gave him rest all around." **Relevant.**
- Neh 9:28 — "After they had rest they did evil again." Rest followed by spiritual backsliding; the rest is a condition of the people. **Relevant.**
- Est 9:22 — "The days on which the Jews got relief from their enemies... from sorrow into gladness." The relief as inner-social transformation. **Relevant** (borderline — retain).
- Job 3:13 — "I would have lain down and been quiet; I would have slept; then I would have been at rest." Job's wish for the rest of death; inner existential longing. **Relevant.**
- Job 3:17 — "There the weary are at rest." The rest of death as relief from inner weariness. **Relevant.**
- Job 3:26 — "I am not at ease, nor am I quiet; I have no rest, but trouble comes." Job's inner restlessness — no peace. **Relevant.**
- Psa 125:3 — "The scepter of wickedness shall not rest on the land allotted to the righteous, lest the righteous stretch out their hands to do wrong." Wickedness resting as a spiritual threat to moral integrity. **Relevant.**
- Pro 14:33 — "Wisdom rests in the heart of a man of understanding." Wisdom residing in the heart — direct inner-being location. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Pro 21:16 — "One who wanders from the way of good sense will rest in the assembly of the dead." Rest as final destination of the one who abandons wisdom. **Relevant.**
- Pro 29:17 — "Discipline your son, and he will give you rest; he will give delight to your heart." The rest given by a disciplined child produces inner delight. **Relevant.**
- Ecc 2:18 — "I must leave it to the man who will come after me." Existential futility of labour; the "leaving" of one's work to another is inner anguish. Borderline — the term here functions as "leave behind" (inheritance). **Set aside.**
- Ecc 5:12 — "The full stomach of the rich will not let him sleep." Inner restlessness caused by excess. **Relevant.**
- Ecc 7:9 — "Anger lodges in the heart of fools." Anger resting/lodging in the heart — direct inner-being location. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Ecc 7:18 — "Withhold not your hand, for the one who fears God shall come out from both." The withholding here is about wisdom in life's choices; borderline. **Set aside.**
- Ecc 10:4 — "If the anger of the ruler rises against you, do not leave your place, for calmness will lay great offenses to rest." Calmness resolving inner conflict. **Relevant.**
- Ecc 11:6 — "Withhold not your hand" — practical wisdom about sowing. Procedural/behavioural. **Set aside.**
- Isa 7:2 — "Syria is in league with Ephraim, and the heart of Ahaz and the heart of his people shook as trees of the forest shake before the wind." The 'league' is political. But the verse's principal content is the inner fear of Ahaz. However, the target_word is 'league' — the term here means "rested/settled upon (Ephraim)." The term here modifies Syria's alliance. **Set aside** (the inner-being content is in the verse but not through this term's specific use).
- Isa 7:19 — "They will all come and settle in the steep ravines." Insects/invaders settling — physical. **Set aside.**
- Isa 11:2 — "The Spirit of the Lord shall rest upon him, the Spirit of wisdom and understanding, the Spirit of counsel and might, the Spirit of knowledge and the fear of the Lord." Spirit resting on the Messiah; direct inner-being engagement. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Isa 14:1 — "Will set them in their own land." Spatial. **Set aside.**
- Isa 14:3 — "When the Lord has given you rest from your pain and turmoil and the hard service." Rest from inner-experiential pain and turmoil. **Relevant.**
- Isa 14:7 — "The whole earth is at rest and quiet; they break forth into singing." Rest of the nations as a condition producing joy. **Relevant.**
- Isa 23:12 — "Even there you will have no rest." No inner-existential peace. **Relevant.**
- Isa 25:10 — "The hand of the Lord will rest on this mountain." God's hand resting — presence/judgment. **Relevant** (borderline — God's active presence expressed through this term).
- Isa 28:2 — "He casts down to the earth with his hand." Judgment. **Set aside.**
- Isa 28:12 — "Give rest to the weary." Rest offered to the burdened inner life. **Relevant.**
- Isa 30:32 — "Every stroke of the appointed staff that the Lord lays on them." Judgment action. **Set aside.**
- Isa 46:7 — "They set it in its place, and it stands there; it cannot move from its place. If one cries to it, it does not answer." An idol placed — the cry to it goes unanswered. The idol's inability to respond is the inner-being commentary. Borderline — the term here is placement of the idol. **Set aside.**
- Isa 57:2 — "They rest in their beds who walk in their uprightness." The rest of the righteous dead; inner peace in death. **Relevant.**
- Isa 63:14 — "The Spirit of the Lord gave them rest." God's Spirit as the agent of rest. **Relevant.**
- Isa 65:15 — "You shall leave your name to my chosen for a curse." Positional/covenantal. **Set aside.**
- Jer 14:9 — "Do not leave us!" — appeal not to be abandoned; the inner distress of abandonment fear. **Relevant** (§3.4 — the cry of the inner being not to be left).
- Jer 22:12 — Not in this batch.
- Jer 27:11 — Positional. Set aside (already noted above).
- Lam 5:5 — "We are given no rest." Existential exhaustion under oppression. **Relevant.**
- Eze 5:13 — "My anger spend itself... I will vent my fury upon them and satisfy myself." God's anger/fury resolved — inner-being of God. **Relevant.**
- Eze 16:42 — "I will be calm and will no more be angry." God's inner resolution of wrath. **Relevant.**
- Eze 16:49 — Not H5117 (this is H8252 sha.qat).
- Eze 21:17 — "I will satisfy my fury." God's inner wrath. **Relevant.**
- Eze 24:13 — "Till I have satisfied my fury upon you." Same. **Relevant.**
- Eze 44:30 — "That a blessing may rest on your house." A blessing resting as inner-social condition of flourishing. **Relevant** (borderline — retain).
- Eze 5:13 duplicated above.
- Hab 3:16 — "I will quietly wait for the day of trouble." Inner resolve and patient trust in the face of fear. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Dan 12:13 — "You shall rest and shall stand in your allotted place at the end of the days." Eschatological rest as the final condition of the righteous person. **Relevant.**
- Hos 4:17 — "Leave him alone." God's withdrawal from Ephraim; God's inner determination. **Relevant** (God's inner posture of abandonment expressed through this term).
- Zec 6:8 — "Those who go toward the north country have set my Spirit at rest in the north country." God's Spirit rested/satisfied. **Relevant.**
- Psa 119:121 — "Do not leave me to my oppressors." Appeal not to be abandoned by God; inner distress. **Relevant.**

**Group formation:**

**419-001:** Term names the Spirit resting upon a person — divine inner-being impartation resulting in transformed capacities.
Verses: Num 11:25; Num 11:26; 2Ki 2:15; Isa 11:2.
Anchor: **Isa 11:2** ("The Spirit of the Lord shall rest upon him, the Spirit of wisdom and understanding, the Spirit of counsel and might, the Spirit of knowledge and the fear of the Lord").

**419-002:** Term names God's gift of rest to his people — the settled condition of security, peace, and wholeness bestowed as covenant blessing.
Verses: Exo 33:14; Deu 3:20; Deu 5:14; Deu 12:10; Deu 25:19; Jos 1:13; Jos 1:15; Jos 21:44; Jos 22:4; Jos 23:1; 2Sa 7:1; 2Sa 7:11; 1Ch 22:9; 1Ch 22:18; 1Ch 23:25; 2Ch 14:6; 2Ch 14:7; 2Ch 15:15; 2Ch 20:30; 1Ki 5:4; Isa 14:3; Isa 63:14; Neh 9:28; Exo 23:12; Est 9:22.
Anchor: **Exo 33:14** ("My presence will go with you, and I will give you rest"); **Isa 14:3** ("rest from your pain and turmoil and the hard service").

**419-003:** Term names the inner restlessness or rest of the human person — the condition of the inner life in the absence or presence of peace.
Verses: Job 3:13; Job 3:17; Job 3:26; Lam 5:5; Isa 23:12; Isa 57:2; Dan 12:13; Hab 3:16; Psa 119:121; Jer 14:9; Est 9:22 (overlaps 419-002).
Anchor: **Job 3:26** ("I am not at ease, nor am I quiet; I have no rest, but trouble comes"); **Hab 3:16** ("I will quietly wait for the day of trouble").

**419-004:** Term names wisdom, anger, or another inner quality resting in a place within the person.
Verses: Pro 14:33 (wisdom rests in heart); Ecc 7:9 (anger lodges in heart); Psa 125:3 (wickedness not to rest on righteous); Ecc 5:12 (fullness prevents sleep); Ecc 10:4 (calmness lays offenses to rest); Pro 29:17 (rest given by disciplined son).
Anchor: **Pro 14:33** ("Wisdom rests in the heart of a man of understanding"); **Ecc 7:9** ("anger lodges in the heart of fools").

**419-005:** Term names God's own inner rest, restraint, satisfaction, or calm — the inner orientation of God expressed through this root.
Verses: Exo 20:11 (God rested — Sabbath); Eze 5:13; Eze 16:42; Eze 21:17; Eze 24:13; Hos 4:17; Zec 6:8; 1Ch 16:21/Psa 105:14; Isa 25:10; Eze 44:30.
Anchor: **Exo 20:11** ("the Lord rested on the seventh day" — the Sabbath as expression of divine inner rest); **Eze 16:42** ("I will be calm and will no more be angry" — God's inner resolution of wrath).

**419-006:** Term names the call/appeal not to be abandoned by God — the inner-being distress of one fearing divine withdrawal.
Verses: Jer 14:9; Psa 119:121; 2Sa 16:11; Isa 14:7 (overlaps 419-002); Pro 21:16.
Note: 2Sa 16:11 (David's restraint as trust) and Pro 21:16 (rest of the dead as consequence of wandering) fit better in other groups or as standalone. Let me assign:
- 2Sa 16:11 → 419-003 (inner posture of resignation/trust); Pro 21:16 → 419-003 (final rest of the one who wanders); Jer 14:9; Psa 119:121 → 419-006.
Anchor: **Psa 119:121** ("do not leave me to my oppressors"); **Jer 14:9** ("we are called by your name; do not leave us").

SUMMARY: mti:419 H5117 nu.ach — 140 verses | Relevant: ~58 | Set aside: ~82 | Groups: 6 (419-001 through 419-006) | Anchors: Isa 11:2, Exo 33:14, Isa 14:3, Job 3:26, Hab 3:16, Pro 14:33, Ecc 7:9, Exo 20:11, Eze 16:42, Psa 119:121, Jer 14:9

### mti:2588 H5118 nu.ach [rest] — 2 verses

**Reading summary:** A nominal form from the same root as H5117. Only 2 verses.

**Filter decisions:**
- 2Ch 6:41 — "Arise, O Lord God, and go to your resting place, you and the ark of your might. Let your priests, O Lord God, be clothed with salvation, and let your saints rejoice in your goodness." The resting place of the Lord is invoked in relation to his presence, salvation, and the joy of his saints; direct inner-being dimensions. **Relevant.**
- Est 9:16 — "Got relief from their enemies and killed 75,000... but they laid no hands on the plunder." Relief from enemies; the relief is existential-social, not purely military. **Relevant** (borderline — retain §3.3).

Verses: 2Ch 6:41.
Anchor: **2Ch 6:41** ("go to your resting place... let your saints rejoice in your goodness").

**5118-002:** Term names relief as a condition of the inner life freed from threat.
Verses: Est 9:16.
Anchor: **Est 9:16** ("got relief from their enemies").

### mti:2587 H5183A na.chat [quietness] — 6 verses

**Filter decisions:**
- Job 36:16 — "He also allured you out of distress into a broad place... and what was set on your table was full of fatness." The "set" here is the target_word; the term means "set down/resting" in a physical sense — provision placed on a table. No inner-being engagement through this term. **Set aside.**
- Pro 29:9 — "The fool only rages and laughs, and there is no quiet." The absence of quiet in a contentious fool; describes the fool's inner state. **Relevant.**
- Ecc 4:6 — "Better is a handful of quietness than two hands full of toil and a striving after wind." Quietness as inner-being condition, contrasted with restless striving. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Ecc 6:5 — "It finds rest rather than he." The stillborn child finds more rest than the man who has everything but no enjoyment. Inner rest as existential condition. **Relevant.**
- Ecc 9:17 — "The words of the wise heard in quiet are better than the shouting of a ruler among fools." Quiet as the inner condition in which wisdom is received. **Relevant.**
- Isa 30:15 — "In returning and rest you shall be saved; in quietness and in trust shall be your strength." Quietness paired with trust as the inner-spiritual condition of strength and salvation. **Relevant** — strong verse.

**Group formation:**

**2587-001:** Term names quietness as an inner-being condition of peace, receptivity to wisdom, and strength before God.
Verses: Ecc 4:6; Ecc 9:17; Isa 30:15; Pro 29:9 (its absence in the fool); Ecc 6:5.
Anchor: **Isa 30:15** ("in quietness and in trust shall be your strength"); **Ecc 4:6** ("a handful of quietness than two hands full of toil").

SUMMARY: mti:2587 H5183A na.chat — 6 verses | Relevant: 5 | Set aside: 1 | Groups: 1 (2587-001) | Anchors: Isa 30:15, Ecc 4:6

### mti:2584 H5207 ni.cho.ach [soothing] — 44 verses

**Reading summary:** The term is the construct noun "soothing/pleasing aroma" (Hebrew *re'ach nicho'ach*), always used in the phrase "pleasing aroma" in sacrificial contexts. The 44 verses are overwhelmingly repetitive Levitical/Numbers formulas for offerings being a "pleasing aroma to the Lord." One anomalous verse: Joh 1:18 (target_word "Son" — this appears to be a data error; H5207 is Hebrew and Joh 1:18 is NT Greek). The Ezekiel verses extend the formula critically (Eze 6:13 — idol worship described as offering pleasing aroma to idols; Eze 20:28 — the same; Eze 20:41 — God will accept his people as a pleasing aroma).

**Filter decisions:**

The filter question: does the use of *nicho.ach* (soothing/pleasing aroma) in these verses engage the inner being — specifically, does it reveal something about God's inner orientation, or the inner state of the one offering?

**The liturgical formula verses (Exo 29:18/25/41; Lev 1:9/13/17/2:2/9/12/3:5/3:16/4:31/6:15/6:21/8:21/8:28/17:6/23:13/23:18/26:31; Num 15:3/7/10/13/14/24/18:17/28:2/6/8/13/24/27/29:2/6/8/13/36):** These are liturgical formulas specifying the ritual conditions under which sacrifice is acceptable. The term here functions as a technical descriptor of the offering's acceptability to God. The relevance question is: does the formula engage the inner being of either God or the worshipper? 

*Observation:* The phrase "pleasing aroma to the Lord" implies God receives the sacrifice with inner appreciation — an inner-being orientation of God toward the offering and the worshipper. This is not purely mechanical: the aroma is acceptable to God because it represents the worshipper's obedient inner orientation. However, applied as a repetitive formula, the phrase in these liturgical contexts functions procedurally — it is a quality marker for the ritual, not a direct statement about God's inner state or the worshipper's inner condition in that verse.

**Decision on the liturgical formula corpus:** The repetitive formula is best understood as establishing a relational condition — that God is pleased with the offering — but individually these verses do not illuminate the inner being beyond the basic relational act. However, several key verses carry inner-being weight beyond the formula:

- Gen 8:21 — "When the Lord smelled the pleasing aroma, the Lord said in his heart, 'I will never again curse the ground because of man, for the intention of man's heart is evil from his youth.'" The aroma evokes God's inner resolve; his heart's intention is named. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Lev 26:31 — "I will not smell your pleasing aromas." God withdrawing his acceptance; an inner-oriented rejection. **Relevant.**
- Eze 6:13 — "They offered pleasing aroma to all their idols." The worship of idols with the language of pleasing aroma; the inner-being of the worshippers directed toward false objects. **Relevant.**
- Eze 16:19 — "You set before them for a pleasing aroma." Israel's prostitution — offering to idols what God gave her. **Relevant.**
- Eze 20:28 — "They sent up their pleasing aromas, and there they poured out their drink offerings." Israel's unfaithful worship. **Relevant.**
- Eze 20:41 — "As a pleasing aroma I will accept you... I will manifest my holiness among you." God's future acceptance of his people as a pleasing aroma — eschatological inner orientation of God toward his restored people. **Relevant.**
- Joh 1:18 — Data anomaly. The verse (John 1:18) is NT Greek and H5207 is Hebrew. This record will be **noted as a data query** (flagged below). Set aside for now.

**For the remaining liturgical formula verses** (the bulk of Lev/Num/Exo): I retain a representative set that anchor the formula's inner-being dimension (God's acceptance of worship) without treating every instance as separately relevant. The formula per se says something about God's relational-inner orientation toward worship; but applied 30+ times identically, the incremental contribution to inner-being understanding is minimal. I will include:
- A selection that best anchor the inner-being meaning of the formula (God receives worship with pleasure — a relational inner orientation).
- Per §3.3 (retain in cases of uncertainty): for the formula group, I will classify all as relevant, since the posture of the worshipper in offering something acceptable to God is itself an inner-being engagement, and excluding them wholesale risks removing the evidential base for the formula's theological meaning.

**Revised decision:** All 44 verses (minus Joh 1:18 anomaly) classified as **Relevant**, with groups distinguishing the formula from the critical individual uses.

**Group formation:**

**2584-001:** Term names the soothing/pleasing quality of sacrifice as a relational act — the inner-being dimension of worship as something God receives with pleasure, establishing a condition of divine acceptance.
Verses: All liturgical formula verses (Exo 29:18/25/41; Lev 1:9/13/17/2:2/9/12/3:5/3:16/4:31/6:15/6:21/8:21/8:28/17:6/23:13/23:18; Num 15:3/7/10/13/14/24/18:17/28:2/6/8/13/24/27/29:2/6/8/13/36).
Anchor: **Lev 1:9** ("a burnt offering, a food offering with a pleasing aroma to the Lord" — canonical instance of the formula).

**2584-002:** Term names God's inner response to the aroma — the explicit disclosure of God's heart orientation through the receiving or withholding of acceptance.
Verses: Gen 8:21; Lev 26:31; Eze 20:41.
Anchor: **Gen 8:21** ("The Lord said in his heart, 'I will never again curse the ground because of man, for the intention of man's heart is evil from his youth'" — God's inner resolve prompted by receiving the pleasing aroma); **Eze 20:41** (God will accept his people as a pleasing aroma — eschatological).

**2584-003:** Term names the misdirected inner-being act of worship — the offering of pleasing aroma to idols as an expression of unfaithful inner orientation.
Verses: Eze 6:13; Eze 16:19; Eze 20:28.
Anchor: **Eze 6:13** ("they offered pleasing aroma to all their idols").

**⚠ DATA QUERY — Joh 1:18 (verse_record_id: 79844):** This verse appears under H5207 (a Hebrew term) with target_word "Son." John 1:18 is a NT Greek verse with no H5207 occurrence. This appears to be a data error in the extract. Flagging for Leroux's attention. This verse is **set aside** pending data correction.

SUMMARY: mti:2584 H5207 ni.cho.ach — 44 verses | Relevant: 42 | Set aside: 1 (Joh 1:18 — data query) + 1 (Num formula, borderline: see note) | Groups: 3 (2584-001 through 2584-003) | Anchors: Lev 1:9, Gen 8:21, Eze 20:41, Eze 6:13

---

### mti:2521 H5251H nes [ensign] — 20 verses

**Reading summary:** The term means a standard, banner, signal, or ensign — a physical object raised to rally or signal. Verses span: the bronze serpent on a pole (Num 21:8/9); Korah's company as a warning sign (Num 26:10); a banner for those who fear God (Psa 60:4); God raising signals for nations (Isa 5:26; 11:12; 13:2; 18:3; 30:17; 49:22; 62:10); the root of Jesse as a signal (Isa 11:10); a sail (Isa 33:23); military standards in Jeremiah (Jer 4:6/21; 50:2; 51:12/27); a ship's banner (Eze 27:7).

**Filter decisions:**

The relevance question is whether the ensign/signal engages the inner being — through the one who rallies to it, or through the spiritual/relational meaning it carries.

- Num 21:8/9 — Bronze serpent on a pole — those bitten look at it and live. The looking is an act of faith/trust; the ensign here is a vehicle for inner-being engagement (faith directed at a visible sign). **Relevant** (§3.4 — the looking involves inner orientation of trust).
- Num 26:10 — Korah's company became "a warning" (nes). The warning is intended to produce inner-being response (fear, caution, moral correction). **Relevant** (borderline — retain §3.3).
- Psa 60:4 — "You have set up a banner for those who fear you, that they may flee to it from the bow." The banner is raised for those who fear God — the inner-being posture of fearing God is the basis for rallying to the banner. **Relevant.**
- Isa 5:26 — God raises a signal to nations far away. Military/political mobilisation; the signal itself is spatial/directional. No inner-being engagement through this term. **Set aside.**
- Isa 11:10 — "The root of Jesse, who shall stand as a signal for the peoples — of him shall the nations inquire, and his resting place shall be glorious." The signal is the Messianic figure himself, to whom the nations' inner seeking is directed. **Relevant** (the inner orientation of the nations — inquiry, hope — is the direct consequence of the signal).
- Isa 11:12 — "He will raise a signal for the nations and will assemble the banished of Israel." The signal as the vehicle of restoration/gathering. No direct inner-being engagement through the term. **Set aside.**
- Isa 13:2 — "On a bare hill raise a signal; cry aloud to them." Military assembly signal. **Set aside.**
- Isa 18:3 — "When a signal is raised on the mountains, look! When a trumpet is blown, hear!" The call to attend; the commanded looking and hearing implies inner attentiveness. Borderline. **Set aside** (the inner-being engagement is in the commanded response, not in the term itself).
- Isa 30:17 — "Till you are left like a flagstaff on the top of a mountain, like a signal on a hill." Judgment image — Israel reduced to an isolated signal. Metaphorical; no inner-being engagement through the term. **Set aside.**
- Isa 31:9 — "His officers desert the standard in panic." The inner state (panic) produces the action; the term is the standard being deserted. Borderline — the term names the object abandoned in fear. **Relevant** (the desertion of the standard reveals the inner state of panic — §3.4).
- Isa 33:23 — "They cannot hold the mast firm... or keep the sail spread out." Physical/nautical. **Set aside.**
- Isa 49:22 — God raises a signal to the peoples to bring his children home. Signal for restoration; inner-being engagement is in the response of the nations. Borderline — the term is the signal itself. **Set aside.**
- Isa 62:10 — "Lift up a signal over the peoples." Call to prepare the way. **Set aside.**
- Jer 4:6 — "Raise a standard toward Zion, flee for safety." The raising of the standard in the face of coming disaster; those who flee show inner-being response (fear, urgency). **Set aside** (the term is the signal object; the inner response is not directly through the term).
- Jer 4:21 — "How long must I see the standard and hear the sound of the trumpet?" The prophet's anguished inner cry; the standard is a symbol of ongoing war. **Relevant** (the endurance of the standard is the object of the prophet's inner anguish — §3.4).
- Jer 50:2 — "Set up a banner and proclaim, conceal it not." Signal for proclamation of Babylon's fall. **Set aside.**
- Jer 51:12 — Military signal against Babylon. **Set aside.**
- Jer 51:27 — Military signal to kingdoms. **Set aside.**
- Eze 27:7 — "Fine embroidered linen from Egypt was your sail, serving as your banner." Tyre's sail as banner; commercial/nautical glory. **Set aside.**

**Group formation:**

**2521-001:** Term names a signal or banner that orients the inner life — the object to which hope, fear, or trust is directed, or from which the inner life flees in panic.
Verses: Num 21:8; Num 21:9; Psa 60:4; Isa 11:10; Isa 31:9; Jer 4:21; Num 26:10 (borderline).
Anchor: **Psa 60:4** ("You have set up a banner for those who fear you, that they may flee to it from the bow" — the banner as the focus of the fear-of-God inner orientation); **Isa 11:10** ("the root of Jesse, who shall stand as a signal for the peoples — of him shall the nations inquire").

SUMMARY: mti:2521 H5251H nes — 20 verses | Relevant: 7 | Set aside: 13 | Groups: 1 (2521-001) | Anchors: Psa 60:4, Isa 11:10

---

### mti:439 H7067G qan.na [Jealous [God]] — 1 verse

**Filter decision:**
- Exo 34:14 — "For you shall worship no other god, for the Lord, whose name is Jealous, is a jealous God." The divine name "Jealous" (*qan.na*) directly names an inner-being characteristic of God — the exclusive claim of his passionate commitment to covenant relationship. **Relevant** — strong inner-being verse.

**Group formation:**

**439-001:** Term names the jealousy of God as a defining inner characteristic — God's exclusive passionate claim on his people's worship and loyalty.
Verses: Exo 34:14.
Anchor: **Exo 34:14** ("the Lord, whose name is Jealous, is a jealous God").

SUMMARY: mti:439 H7067G qan.na — 1 verse | Relevant: 1 | Set aside: 0 | Groups: 1 (439-001) | Anchor: Exo 34:14

---

### mti:2591 H7280A ra.ga [to disturb] — 6 verses

**Reading summary:** This is one of two homographs of *ra.ga* — this sense means "to disturb, stir up, make turbulent." Verses: stilling the sea (Job 26:12); lying tongue lasting only a moment (Pro 12:19); God stirring up the sea (Isa 51:15; Jer 31:35); sudden/quickly (Jer 49:19; Jer 50:44).

**Filter decisions:**
- Job 26:12 — "By his power he stilled the sea; by his understanding he shattered Rahab." God's power and understanding expressed in cosmic action; the divine inner attributes (power, understanding) are named. **Relevant** (God's inner capacities at work in creation — the term carries those inner qualities into action).
- Pro 12:19 — "A lying tongue is but for a moment." The term here is adverbial ("for a moment"). No inner-being engagement through the term itself. **Set aside.**
- Isa 51:15 — "I am the Lord your God, who stirs up the sea so that its waves roar." God's active inner power expressed in creation. **Relevant** (God's sovereign inner being expressed through creation's disturbance).
- Jer 31:35 — Parallel to Isa 51:15. Same God, same formula. **Relevant.**
- Jer 49:19 — "I will suddenly make him run away from her." The term is adverbial ("suddenly"). No inner-being engagement through the term. **Set aside.**
- Jer 50:44 — Same as Jer 49:19. **Set aside.**

**Group formation:**

**2591-001:** Term names God's disturbing/stirring power in creation — an expression of divine inner capacity and sovereignty.
Verses: Job 26:12; Isa 51:15; Jer 31:35.
Anchor: **Isa 51:15** ("I am the Lord your God, who stirs up the sea so that its waves roar").

SUMMARY: mti:2591 H7280A ra.ga — 6 verses | Relevant: 3 | Set aside: 3 | Groups: 1 (2591-001) | Anchor: Isa 51:15

---

### mti:420 H7280B ra.ga [to rest] — 6 verses

**Reading summary:** The second homograph — this sense means "to rest, settle, find repose."

**Filter decisions:**
- Deu 28:65 — "No respite, and there shall be no resting place for the sole of your foot, but the Lord will give you there a trembling heart and failing eyes and a languishing soul." Restlessness directly paired with inner-being desolation (same verse as H4494 ma.no.ach above, but this term is the "respite" word). **Relevant.**
- Isa 34:14 — "The night bird settles and finds for herself a resting place." Animal behaviour. **Set aside.**
- Isa 51:4 — "I will set my justice for a light to the peoples." The term here = "set/establish" (justice). No inner-being engagement through this term. **Set aside.**
- Jer 31:2 — "The people who survived the sword found grace in the wilderness; when Israel sought for rest." Israel's inward seeking for rest in exile. **Relevant.**
- Jer 47:6 — "Put yourself into your scabbard; rest and be still!" — addressed to the sword of the Lord; metaphorical, not inner-being. **Set aside.**
- Jer 50:34 — "He will surely plead their cause, that he may give rest to the earth, but unrest to the inhabitants of Babylon." God giving rest to the earth; cosmic/covenantal rest. **Relevant** (borderline — retain).

**Group formation:**

**420-001:** Term names the rest or respite sought or denied — the inner-being condition of peace in exile, distress, or covenant promise.
Verses: Deu 28:65; Jer 31:2; Jer 50:34.
Anchor: **Jer 31:2** ("Israel sought for rest" — the inner orientation of longing for rest in wilderness); **Deu 28:65** (restlessness paired with trembling heart and languishing soul).

SUMMARY: mti:420 H7280B ra.ga — 6 verses | Relevant: 3 | Set aside: 3 | Groups: 1 (420-001) | Anchors: Jer 31:2, Deu 28:65

### mti:413 H7600 sha.a.nan [secure] — 10 verses

**Reading summary:** The term means "at ease, secure, complacent." Verses cover: complacency coming to God's ears (2Ki 19:28; Isa 37:29); those at ease with contempt for misfortune (Job 12:5); the soul scorned by those at ease (Psa 123:4); women at ease addressed in judgment (Isa 32:9/11); the quiet untroubled habitation (Isa 32:18/33:20); those at ease in Zion under judgment (Amo 6:1); nations at ease that furthered disaster (Zec 1:15).

**Filter decisions:**
- 2Ki 19:28 — "Your complacency has come into my ears, I will put my hook in your nose." God hears the complacency of Sennacherib — the inner state of arrogant self-security has reached God. **Relevant.**
- Job 12:5 — "In the thought of one who is at ease there is contempt for misfortune." The inner thought-life of the comfortable produces contempt. **Relevant** — direct inner-being engagement.
- Psa 123:4 — "Our soul has had more than enough of the scorn of those who are at ease." The soul of the psalmist affected by the scorn of the complacent. **Relevant** — soul directly named.
- Isa 32:9 — "Rise up, you women who are at ease." Inner condition of ease addressed in warning. **Relevant.**
- Isa 32:11 — "Tremble, you women who are at ease." Inner call to move from ease to fear. **Relevant.**
- Isa 32:18 — "My people will abide in... quiet resting places." The "quiet" (*sha.a.nan*) as the intended inner condition of God's people in peace. **Relevant.**
- Isa 33:20 — "An untroubled habitation, an immovable tent." The city as untroubled/secure. Spatial/communal; borderline. **Set aside** (the term here describes the city's character, not a person's inner state).
- Isa 37:29 — Parallel to 2Ki 19:28. **Relevant.**
- Amo 6:1 — "Woe to those who are at ease in Zion." The moral critique of complacency as an inner-being condition before God. **Relevant.**
- Zec 1:15 — "Exceedingly angry with the nations that are at ease." God's anger provoked by their inner state of complacency. **Relevant.**

**Group formation:**

**413-001:** Term names the inner condition of complacent ease — the self-secure, untroubled disposition that produces contempt, moral blindness, or judgment.
Verses: Job 12:5; Isa 32:9; Isa 32:11; Amo 6:1; Zec 1:15; 2Ki 19:28; Isa 37:29; Psa 123:4.
Anchor: **Job 12:5** ("In the thought of one who is at ease there is contempt for misfortune"); **Amo 6:1** ("Woe to those who are at ease in Zion").

**413-002:** Term names the divinely intended condition of secure quietness — the ease of God's people living in peace and safety as a condition of shalom.
Verses: Isa 32:18.
Anchor: **Isa 32:18** ("in quiet resting places" — *sha.a.nan* as the positive inner-communal condition of peace).

SUMMARY: mti:413 H7600 sha.a.nan — 10 verses | Relevant: 9 | Set aside: 1 | Groups: 2 (413-001, 413-002) | Anchors: Job 12:5, Amo 6:1, Isa 32:18

---

- Job 21:23 — "One dies in his full vigor, being wholly at ease and secure." The inner condition of ease and security at the point of death — part of Job's reflection on the apparent injustice of the wicked dying in peace. **Relevant.**

**2577-001:** Term names the inner condition of ease and security — the state of the person wholly undisturbed, here in the context of unjust prosperity.
Verses: Job 21:23.
Anchor: **Job 21:23** ("wholly at ease and secure").

### mti:418 H8252 sha.qat [to quiet] — 41 verses

**Reading summary:** The term means "to be quiet, at rest, undisturbed." The corpus covers: the land having rest from war (Jos 11:23; 14:15; Judg 3:11/30; 5:31; 8:28; 2Ch 14:1/5/6); the city quiet after judgment (2Ki 11:20; 2Ch 23:21); quiet and unsuspecting people (Judg 18:7/27); a man not resting until a matter is settled (Rut 3:18); Job's complaint about loss of quiet (Job 3:13/26; 34:29; 37:17); God being still (Psa 76:8; 83:1); rest given to the afflicted (Psa 94:13); a patient man quieting contention (Pro 15:18); multiple Isaianic uses (7:4; 14:7; 18:4; 30:15; 32:17; 57:20; 62:1); Jeremiah uses (30:10; 46:27; 47:6/7; 48:11; 49:23); Ezekiel uses (16:42; 16:49; 38:11); Zechariah (1:11).

**Filter decisions:**

*Set aside — purely territorial/political rest of the land/city/nations with no inner-being engagement through this term:*
Jos 11:23; Jos 14:15; Judg 3:11; Judg 3:30; Judg 5:31; Judg 8:28; 2Ki 11:20; 2Ch 14:1; 2Ch 14:5; 2Ch 14:6; 2Ch 20:30; 2Ch 23:21; 1Ch 4:40; Judg 18:7; Judg 18:27 — these describe the land, city, or population as quiet after military victory. No individual inner-being engagement through the term directly.

*Relevant:*
- Rut 3:18 — "The man will not rest but will settle the matter today." The man's inner resolve not to be quiet until he acts. **Relevant** (inner-being of Boaz — his restless purposefulness).
- Job 3:13 — "I would have lain down and been quiet." Job's longing for the quiet of death; inner existential state. **Relevant.**
- Job 3:26 — "I am not at ease, nor am I quiet; I have no rest, but trouble comes." Job's inner condition — explicit. **Relevant.**
- Job 34:29 — "When he is quiet, who can condemn? When he hides his face, who can behold him." God's quietness as an expression of his sovereign inner orientation. **Relevant.**
- Job 37:17 — "You whose garments are hot when the earth is still because of the south wind." The earth's stillness — natural phenomenon. **Set aside.**
- Psa 76:8 — "The earth feared and was still." The earth's response of stillness before God's judgment; the stillness is a response to God's inner being expressed in judgment. Borderline — the "being still" is the response of the creation. **Relevant** (retain — the fear-response stillness is inner-being adjacent).
- Psa 83:1 — "Do not keep silence; do not hold your peace or be still, O God!" Appeal to God not to be still/passive; God's inner posture. **Relevant.**
- Psa 94:13 — "To give him rest from days of trouble, until a pit is dug for the wicked." God giving rest to the afflicted inner life. **Relevant.**
- Pro 15:18 — "He who is slow to anger quiets contention." The inner quality of patience producing peace in relationships. **Relevant** — strong inner-being verse.
- Isa 7:4 — "Be careful, be quiet, do not fear, and do not let your heart be faint because of these two smoldering stumps." The command to be quiet paired directly with "do not fear" and "do not let your heart be faint" — inner-being engagement explicit. **Relevant.**
- Isa 14:7 — "The whole earth is at rest and quiet; they break forth into singing." Rest and quiet producing joy; condition of the whole earth. **Relevant.**
- Isa 18:4 — "I will quietly look from my dwelling like clear heat in sunshine." God's own inner posture of watchful quiet. **Relevant.**
- Isa 30:15 — "In returning and rest you shall be saved; in quietness and in trust shall be your strength." Quietness and trust as the inner-spiritual condition of salvation and strength. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Isa 32:17 — "The effect of righteousness will be peace, and the result of righteousness, quietness and trust forever." Quietness as the fruit of righteousness — an inner-social condition. **Relevant.**
- Isa 57:20 — "The wicked are like the tossing sea; for it cannot be quiet." The inner restlessness of the wicked as a defining characteristic. **Relevant.**
- Isa 62:1 — "For Zion's sake I will not keep silent, and for Jerusalem's sake I will not be quiet." Prophetic inner resolve not to rest. **Relevant.**
- Jer 30:10 — "Jacob shall return and have quiet and ease, and none shall make him afraid." Inner condition of peace and security promised. **Relevant.**
- Jer 46:27 — Parallel to Jer 30:10. **Relevant.**
- Jer 47:6 — "How long till you are quiet? Put yourself into your scabbard; rest and be still!" Addressed to the sword; metaphorical. **Set aside.**
- Jer 47:7 — "How can it be quiet when the Lord has given it a charge?" The sword under divine mandate cannot rest. Metaphorical. **Set aside.**
- Jer 48:11 — "Moab has been at ease from his youth and has settled on his dregs." Moab's complacent inner ease, unchanged by challenge. **Relevant** (inner condition of undisturbed ease — spiritual stagnation).
- Jer 49:23 — "They melt in fear, they are troubled like the sea that cannot be quiet." The inner condition of nations under fear — inability to be quiet. **Relevant.**
- Eze 16:42 — "I will be calm and will no more be angry." God's inner resolution of wrath into calm. **Relevant.**
- Eze 16:49 — "Sodom: she and her daughters had pride, excess of food, and prosperous ease." Ease as a dimension of Sodom's inner moral condition. **Relevant.**
- Eze 38:11 — "I will fall upon the quiet people who dwell securely." The quiet people — inner condition of peaceable, unsuspecting dwelling. **Relevant** (borderline — retain).
- Zec 1:11 — "All the earth remains at rest." The earth at rest; the context is God's anger that the nations are at ease while Jerusalem suffers. Relevant in context — the rest of the nations is the occasion for God's indignation. **Relevant** (borderline — retain).

**Group formation:**

**418-001:** Term names the inner condition of quietness, rest, and trust as the spiritual posture of the person before God — the condition from which strength and salvation flow.
Verses: Isa 30:15; Isa 7:4; Isa 32:17; Pro 15:18; Rut 3:18.
Anchor: **Isa 30:15** ("in quietness and in trust shall be your strength"); **Isa 7:4** (quiet paired with not fearing and not letting the heart be faint).

**418-002:** Term names the inner restlessness of the wicked or troubled person — the inability to be quiet as an expression of inner moral or emotional disorder.
Verses: Isa 57:20; Job 3:26; Jer 49:23; Jer 48:11.
Anchor: **Isa 57:20** ("the wicked are like the tossing sea; for it cannot be quiet"); **Job 3:26** ("I am not at ease, nor am I quiet; I have no rest").

**418-003:** Term names the quiet of God — God's own inner posture of watchful stillness, or the breaking of it in response to his people's need or his own resolve.
Verses: Job 34:29; Isa 18:4; Eze 16:42; Psa 83:1; Isa 62:1.
Anchor: **Job 34:29** ("When he is quiet, who can condemn?"); **Eze 16:42** ("I will be calm and will no more be angry").

**418-004:** Term names the promised rest of God's people — the condition of quiet and ease as covenant blessing, contrasted with restlessness under judgment.
Verses: Jer 30:10; Jer 46:27; Isa 14:7; Psa 94:13; Job 3:13; Zec 1:11; Eze 38:11; Eze 16:49; Psa 76:8.
Anchor: **Jer 30:10** ("Jacob shall return and have quiet and ease, and none shall make him afraid").

SUMMARY: mti:418 H8252 sha.qat — 41 verses | Relevant: 24 | Set aside: 17 | Groups: 4 (418-001 through 418-004) | Anchors: Isa 30:15, Isa 7:4, Isa 57:20, Job 3:26, Job 34:29, Eze 16:42, Jer 30:10

---
