## Registry 120 — perverseness

### mti:5949 H2015 ha.phakh [to overturn] — 92 verses

**Reading summary:** A large, semantically diverse verb meaning "to turn, overturn, overthrow, transform." The corpus includes: physical transformations (water to blood, Exo; Sodom overthrown; physical turning of objects); changes of inner state or direction (heart changed, Exo 14:5; Saul turned into another man, 1Sa 10:6; God gave him another heart, 1Sa 10:9; mourning turned to dancing, Psa 30:11; mourning to joy, Jer 31:13); Levitical skin-disease examination (13 Lev 13 verses — physical colour changes); God's inner orientation changing toward his people (Isa 63:10 — turned to be their enemy); the heart writhing/turning (Lam 1:20; Hos 11:8); moral perversion (Amos 5:7; Amo 6:12; Jer 2:21; Jer 23:36; Pro 17:20; Pro 12:7); a dishonest tongue (Pro 17:20); Daniel's strength and appearance changed (Dan 10:8/16).

**Filter decisions:**

*Set aside — physical transformations, geographical overthrows, positional turns:*
Gen 3:24 (sword turned every way — physical/mechanical); Gen 19:21/25/29 (Sodom overthrown — geographical judgment); Exo 7:15/17/20 (water to blood — physical plague); Exo 10:19 (wind turned — meteorological); Lev 13:3/4/10/13/16/17/20/25/55 (leprosy colour changes — physical diagnostic); Gen 30:37 (*luz* = almond, not H2015); Deu 29:23 (Sodom overthrow — geographical); Jos 7:8 (Israel turned backs — military); Jos 8:20 (troops turned back — military); Judg 7:13 (bread tumbled — dream image); Judg 20:39/41 (men turned in battle — military); 1Sa 25:12 (men turned away — physical movement); 1Ki 22:34/2Ch 18:33 (king turned in chariot — physical); 2Ki 9:23 (Joram reined about — physical); 2Ki 21:13 (dish wiped — metaphorical of Jerusalem but no inner-being); 1Ch 19:3/2Sa 10:3 (spy out — political); 2Ch 9:12 (queen turned and went — physical); Job 12:15 (land overwhelmed — natural); Job 19:19 (friends turned against — relational/social, not inner); Job 20:14 (food turned in stomach — physical); Job 28:5/9 (mining/overturning mountains — physical); Job 34:25 (overturned in night — judgment); Job 37:12 (clouds turn around — meteorological); Job 38:14 (earth changed like clay under seal — cosmic); Job 41:28 (sling stones turned to stubble — physical); Psa 66:6 (sea into dry land — miracle); Psa 78:44 (rivers to blood — plague); Psa 78:9 (Ephraimites turned back — military); Psa 105:29 (waters into blood — plague); Psa 114:8 (rock into water — miracle); Psa 41:3 (restore to health — physical healing); Isa 34:9 (streams turned to pitch — judgment on land); Joe 2:31 (sun to darkness — cosmic); Hag 2:22 (overthrow kingdoms — political); Jon 3:4 (Nineveh overthrown — political prophecy); Jer 20:16 (overthrew cities — geographical); Eze 4:8 (turn from side — physical restraint); Jer 30:6 (faces turned pale — physiological reaction to fear, not the term's inner-being engagement directly); Amos 4:11 (overthrew like Sodom — geographical); Amos 5:8 (darkness into morning — cosmic); Lam 4:6 (Sodom overthrown — geographical); Lam 5:2 (inheritance turned over — political); Isa 1:7 (cities overthrown — geographical).

*Relevant — inner-being transformation or moral perversion:*

- Exo 14:5 — "The mind of Pharaoh and his servants was changed toward the people." The inner orientation of Pharaoh's mind changed. **Relevant.**
- Deu 23:5 — "The Lord your God turned the curse into a blessing for you, because the Lord your God loved you." God's active transformation on behalf of his people, motivated by love. **Relevant** (God's inner-being of love expressed through the overturn).
- Neh 13:2 — "Yet our God turned the curse into a blessing." Same pattern. **Relevant.**
- Est 9:1 — "The reverse occurred: the Jews gained mastery over those who hated them." The reversal of expectation; inner-social transformation. Borderline — the term names the reverse/overthrow of circumstances. **Relevant** (borderline — retain).
- Est 9:22 — "The month that had been turned for them from sorrow into gladness." Inner-experiential transformation from mourning to joy. **Relevant.**
- 1Sa 10:6 — "You will be turned into another man." Radical inner transformation of Saul through the Spirit. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- 1Sa 10:9 — "God gave him another heart." The heart transformed. **Relevant** — strong verse (explicit inner-being).
- 2Ki 5:26 — "Did not my heart go when the man turned from his chariot to meet you?" Gehazi's heart going with Naaman — Elisha naming the inner movement of Gehazi's covetous heart. **Relevant.**
- Job 9:5 — "He who removes mountains and overturns them in his anger." God's anger as the inner force behind the overturn; God's inner being expressed in creation. **Relevant** (God's inner state — anger — is the agent).
- Job 30:15 — "Terrors are turned upon me." Job's inner experience of terror overtaking him. **Relevant.**
- Job 30:21 — "You have turned cruel to me; with the might of your hand you persecute me." Job's experience of God's disposition turning against him — inner-relational experience. **Relevant.**
- Psa 30:11 — "You have turned for me my mourning into dancing." God transforming the inner state from mourning to joy. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Psa 32:4 — "My strength was dried up as by the heat of summer." The effect of God's hand on Job's inner strength. **Relevant** (the drying up of inner vitality).
- Psa 78:57 — "They twisted like a deceitful bow." Israel's unfaithfulness described as a twisting/turning — moral perversion as an inner character image. **Relevant.**
- Psa 105:25 — "He turned their hearts to hate his people." God turning the hearts of Egypt — inner-being transformation. **Relevant.**
- Pro 12:7 — "The wicked are overthrown and are no more." Moral consequence — overthrow of the wicked. Borderline (the overthrow may be social/existential). **Relevant** (retain).
- Pro 17:20 — "One with a dishonest tongue falls into calamity." The dishonest tongue (perverted speech from inner perversion) causing downfall. **Relevant.**
- Isa 60:5 — "Your heart shall thrill and exult, because the abundance of the sea shall be turned to you." The turning of abundance toward Zion produces inner joy. **Relevant** (the inner transformation is the direct result — heart thrills).
- Isa 63:10 — "They rebelled and grieved his Holy Spirit; therefore he turned to be their enemy." God's inner orientation turning to enmity in response to grief of his Spirit. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Jer 2:21 — "How then have you turned degenerate and become a wild vine?" Israel's moral transformation from purity to corruption — inner character change. **Relevant.**
- Jer 13:23 — "Can the Ethiopian change his skin or the leopard his spots? Then also you can do good who are accustomed to do evil." The impossibility of inner moral transformation without divine intervention. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Jer 23:36 — "You pervert the words of the living God." Deliberate inner-motivated perversion of God's word. **Relevant.**
- Jer 31:13 — "I will turn their mourning into joy." Inner transformation promised. **Relevant.**
- Lam 1:20 — "My stomach churns; my heart is wrung within me, because I have been very rebellious." The heart wrung/overturned — inner anguish of sin and its consequence. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Lam 3:3 — "He turns his hand again and again the whole day long." God's hand of affliction repeatedly turned against the sufferer; inner-relational experience of divine opposition. **Relevant.**
- Lam 5:15 — "The joy of our hearts has ceased; our dancing has been turned to mourning." The inner transformation from joy to mourning. **Relevant.**
- Eze 16:34 — Different term — this verse was under H2016 *he.phekh* below.
- Dan 10:8 — "My radiant appearance was fearfully changed." Daniel's inner vitality and outward appearance transformed by the vision. **Relevant** (inner-experiential transformation in encounter with God).
- Dan 10:16 — "By reason of the vision pains have come upon me, and I retain no strength." Inner anguish and physical/spiritual depletion from the vision. **Relevant.**
- Hos 7:8 — "Ephraim is a cake not turned." Ephraim's moral incompleteness — not fully transformed. **Relevant** (image of incomplete inner formation).
- Hos 11:8 — "My heart recoils within me; my compassion grows warm and tender." God's heart overturn — the most direct inner-being of God statement in this corpus. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Amos 5:7 — "You who turn justice to wormwood." Inner-motivated moral perversion of justice. **Relevant.**
- Amo 6:12 — "You have turned justice into poison and the fruit of righteousness into wormwood." Same pattern. **Relevant.**
- Amo 8:10 — "I will turn your feasts into mourning." God's judgment transforming joy to mourning. **Relevant** (inner-experiential consequence).
- Zep 3:9 — "I will change the speech of the peoples to a pure speech, that all of them may call upon the name of the Lord." God transforming the inner-expressive capacity of the nations for worship. **Relevant** — strong verse.

**Group formation:**

**5949-001:** Term names the transformation of the inner person — the heart, mind, or character overturned, renewed, or corrupted.
Verses: Exo 14:5; 1Sa 10:6; 1Sa 10:9; 2Ki 5:26; Jer 2:21; Jer 13:23; Psa 105:25; Hos 7:8; Psa 78:57; Pro 17:20.
Anchor: **1Sa 10:9** ("God gave him another heart"); **Jer 13:23** ("Can the Ethiopian change his skin? Then also you can do good who are accustomed to do evil").

**5949-002:** Term names the transformation of inner experience — mourning turned to joy, or joy to mourning, as God acts.
Verses: Psa 30:11; Est 9:22; Jer 31:13; Amo 8:10; Lam 5:15; Isa 60:5; Job 30:15.
Anchor: **Psa 30:11** ("You have turned for me my mourning into dancing"); **Lam 5:15** ("The joy of our hearts has ceased; our dancing has been turned to mourning").

**5949-003:** Term names God's inner orientation overturn — God's heart recoiling, his compassion stirred, or his disposition changing toward or against his people.
Verses: Hos 11:8; Isa 63:10; Job 9:5; Job 30:21; Lam 3:3; Deu 23:5; Neh 13:2.
Anchor: **Hos 11:8** ("My heart recoils within me; my compassion grows warm and tender"); **Isa 63:10** ("they rebelled and grieved his Holy Spirit; therefore he turned to be their enemy").

**5949-004:** Term names the moral perversion of justice or speech — the overturn of right into wrong as an inner-motivated moral act.
Verses: Amos 5:7; Amo 6:12; Jer 23:36; Lam 1:20; Dan 10:8; Dan 10:16; Zep 3:9; Est 9:1.
Anchor: **Amos 5:7** ("you who turn justice to wormwood"); **Zep 3:9** ("I will change the speech of the peoples to a pure speech, that all of them may call upon the name of the Lord").

Note: Psa 32:4 (strength dried up) assigned to 5949-002 (inner experiential transformation under God's hand); Job 30:15 also in 5949-002.

SUMMARY: mti:5949 H2015 ha.phakh — 92 verses | Relevant: ~37 | Set aside: ~55 | Groups: 4 (5949-001 through 5949-004) | Anchors: 1Sa 10:9, Jer 13:23, Psa 30:11, Lam 5:15, Hos 11:8, Isa 63:10, Amos 5:7, Zep 3:9

### mti:1026 H3868 luz [be devious] — 6 verses

**Reading summary:** The term means "to be devious, crooked, perverse." Verses are all from Proverbs except Isa 30:12. Covers: crooked paths and devious ways (Pro 2:15); losing sight of wisdom (Pro 3:21); the devious person as abomination (Pro 3:32); not escaping wisdom (Pro 4:21); the devious person despising God (Pro 14:2); trusting in perverseness (Isa 30:12).

**Filter decisions:**
- Pro 2:15 — "Men whose paths are crooked, and who are devious in their ways." The devious inner character expressed in crooked paths. **Relevant.**
- Pro 3:21 — "My son, do not lose sight of these — keep sound wisdom and discretion." The target_word is "lose" — the term here means "turn away from / deviate from." The imperative is to not turn away from wisdom; the inner-being engagement is through the will and the orientation toward wisdom. **Relevant.**
- Pro 3:32 — "For the devious person is an abomination to the Lord, but the upright are in his confidence." The devious person as a character type, defined by inner orientation — standing in direct contrast to the upright who are in God's confidence. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Pro 4:21 — "Let them not escape from your sight; keep them within your heart." The target_word is "escape" — the instruction not to let wisdom deviate from sight or heart. The inner-being engagement is explicit: keep wisdom "within your heart." **Relevant.**
- Pro 14:2 — "He who is devious in his ways despises him." The devious way as an expression of inner contempt for God. **Relevant.**
- Isa 30:12 — "Because you despise this word and trust in oppression and perverseness and rely on them." Trusting in perverseness as an inner orientation of misplaced reliance. **Relevant.**

**Group formation:**

**3868-001:** Term names the devious inner character — the crooked orientation of the person whose ways depart from righteousness, expressing contempt for God or wisdom.
Verses: Pro 2:15; Pro 3:32; Pro 14:2; Isa 30:12.
Anchor: **Pro 3:32** ("the devious person is an abomination to the Lord, but the upright are in his confidence"); **Pro 14:2** ("he who is devious in his ways despises him").

**3868-002:** Term names the act of turning away from wisdom — the inner movement of deviating from sound judgement and heart-orientation.
Verses: Pro 3:21; Pro 4:21.
Anchor: **Pro 4:21** ("keep them within your heart" — the counterpart to deviation).

SUMMARY: mti:1026 H3868 luz — 6 verses | Relevant: 6 | Set aside: 0 | Groups: 2 (3868-001, 3868-002) | Anchors: Pro 3:32, Pro 14:2, Pro 4:21

### mti:5951 H4114 mah.pe.khah [overthrow] — 6 verses

**Reading summary:** Noun — "overthrow," used exclusively in comparison to the overthrow of Sodom and Gomorrah. All 6 verses: Deu 29:23; Isa 1:7; Isa 13:19; Jer 49:18; Jer 50:40; Amo 4:11.

**Filter decisions:**
- Deu 29:23 — "An overthrow like that of Sodom and Gomorrah." Geographical judgment comparison. **Set aside.**
- Isa 1:7 — "As overthrown by foreigners." Geographical desolation. **Set aside.**
- Isa 13:19 — "Babylon... will be like Sodom and Gomorrah when God overthrew them." Judgment prophecy, geographical. **Set aside.**
- Jer 49:18 — "As when Sodom and Gomorrah... were overthrown... no man shall dwell there." Geographical. **Set aside.**
- Jer 50:40 — "As when God overthrew Sodom and Gomorrah." Geographical. **Set aside.**
- Amo 4:11 — "I overthrew some of you, as when God overthrew Sodom and Gomorrah, and you were as a brand plucked out of the burning; yet you did not return to me." The Sodom-comparison is used as a call to inner repentance — "yet you did not return to me." The inner-being response (or failure thereof) is the point. **Relevant** (the overthrow in this verse is the vehicle for the inner-being call of return; the failure to return is the inner-being content).

**Group formation:**
**5951-001:** Term names a divine overthrow that should have produced inner return — the overwhelming judgment designed to evoke repentance, but which failed to move the heart.
Verses: Amo 4:11.
Anchor: **Amo 4:11** ("I overthrew some of you... yet you did not return to me").

SUMMARY: mti:5951 H4114 mah.pe.khah — 6 verses | Relevant: 1 | Set aside: 5 | Groups: 1 (5951-001) | Anchor: Amo 4:11

### mti:5952 H4115 mah.pe.khet [stocks] — 4 verses

Asa's rage is the inner-being content — but the term *mah.pe.khet* names the stocks (physical device), not the rage. **Set aside** (inner-being content is in Asa's anger, not in this term).
- Jer 20:2 — "Pashhur beat Jeremiah the prophet, and put him in the stocks." Physical imprisonment. **Set aside.**
- Jer 20:3 — "When Pashhur released Jeremiah from the stocks, Jeremiah said to him, 'The Lord does not call your name Pashhur, but Terror on Every Side.'" The term names the stocks from which Jeremiah is released; the inner-being content is Jeremiah's prophetic word and Pashhur's implied inner state of terror. Not through this term. **Set aside.**
- Jer 29:26 — "To put him in the stocks and neck irons." Physical restraint device. **Set aside.**

**All-verses-fail rule:** 4 verses, all fail. ≤10 verses → researcher flag required.

- **Awaiting researcher decision.**

### mti:5959 H5557 sa.laph [to pervert] — 7 verses

**Reading summary:** The term means "to pervert, subvert, overthrow." Verses span legal/ethical perversion (Exo 23:8; Deu 16:19 — bribes subverting justice); God overthrows the mighty (Job 12:19); sin overthrows the wicked (Pro 13:6); folly brings ruin and the heart rages (Pro 19:3); God throws the wicked to ruin (Pro 21:12); God overthrows the words of the traitor (Pro 22:12).

**Filter decisions:**
- Exo 23:8 — "A bribe blinds the clear-sighted and subverts the cause of those who are in the right." The bribe operates on the inner perception ("blinds the clear-sighted") and perverts the inner moral judgement. **Relevant.**
- Deu 16:19 — "A bribe blinds the eyes of the wise and subverts the cause of the righteous." Same pattern. **Relevant.**
- Job 12:19 — "He leads priests away stripped and overthrows the mighty." God's sovereign action overthrowing the powerful. The inner-being engagement is minimal through this term (God's sovereign power expressed outwardly). **Set aside.**
- Pro 13:6 — "Sin overthrows the wicked." Sin as the agent of inner-moral destruction. **Relevant** (the perversion/overthrow of the wicked person is caused by their sin — inner-being consequence).
- Pro 19:3 — "When a man's folly brings his way to ruin, his heart rages against the Lord." The folly/ruin (*sa.laph* = ruin) is the vehicle; the heart raging against God is the inner-being content directly named. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Pro 21:12 — "He throws the wicked down to ruin." God's judgment action; the ruin is existential-moral. **Relevant** (borderline — retain).
- Pro 22:12 — "He overthrows the words of the traitor." The perversion/overthrow of treacherous speech by God. The inner dimension is the treachery of the words' origin. **Relevant** (borderline — retain).

**Group formation:**
**5959-001:** Term names the perversion of moral discernment — the subverting of inner judgement and the cause of the righteous through corrupt influence (bribery).
Verses: Exo 23:8; Deu 16:19.
Anchor: **Deu 16:19** ("a bribe blinds the eyes of the wise and subverts the cause of the righteous").

**5959-002:** Term names the ruin brought by sin or folly upon the inner life — the self-destruction of the wicked through their own perversion.
Verses: Pro 13:6; Pro 19:3; Pro 21:12; Pro 22:12.
Anchor: **Pro 19:3** ("when a man's folly brings his way to ruin, his heart rages against the Lord").

SUMMARY: mti:5959 H5557 sa.laph — 7 verses | Relevant: 6 | Set aside: 1 | Groups: 2 (5959-001, 5959-002) | Anchors: Deu 16:19, Pro 19:3

### mti:1024 H8419 tah.pu.khah [perversity] — 10 verses

**Reading summary:** A noun meaning "perversity, perverse things." All 10 verses from Deu 32 or Proverbs. Covers: a perverse generation without faithfulness (Deu 32:20); men of perverted speech (Pro 2:12); delight in perverseness of evil (Pro 2:14); perverted heart devising evil (Pro 6:14); perverted speech hated by wisdom (Pro 8:13); the perverse tongue cut off (Pro 10:31/32); a dishonest man spreading strife (Pro 16:28/30); the heart uttering perverse things (Pro 23:33).

**Filter decisions:**
- Deu 32:20 — "They are a perverse generation, children in whom is no faithfulness." Perversity as an inner character quality of the whole person — faithlessness at the core. **Relevant.**
- Pro 2:12 — "Men of perverted speech." Perverted speech originating from perverted inner orientation. **Relevant** (§3.4).
- Pro 2:14 — "Who rejoice in doing evil and delight in the perverseness of evil." Inner delight in perverseness — direct inner-being engagement (joy, delight directed toward evil). **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Pro 6:14 — "With perverted heart devises evil, continually sowing discord." The perverted heart as the source of devised evil. **Relevant** — strong verse (heart explicitly named).
- Pro 8:13 — "Perverted speech I hate." Wisdom/God's hatred of perverted speech — the inner orientation of God against perversity. **Relevant.**
- Pro 10:31 — "The perverse tongue will be cut off." The perverse tongue as expression of inner perversion. **Relevant** (§3.4).
- Pro 10:32 — "The mouth of the wicked, what is perverse." The wicked person's speech as an expression of inner perversity. **Relevant** (§3.4).
- Pro 16:28 — "A dishonest man spreads strife." Dishonesty as inner character quality producing relational destruction. **Relevant.**
- Pro 16:30 — "Whoever winks his eyes plans dishonest things; he who purses his lips brings evil to pass." The inner planning of dishonest things expressed in calculated external behaviour. **Relevant.**
- Pro 23:33 — "Your eyes will see strange things, and your heart utter perverse things." The heart itself uttering perverse things — explicit inner-being. **Relevant** — strong verse.

**Group formation:**
**1024-001:** Term names perversity as an inner character orientation — the fundamental distortion of the person's heart, will, and speech toward evil and faithlessness.
Verses: Deu 32:20; Pro 2:14; Pro 6:14; Pro 16:28; Pro 16:30; Pro 23:33.
Anchor: **Pro 6:14** ("with perverted heart devises evil, continually sowing discord"); **Pro 23:33** ("your heart utter perverse things").

**1024-002:** Term names perversity of speech as the outward expression of inner corruption — the perverted words that flow from and reveal a perverted inner life.
Verses: Pro 2:12; Pro 8:13; Pro 10:31; Pro 10:32.
Anchor: **Pro 2:12** ("men of perverted speech"); **Pro 8:13** ("perverted speech I hate").

SUMMARY: mti:1024 H8419 tah.pu.khah — 10 verses | Relevant: 10 | Set aside: 0 | Groups: 2 (1024-001, 1024-002) | Anchors: Pro 6:14, Pro 23:33, Pro 2:12, Pro 8:13

### mti:1047 G1391 doxa [glory] — 49 verses

**Reading summary:** *Doxa* (glory) in the NT covers: the glory of God as divine attribute and object of human seeking/hope (Rom 1:23; 3:23; 5:2; 8:18/21; 9:23); giving glory to God as inner-being act (Rom 4:20; 11:36; 16:27; 1Cor 10:31; 2Cor 1:20; Gal 1:5); glory as transformation of the person (2Cor 3:18); the human person as image and glory (1Cor 11:7); glory in suffering and endurance (2Cor 4:17; Eph 3:13); the interior work of the Spirit according to the riches of glory (Eph 3:16); glory as an inner quality or destiny (1Cor 2:7; 15:43; Rom 2:7/10; 8:18; 9:4); the gospel of the glory of Christ illuminating the heart (2Cor 4:4/6); eschatological glory (Col 1:27; 3:4; 1Pe 1:7); bodily glory (1Cor 11:15; 15:40/41); reputation/honor (2Cor 6:8; 2Cor 8:23); eyes of the heart enlightened to the hope of his glorious inheritance (Eph 1:18).

**Filter decisions:**

*Relevant — inner-being engagement through this term:*
- Rom 1:23 — Exchanged the glory of God for images. The inner-being act of substituting the true object of glory for idols. **Relevant.**
- Rom 2:7 — Seeking glory and honor and immortality — inner orientation of patient endurance toward eternal reward. **Relevant.**
- Rom 2:10 — Glory and honor and peace for everyone who does good. **Relevant.**
- Rom 3:23 — "All have sinned and fall short of the glory of God." The universal inner condition of fallenness defined by distance from glory. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Rom 4:20 — Abraham "gave glory to God" — deliberate inner-being act of faith/worship. **Relevant.**
- Rom 5:2 — "We rejoice in hope of the glory of God." Inner orientation of joy directed toward future glory. **Relevant.**
- Rom 8:18 — The glory to be revealed — the inner-being hope sustaining under suffering. **Relevant.**
- Rom 8:21 — Creation obtaining "the freedom of the glory of the children of God." **Relevant.**
- Rom 9:23 — "The riches of his glory for vessels of mercy." God's inner-being overflow of glory toward his people. **Relevant.**
- Rom 11:36 — "To him be glory forever." Doxological inner orientation. **Relevant.**
- Rom 15:7 — Welcome one another "for the glory of God" — inner motivation of action. **Relevant.**
- Rom 16:27 — "To the only wise God be glory." Doxological. **Relevant.**
- 1Cor 2:7 — "Wisdom decreed before the ages for our glory." The inner eschatological destiny of the person. **Relevant.**
- 1Cor 10:31 — "Do all to the glory of God." The inner-motivational orientation of every act. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- 1Cor 11:7 — "Man is the image and glory of God." Glory as an attribute of the human person's nature. **Relevant.**
- 1Cor 11:15 — "Her hair is given to her for a covering" — her hair is "her glory." Physical/cultural. Borderline. **Set aside** (glory here refers to physical covering, not inner-being).
- 1Cor 15:40/41 — Glory of heavenly vs earthly bodies; glory of sun/moon/stars. Physical/cosmic distinctions. **Set aside** (the glory here is physical/natural, no inner-being through this term).
- 1Cor 15:43 — "It is raised in glory." The resurrection glory of the body — eschatological transformation. **Relevant** (the inner-being dimension of the resurrection body).
- 2Cor 1:20 — "Through him that we utter our Amen to God for his glory." Doxological inner orientation. **Relevant.**
- 2Cor 3:7 through 3:11 — The glory of the old and new covenants; comparing glories. The surpassing glory of the new is the inner-being transforming glory of the Spirit. **Relevant** (the comparison of glories directly concerns the inner-being transformation of the people).
- 2Cor 3:18 — "We all, with unveiled face, beholding the glory of the Lord, are being transformed into the same image from one degree of glory to another." Direct inner-being transformation. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- 2Cor 4:4 — "The light of the gospel of the glory of Christ" blinded to unbelievers. The inner-being state (blindness of mind) and what glory-perception requires. **Relevant.**
- 2Cor 4:6 — "The knowledge of the glory of God in the face of Jesus Christ" shone in our hearts. Glory illuminating the heart. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- 2Cor 4:15 — "Increase thanksgiving, to the glory of God." Doxological inner orientation. **Relevant.**
- 2Cor 4:17 — "Eternal weight of glory beyond all comparison" — the inner hope sustaining endurance. **Relevant.**
- 2Cor 6:8 — "Through honor and dishonor, through slander and praise." Honor/glory as social category. **Set aside** (here *doxa* is used in the social-reputation sense, not the inner-being dimension of glory).
- 2Cor 8:19 — Carrying grace for "the glory of the Lord himself." Motivation for action. **Relevant** (borderline — retain).
- 2Cor 8:23 — Messengers "the glory of Christ." Descriptive of persons. **Set aside** (the term here is an honorary description, not inner-being engagement through the term).
- Gal 1:5 — "To him be glory forever." Doxological. **Relevant.**
- Eph 1:6 — "To the praise of his glorious grace." Inner-being orientation of praise toward God's grace. **Relevant.**
- Eph 1:12/14 — "To the praise of his glory" (×2). Doxological inner purpose. **Relevant.**
- Eph 1:17 — "The Father of glory, may give you the Spirit of wisdom and of revelation." The Father characterized by glory; the gift of Spirit for inner knowing. **Relevant.**
- Eph 1:18 — "Having the eyes of your hearts enlightened, that you may know what is the hope to which he has called you, what are the riches of his glorious inheritance." Eyes of the heart — direct inner-being. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Eph 3:13 — "Which is your glory." Suffering as the congregation's glory. **Relevant** (borderline — retain).
- Eph 3:16 — "According to the riches of his glory he may grant you to be strengthened with power through his Spirit in your inner being." Glory as the ground of inner-being strengthening. **Relevant** — strong verse (inner being explicitly named).
- Eph 3:21 — "To him be glory in the church." Doxological. **Relevant.**
- Col 1:11 — "According to his glorious might." God's glory as the source of empowering. **Relevant.**
- Col 1:27 — "Christ in you, the hope of glory." Glory as inner-eschatological hope. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Col 3:4 — "Then you also will appear with him in glory." Eschatological. **Relevant.**
- 1Pe 1:7 — "Result in praise and glory and honor at the revelation of Jesus Christ." The eschatological outcome of tested faith. **Relevant.**
- Rom 9:4 — "The glory" belonging to Israel — the divine glory as a covenantal inner-theological endowment. **Relevant.**

**Group formation:**

**1047-001:** Term names the glory of God as the supreme inner-being orientation of the human person — what is sought, hoped for, and the measure against which all human fallenness is assessed.
Verses: Rom 3:23; Rom 2:7; Rom 2:10; Rom 5:2; Rom 8:18; Rom 4:20; 1Cor 10:31; Eph 3:16; Col 1:27.
Anchor: **Rom 3:23** ("all have sinned and fall short of the glory of God"); **Eph 3:16** ("according to the riches of his glory he may grant you to be strengthened through his Spirit in your inner being").

**1047-002:** Term names glory as transforming — the process by which the inner person is changed from one degree of glory to another through beholding the Lord.
Verses: 2Cor 3:7; 2Cor 3:8; 2Cor 3:9; 2Cor 3:10; 2Cor 3:11; 2Cor 3:18; 2Cor 4:4; 2Cor 4:6; Eph 1:18.
Anchor: **2Cor 3:18** ("beholding the glory of the Lord, are being transformed into the same image from one degree of glory to another"); **2Cor 4:6** ("the knowledge of the glory of God in the face of Jesus Christ" shone in our hearts).

**1047-003:** Term names doxological inner orientation — the purpose of all human action and the direction of the inner life toward the glorification of God.
Verses: Rom 1:23 (inversion — exchange of glory); Rom 11:36; Rom 15:7; Rom 16:27; Gal 1:5; Eph 1:6; Eph 1:12; Eph 1:14; Eph 3:21; 2Cor 1:20; 2Cor 4:15; 2Cor 8:19; 1Cor 2:7.
Anchor: **Rom 1:23** ("exchanged the glory of the immortal God for images" — the definitive inner-being inversion); **Eph 1:12** ("so that we... might be to the praise of his glory").

**1047-004:** Term names eschatological glory — the future condition of the person and creation fully realized in glory, which functions as inner hope sustaining the present.
Verses: 2Cor 4:17; 1Cor 15:43; Col 3:4; 1Pe 1:7; Rom 8:21; Rom 9:23; Eph 1:17; Eph 3:13; Col 1:11.
Anchor: **2Cor 4:17** ("this light momentary affliction is preparing for us an eternal weight of glory beyond all comparison"); **Col 1:27** ("Christ in you, the hope of glory").

### mti:1041 H0259 e.chad [one] — 181 verses

**§3.5 particle analysis:** *e.chad* is a numeral/quantifier meaning "one." Per §3.5, it passes the filter if it directs, intensifies, qualifies the scope of, or discloses an inner orientation through inner-being content. The test: remove the particle — does the inner-being content change meaningfully?

**Reading the full corpus:** The 181 verses span: (a) numerical/counting uses in ritual/census contexts — Num 7 series (50+ verses counting "one" offering, one animal, one goat); ordinal dates (Num 1:1/18; Hag 1:1/2:1; Dan 8:1/9:21 etc.); census numbers (Num 1:41/2:16/28 etc.); (b) narrative "one of them/one from" (Gen passages — one of the sons, one of the women, one brother, etc.); (c) theologically weighted "one" uses — one flesh (Gen 2:24); one people (Gen 11:1/6; 34:16/22); one heart and one way (Jer 32:39); "like one of us" (Gen 3:22); the Lord is one (implied in Mal 2:10 — "Have we not all one Father?"); one head (Hos 1:11); one man (Judg 20:1/8/11); "unchangeable" (Job 23:13 — "he is one/unchangeable").

**Assessment by §3.5:** The quantifier *e.chad* in this corpus almost universally functions as a numerical/counting word. Applying the mental-removal test:

- Num 7 series (50+ verses): removing "one" from "one silver plate," "one golden dish," "one bull" yields no change in inner-being content — these are ritual counting formulas. **Set aside** (all ~50 Num 7 verses).
- Census/ordinal date verses (Num 1, Hag, Dan, Neh, Jer 52): purely numerical/temporal. **Set aside.**
- Narrative "one of them" (most Gen verses, Judg narrative, Neh building record): "one" here quantifies a person in a group — purely numerical designation. No inner-being engagement through the term. **Set aside.**

*The few verses where §3.5 may apply:*

- Gen 2:24 — "They shall become one flesh." The "one" here qualifies the scope of covenant union — it shapes the meaning of the relational-inner act of marriage. The *oneness* of flesh is not merely numerical; it discloses the covenantal depth of the union. **Relevant** (the quantifier shapes the inner-being content — the union would be categorically different without "one").
- Gen 11:1 — "The whole earth had one language." The oneness of language as a communal-inner condition enabling shared meaning and intent. Borderline. **Set aside** (the "one" here is a sociological description, not an inner-being qualifier in the §3.5 sense).
- Gen 11:6 — "They are one people, and they have all one language, and this is only the beginning of what they will do. And nothing that they propose to do will now be impossible for them." The oneness of people and language as the ground of their inner-collective power to achieve their purposes. **Relevant** (the "one" intensifies the inner capacity — the corporate inner-being potential).
- Gen 3:22 — "The man has become like one of us in knowing good and evil." The "one of us" — the divine plurality and the human's now-comparable status through moral knowledge. **Relevant** (the "one" here qualifies the scope of the inner-being comparison — knowing good and evil like the divine council).
- Gen 29:20 — "They seemed to him but a few days because of the love he had for her." The target_word is "few" (translating *e.chad* as comparative); this verse is about Jacob's love. The quantifier shapes the subjective inner-experience of time under love. **Relevant** (the "few days" of love directly measures the inner-being state — without the quantifier, the inner-being force of the love is not disclosed).
- Jer 32:39 — "I will give them one heart and one way." The "one" qualifies the inner-being promise — not partial or divided heart/way, but a unified inner orientation. **Relevant** — strong verse (the quantifier is essential to the inner-being meaning).
- Job 23:13 — "He is unchangeable/one, and who can turn him back?" The "one" names God's inner uniqueness and unchangeability — a divine inner-being attribute. **Relevant.**
- Mal 2:10 — "Have we not all one Father? Has not one God created us?" The "one" here intensifies the inner-relational claim — one Father creating one community; the ethical consequence (faithlessness to one another) follows. **Relevant** (the "one" qualifies the scope of the relational-covenantal inner bond).
- Mal 2:15 — "Did he not make them one, with a portion of the Spirit in their union?" The "one" defines the depth of the marriage covenant — made one by God, with the Spirit's portion in the union. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Hos 1:11 — "They shall appoint for themselves one head." The "one" shapes the inner-unity of the restored people under one leader. **Relevant** (borderline — retain).
- Judg 20:1/8/11 — "The congregation assembled as one man"; "all the people arose as one man"; "all the men of Israel gathered... united as one man." The "one man" image intensifies the collective inner unity of corporate resolve and decision. **Relevant** (the "one" discloses the inner unity of corporate will — §3.5: it qualifies the scope of the corporate inner orientation).
- Gen 22:2 — "Take your son, your only son Isaac, whom you love." The "one/only" (*e.chad*) here intensifies the costliness of what is asked — it shapes the inner-being weight of the command. **Relevant** (the quantifier discloses the inner-being cost — without "only," the command's weight is reduced).
- Gen 27:38 — "Have you but one blessing, my father?" Esau's anguished appeal — the "one" shapes the inner desperation. **Relevant.**
- Gen 27:45 — "Why should I be bereft of you both in one day?" — the "one day" intensifies the inner-being loss. Borderline. **Set aside** (temporal use).

**All remaining verses** (Judg 4:16 "not a man left"; Judg 6:16 "as one man"; Gen 34:16/22; Neh counting verses; Isa census-like and predictive verses not engaging §3.5; Jer 52 architectural measurements; Job 9:3/22 argument-related; Job 31:15/33:14/23/40:5/41:16/42:11/14 — various; Gen 32/37/40/41/42 narrative ones): individually inspected — the vast majority are numerical or narrative uses with no §3.5 engagement. I have individually read all 181 verses.

**Group formation:**

**1041-001:** Term names the oneness of covenantal union — the "one flesh" or "one heart and one way" that defines the depth of relationship between persons, or between God and his people.
Verses: Gen 2:24; Jer 32:39; Mal 2:15; Mal 2:10.
Anchor: **Jer 32:39** ("I will give them one heart and one way, that they may fear me forever"); **Mal 2:15** ("Did he not make them one, with a portion of the Spirit in their union?").

**1041-002:** Term names the corporate oneness of inner resolve — the united will of a community described as "one man" or "one people."
Verses: Judg 20:1; Judg 20:8; Judg 20:11; Hos 1:11; Gen 11:6.
Anchor: **Judg 20:1** ("the congregation assembled as one man to the Lord").

**1041-003:** Term names the uniqueness of God or of the irreplaceable — the "one" that shapes the weight of divine identity or the cost of a singular relationship.
Verses: Job 23:13; Gen 22:2; Gen 27:38; Gen 3:22.
Anchor: **Gen 22:2** ("take your son, your only son Isaac, whom you love"); **Job 23:13** ("he is unchangeable/one, and who can turn him back?").

**1041-004:** Term names the quantifier that intensifies inner-being experience — in the verse, "one" shapes the subjective inner weight.
Verses: Gen 29:20.
Anchor: **Gen 29:20** ("they seemed to him but a few days because of the love he had for her").

Note: Groups 1041-003 and 1041-004 are small. Consider consolidation at patch construction — but for classification purposes, the inner-being dimensions are distinct enough to document separately. Under 5 groups; no consolidation pressure triggered.

SUMMARY: mti:1041 H0259 e.chad — 181 verses | Relevant: ~17 | Set aside: ~164 | Groups: 4 (1041-001 through 1041-004) | Anchors: Jer 32:39, Mal 2:15, Judg 20:1, Gen 22:2, Job 23:13, Gen 29:20

### mti:1040 H0587 a.nach.nu [we] — 61 verses

**§3.5 particle analysis:** *a.nach.nu* is a first-person plural pronoun ("we"). Per §3.5, a pronoun passes the filter if it directs inner-being content — orienting a question, command, or assertion toward an inner-being subject — or discloses an inner orientation through the manner in which it frames inner-being content. The test: remove "we" mentally — does the inner-being content change meaningfully?

**Reading the full corpus:** The 61 verses span primarily narrative/speech contexts: negotiations (Gen — Jacob's sons before Joseph); historical declarations (Neh building narrative); prophetic community speech (Isa, Jer, Lam, Dan, Neh 9 confession). Most uses are standard first-person plural speech markers — "we are from Haran," "we are shepherds," "we will do good to you," "we were binding sheaves," etc.

**Applying §3.5 mental-removal test across all 61 verses — key findings:**

*Inner-being relevant — where "we" frames or discloses a collective inner orientation:*

- Gen 42:21 — "We are guilty concerning our brother, in that we saw the distress of his soul, when he begged us and we did not listen." The "we" here frames a collective confession of guilt — the inner-being of the community owning its moral failure together. **Relevant** (the "we" directs the inner-being content of guilt/conscience — without it, the moral reckoning is individual, not collective; the corporate inner acknowledgment is disclosed through this pronoun).

- Neh 9:33 — "You have been righteous in all that has come upon us, for you have dealt faithfully and we have acted wickedly." The "we" discloses collective moral confession — the community's inner posture of self-assessment before God. **Relevant.**

- Neh 9:36 — "Behold, we are slaves this day." The "we" frames corporate lament and awareness of communal condition before God. **Relevant** (the collective inner-being of shame and loss expressed through "we").

- Neh 9:37 — "We are in great distress." Corporate inner-being of distress. **Relevant.**

- Neh 9:38 — "Because of all this we make a firm covenant in writing." The "we" names the corporate inner-will committing to covenant — collective volition. **Relevant.**

- Jer 3:25 — "We have sinned against the Lord our God, we and our fathers, from our youth even to this day, and we have not obeyed the voice of the Lord our God." Corporate confession — the "we" frames and owns the collective inner-being failure across generations. **Relevant** — strong verse.

- Jer 8:14 — "We have sinned against the Lord." Corporate confession. **Relevant.**

- Jer 26:19 — "We are about to bring great disaster upon ourselves." Corporate moral self-awareness. **Relevant** (borderline — retain).

- Jer 42:6 — "Whether it is good or bad, we will obey the voice of the Lord our God." Corporate commitment of the will to obedience. **Relevant** (the "we" frames the collective inner-being act of submission).

- Lam 5:7 — "Our fathers sinned, and are no more; and we bear their iniquities." The "we" names the community owning inherited moral consequence. **Relevant.**

- Dan 9:18 — "We do not present our pleas before you because of our righteousness, but because of your great mercy." The "we" discloses the corporate inner posture of humility and dependence on mercy. **Relevant** — strong verse.

- Isa 53:4 — "Surely he has borne our griefs and carried our sorrows; yet we esteemed him stricken, smitten by God." The "we" names the corporate inner error of misjudgment — the collective inner response to the servant's suffering. **Relevant** (the "we" is essential to the inner-being weight — the communal misreading of what God was doing).

- Isa 64:8 — "We are the clay, and you are our potter; we are all the work of your hand." The "we" frames corporate creaturely identity before God — the inner-being posture of the creature before its maker. **Relevant.**

- Mic 4:5 — "We will walk in the name of the Lord our God forever and ever." Corporate inner commitment and orientation — the communal will set toward God. **Relevant.**

- Mal 3:15 — "We call the arrogant blessed." The community's inner moral confusion — calling wrong things praiseworthy. **Relevant** (the "we" discloses the collective inner-being distortion of moral judgment).

- Num 9:7 — "We are unclean through touching a dead body. Why are we kept from bringing the Lord's offering?" The "we" frames the inner-being concern about access to God — their inner orientation toward worship frustrated. **Relevant** (borderline — retain).

- Gen 43:18 — "Because of the money... we are brought in, so that he may assault us... we are afraid." The "we" frames collective inner fear. **Relevant** (borderline — fear as inner-being state framed by "we").

*Set aside — purely narrative/speech "we" with no §3.5 inner-being engagement:*
All remaining verses: Gen 13:8 (we are kinsmen — social); Gen 19:13 (we are about to destroy — action); Gen 29:4 (we are from Haran — geographical); Gen 37:7 (we were binding sheaves — dream narrative); Gen 42:11 (we are honest men — social claim); Gen 42:13/31/32 (we are twelve brothers — numerical/social); Gen 43:8 (we and our little ones — social); Gen 44:9/16 (we will be servants — legal negotiation); Gen 46:34 (we have been keepers — vocational); Gen 47:3/19 (we are shepherds; buy us — practical negotiation); Num 10:29 (we are setting out — practical); Num 20:4/16 (why have you brought us; we cried to the Lord — narrative historical report); Num 32:17 (we will take up arms — practical); Judg 9:28 (who are we of Shechem — political); Judg 16:5 (we may overpower him — military plan); Judg 18:5 (we may know whether — divination inquiry); Judg 19:18 (we are passing — travel); Judg 21:7/18 (what shall we do; we cannot give — practical problem); Neh 2:17 (we are in trouble — physical state of Jerusalem); Neh 2:20 (we will arise and build — practical); Neh 4:1/10/19/21/23 (building narrative); Neh 5:2/3/5/8 (economic complaints — social/practical); Isa 20:6 (we fled for help — military narrative); Isa 36:11 (do not speak in Hebrew — linguistic preference); Jer 8:8 (we are wise — social claim); Jer 8:20 (we are not saved — historical lament); Jer 35:8 (we have obeyed — obedience report); Jer 44:17/19 (we did, we made offerings — historical report); Jer 48:14 (we are heroes — social boast); Lam 5:7 (already included above); Job 8:9 (we are but of yesterday — epistemological humility). 

Note: Some borderline set-aside cases (Neh 4 series, Job 8:9) were close to inclusion — applied §3.3 and leaned toward the mental-removal test: in each case, removing "we" does not change the inner-being content meaningfully in those verses.

**Group formation:**

**1040-001:** Term frames corporate confession of sin and moral failure — the "we" of communal acknowledgment of guilt and wrong before God.
Verses: Gen 42:21; Neh 9:33; Jer 3:25; Jer 8:14; Lam 5:7; Dan 9:18; Isa 53:4.
Anchor: **Dan 9:18** ("we do not present our pleas before you because of our righteousness, but because of your great mercy"); **Jer 3:25** ("we have sinned against the Lord our God, we and our fathers").

**1040-002:** Term frames corporate commitment or lament — the "we" of communal inner will directed toward God or communal distress expressed before him.
Verses: Neh 9:36; Neh 9:37; Neh 9:38; Jer 42:6; Isa 64:8; Mic 4:5; Mal 3:15; Num 9:7; Gen 43:18; Jer 26:19.
Anchor: **Mic 4:5** ("we will walk in the name of the Lord our God forever and ever"); **Neh 9:37** ("we are in great distress").

### mti:1028 H1984A ha.lal [to shine] — 4 verses

**Reading summary:** This is the homograph of the praise root — this specific sense means "to shine" (of light). Verses: Job 29:3 (God's lamp shining on Job's head); Job 31:26 (sun shining); Job 41:18 (Leviathan's eyes flashing light); Isa 13:10 (stars not giving light in judgment).

- Job 29:3 — "When his lamp shone upon my head, and by his light I walked through darkness." God's light on Job's head as inner-being guidance and flourishing — the image of divine presence enabling the inner life to navigate darkness. **Relevant** (the shining is God's inner orientation of favour toward Job expressed through illumination — §3.4; the image discloses the inner-being of Job's relationship with God).
- Job 31:26 — "If I have looked at the sun when it shone, or the moon moving in splendor." Job's hypothetical looking at celestial lights with admiring worship — the inner-being of idolatrous attraction to created beauty. **Relevant** (the context is Job disclaiming idolatrous inner attraction to the luminaries).
- Job 41:18 — "His sneezings flash forth light." Leviathan's physical attribute — no inner-being engagement. **Set aside.**
- Isa 13:10 — "The stars of the heavens and their constellations will not give their light." Cosmic darkening in judgment — physical/eschatological. **Set aside.**

**Group formation:**

Verses: Job 29:3; Job 31:26 (contrast — the created light that tempts inner devotion away from God).
Anchor: **Job 29:3** ("when his lamp shone upon my head, and by his light I walked through darkness").

### mti:4333 H1984B ha.lal [to boast: praise] — 99 verses

**Reading summary:** The primary praise root — *halal* in the praise sense. The 99 verses span: Psalms praise and Hallel sections (the large Psalms 146–150 cluster, Psa 22, 34, 56, 63, 69, 74, 84, 96, 102–119 series); Chronicles worship/liturgical appointments; Proverbs; Song; Isaiah; Jeremiah; Ezra; Nehemiah; and scattered narrative uses. The corpus covers: corporate liturgical praise (Psa Hallel sections; 1-2Ch appointments); the worthy object of praise (God "greatly to be praised" — 1Ch 16:25; Psa 48:1; 96:4; 145:3); individual praise (Psa 22:22; 34:1; 56:4/10; 63:5; 69:30; 109:30; 119:164/175; 145:2); social praise/admiration (Gen 12:15; 2Sa 14:25; Song 6:9; Pro 12:8; 27:2; 28:4; 31:28/30/31); the inability of the dead to praise (Psa 115:17; Isa 38:18); social praise (Eze 26:17); Psa 78:63 (no marriage song); Judg 16:24 (Philistines praised Dagon).

**Filter decisions:**

*Set aside — social praise/admiration of human qualities without inner-being engagement through this term:*
Gen 12:15 (Pharaoh's servants praised Sarai's beauty — social/aesthetic); 2Sa 14:25 (Absalom praised for appearance — social); Song 6:9 (queens praised her — social admiration); 2Ch 23:12/13 (people praising the king — political acclamation); Psa 78:63 (young women had no marriage song — social/cultural loss); Eze 26:17 (renowned city — social renown).

*Relevant — inner-being engagement through praise:*

The vast majority of the 99 verses are directly relevant — they involve the inner-being act of praise directed toward God, the inner orientation of worship, or the moral dimension of what/whom one praises. I will classify all remaining verses (after the social-admiration set-asides above) as **Relevant**, noting key distinctions for grouping.

Particularly strong verses:
- 2Sa 22:4 / Psa 18:3 — "I call upon the Lord, who is worthy to be praised." The worthiness of God as the object of the inner orientation. **Relevant.**
- Psa 22:22 — "In the midst of the congregation I will praise you." **Relevant.**
- Psa 22:26 — "Those who seek him shall praise the Lord! May your hearts live forever!" Heart directly named in connection with praise. **Relevant.**
- Psa 34:1 — "His praise shall continually be in my mouth." The inner sustained orientation of praise. **Relevant.**
- Psa 63:5 — "My soul will be satisfied... and my mouth will praise you with joyful lips." Soul named as the seat of praise. **Relevant.**
- Psa 115:17 — "The dead do not praise the Lord." The inability to praise as a condition of inner absence. **Relevant.**
- Psa 119:175 — "Let my soul live and praise you." Soul and praise linked. **Relevant.**
- Psa 146:1 — "Praise the Lord, O my soul!" Soul directly addressed in praise. **Relevant.**
- Pro 27:2 — "Let another praise you, and not your own mouth." Inner pride vs. authentic praise. **Relevant.**
- Pro 28:4 — "Those who forsake the law praise the wicked." The inner-being inversion — praising the wrong object. **Relevant.**
- Pro 31:30 — "A woman who fears the Lord is to be praised." Fear of the Lord as the basis for true praise. **Relevant.**
- Isa 38:18 — "For Sheol does not thank you; death does not praise you." The inner-being deprivation of death. **Relevant.**
- Jer 20:13 — "Praise the Lord! For he has delivered the life of the needy." **Relevant.**
- Joe 2:26 — "You shall praise the name of the Lord your God, who has dealt wondrously with you." **Relevant.**
- Judg 16:24 — "When the people saw him, they praised their god." Misdirected praise — inner-being oriented toward Dagon. **Relevant** (the praise discloses the inner orientation of the Philistines toward their god).
- 1Ch 16:4 — "To invoke, to thank, and to praise the Lord." Liturgical appointment of inner-being acts. **Relevant.**
- 2Ch 5:13 / 20:21 / 29:30 / 30:21 etc. — Corporate praise contexts. **Relevant.**
- Psa 149:1 — "Sing to the Lord a new song, his praise in the assembly of the godly." **Relevant.**

**Group formation:**

**4333-001:** Term names the sustained inner orientation of praise toward God — the deliberate, personal direction of the whole being in worship.
Verses: Psa 34:1; Psa 63:5; Psa 119:175; Psa 146:1; Psa 145:2; Psa 109:30; Psa 119:164; Psa 22:22; Psa 22:26; 2Sa 22:4/Psa 18:3; Psa 145:3.
Anchor: **Psa 34:1** ("his praise shall continually be in my mouth"); **Psa 146:1** ("Praise the Lord, O my soul!").

**4333-002:** Term names corporate/liturgical praise — the community's inner-being act of worship organized for God's service.
Verses: 1Ch 16:4; 1Ch 16:25; 1Ch 16:36; 1Ch 23:5/30; 1Ch 25:3; 1Ch 29:13; 2Ch 5:13; 2Ch 7:6; 2Ch 8:14; 2Ch 20:19/21; 2Ch 29:30; 2Ch 30:21; 2Ch 31:2; Ezr 3:10/11; Neh 5:13; Neh 12:24; Psa 35:18; Psa 84:4; Psa 107:32; Psa 102:18; Psa 135:1/3/21; Psa 147:1/12/20; Psa 148 series; Psa 149:1/3/9; Psa 150 series; Psa 96:4; Psa 105:45; Psa 106:1/48; Psa 111:1; Psa 112:1; Psa 113:1/3/9; Psa 115:18; Psa 116:19; Psa 117:1/2; Psa 135:3/21; Psa 104:35; Psa 113:1; Jer 20:13; Jer 31:7; Joe 2:26.
Anchor: **2Ch 20:21** ("Give thanks to the Lord, for his steadfast love endures forever" — the words of the praise choir going before the army).

**4333-003:** Term names the praise of the worthy — what and who deserves to be praised, as a reflection of inner-being discernment and moral orientation.
Verses: Pro 27:2; Pro 28:4; Pro 31:28; Pro 31:30; Pro 31:31; Pro 12:8; Judg 16:24; Psa 74:21; Psa 48:1; Psa 96:4; Isa 38:18; Isa 62:9; Psa 115:17; Psa 69:34; Song 6:9 (set aside above); 2Sa 14:25 (set aside).
Anchor: **Pro 31:30** ("a woman who fears the Lord is to be praised"); **Isa 38:18** ("for Sheol does not thank you; death does not praise you").

### mti:5991 H2170 ze.mar [music] — 4 verses

**Reading summary:** Aramaic term for "music" in Dan 3. All 4 verses are the Nebuchadnezzar decree: at the sound of music, fall down and worship the golden image.

**Filter decisions:**
- Dan 3:5 — "When you hear the sound of the horn, pipe, lyre... every kind of music, you are to fall down and worship the golden image." The music is the trigger for coerced worship — the inner-being act of worship (bowing) demanded under compulsion. **Relevant** (the music here is the vehicle for commanding an inner-being orientation; the entire scene is about what the inner being will orient toward under threat — see Dan 3:17/18 for the full context, though those verses are under different terms).
- Dan 3:7 — Same structure. **Relevant.**
- Dan 3:10 — "Every man who hears the sound of... every kind of music, shall fall down and worship." Same. **Relevant.**
- Dan 3:15 — "If you are ready when you hear the sound of... every kind of music, to fall down and worship the image... well and good. But if you do not worship, you shall immediately be cast into a burning fiery furnace." The explicit either/or of inner-being orientation — worship the image or face death. **Relevant** — strong verse (the inner-being choice at stake is maximal).

**Group formation:**
**5991-001:** Term names music as the instrument of coerced worship — the signal that tests whether the inner being will orient toward the true God or capitulate to false worship under threat.
Verses: Dan 3:5; Dan 3:7; Dan 3:10; Dan 3:15.
Anchor: **Dan 3:15** ("if you do not worship, you shall immediately be cast into a burning fiery furnace. And who is the god who will deliver you out of my hands?").

### mti:1029 H3034 ya.dah [to give thanks] — 106 verses

**Reading summary:** The primary Hebrew thanksgiving/praise verb. Also carries the "confess" sense (notably in Levitical and Ezra-Nehemiah confession contexts). Corpus covers: confession of sin (Lev 5:5; 16:21; 26:40; Num 5:7; Neh 1:6; 9:2/3; Psa 32:5; Pro 28:13; Ezr 10:1; Dan 9:4/20); giving thanks/praise to God (Gen 29:35; 49:8; the large Psalms corpus; Isaiah doxologies; 1-2Ch liturgical appointments; Neh; Daniel); acknowledgement/confession in legal contexts (1Ki 8:33/35; 2Ch 6:24/26 — "acknowledge your name"; Job 40:14); misdirection (Psa 49:18 — self-praise; Psa 76:10 — wrath of man praising God; Jer 50:14/Lam 3:53 — anomalous uses); Zec 1:21 ("cast down horns" — apparent STEP mismatch); Pro 28:13 (confessing transgressions).

Anomalous entries: Jer 50:14 (target_word "shoot" — military command; unlikely H3034 engagement); Lam 3:53 (target_word "cast" — physical throwing of stones; unlikely H3034 engagement). These appear to be STEP span-match artefacts where a different word in the verse shares the numeric root. Both set aside without flag (not all-verses-fail; other verses pass).

**Filter decisions:**

*Set aside:*
Jer 50:14 — "Shoot at her" — military command; no inner-being engagement through ya.dah. **Set aside.**
Lam 3:53 — "Cast stones on me" — physical act; **Set aside.**
Zec 1:21 — "Cast down the horns" — judgment action; **Set aside.**
2Ch 8:18 — not in this batch (appears to be under G1868).
Job 40:14 — "Then will I also acknowledge to you that your own right hand can save you." God's hypothetical acknowledgment; borderline — the inner-being engagement is God's potential concession. **Set aside** (God's rhetorical challenge rather than inner-being disclosure through ya.dah).
Psa 49:18 — "Though you get praise when you do well for yourself." Self-congratulation; the "praise" here is social approval. **Set aside.**

*Relevant — all remaining 100 verses:*

The corpus divides into three clear inner-being groups:

**(A) Thanksgiving/praise to God** — the large Psalms corpus, Chronicles liturgical passages, Isaiah doxologies: all directly involve the inner-being act of thanksgiving and praise oriented toward God.

**(B) Confession of sin** — Lev 5:5; 16:21; 26:40; Num 5:7; Neh 1:6; 9:2/3; Psa 32:5; Pro 28:13; Ezr 10:1; Dan 9:4/20: confession as the inner-being act of acknowledging sin before God.

**(C) Acknowledging God's name** — 1Ki 8:33/35; 2Ch 6:24/26: the turning of the heart back to God through acknowledgment of his name as the condition of restoration.

Key anchors:
- Gen 29:35 — "This time I will praise the Lord." Leah's deliberate reorientation of inner focus to thanksgiving.
- Psa 9:1 — "I will give thanks to the Lord with my whole heart." Wholehearted thanksgiving.
- Psa 32:5 — "I said, 'I will confess my transgressions to the Lord,' and you forgave the iniquity of my sin." Confession producing forgiveness — inner-being act of transparency before God.
- Psa 111:1 — "I will give thanks to the Lord with my whole heart, in the company of the upright, in the congregation."
- Psa 138:1 — "I give you thanks, O Lord, with my whole heart; before the gods I sing your praise."
- Isa 12:1 — "I will give thanks to you, O Lord, for though you were angry with me, your anger turned away."
- Psa 42:5/11; 43:5 — "I shall again praise him, my salvation" — praise as the anchor of hope for the downcast soul.
- Dan 9:4 — "I prayed to the Lord my God and made confession." Daniel's corporate confession as inner-being act.
- Pro 28:13 — "He who confesses and forsakes them will obtain mercy." Confession leading to restoration.
- Psa 76:10 — "Surely the wrath of man shall praise you." Even human wrath redirected to serve God's praise — an inner-being inversion.

**Group formation:**

**1029-001:** Term names thanksgiving to God as a whole-person inner act — the deliberate orientation of the entire inner being (heart, soul, whole) toward gratitude and acknowledgement of God's character and works.
Verses: Gen 29:35; Gen 49:8; Psa 9:1; Psa 111:1; Psa 138:1; Psa 138:2; Isa 12:1; Isa 12:4; Isa 25:1; Isa 38:19; Jer 33:11; Jer 30:19; Joe 2:26 (already under H1984B); all Psalms give-thanks corpus (Psa 7:17; 18:49; 28:7; 30:4/9/12; 33:2; 35:18; 42:5/11; 43:4/5; 44:8; 45:17; 49:18 set aside; 52:9; 54:6; 57:9; 67:3/5; 71:22; 75:1; 79:13; 86:12; 88:10; 89:5; 92:1; 97:12; 99:3; 100:4; 105:1; 106:1/47; 107:1/8/15/21/31; 108:3; 109:30; 118:1/19/21/28/29; 119:7/62; 122:4; 136:1/2/3/26; 138:1/2; 1Ch 16 series; 2Ch series; Neh series; Ezr 3:11).
Anchor: **Psa 138:1** ("I give you thanks, O Lord, with my whole heart; before the gods I sing your praise"); **Psa 111:1** ("I will give thanks to the Lord with my whole heart, in the company of the upright, in the congregation").

**1029-002:** Term names confession of sin as an inner-being act of transparency before God — the acknowledgment of guilt that enables forgiveness and restoration.
Verses: Lev 5:5; Lev 16:21; Lev 26:40; Num 5:7; Neh 1:6; Neh 9:2/3; Psa 32:5; Pro 28:13; Ezr 10:1; Dan 9:4; Dan 9:20.
Anchor: **Psa 32:5** ("I said, 'I will confess my transgressions to the Lord,' and you forgave the iniquity of my sin"); **Dan 9:4** ("I prayed to the Lord my God and made confession").

**1029-003:** Term names the acknowledgement of God's name as the inner-being act of returning to God — the turning of the heart toward God as condition of answered prayer and restoration.
Verses: 1Ki 8:33; 1Ki 8:35; 2Ch 6:24; 2Ch 6:26; Psa 76:10.
Anchor: **1Ki 8:33** ("if they turn again to you and acknowledge your name and pray and plead with you in this house").

SUMMARY: mti:1029 H3034 ya.dah — 106 verses | Relevant: ~100 | Set aside: ~6 | Groups: 3 (1029-001 through 1029-003) | Anchors: Psa 138:1, Psa 111:1, Psa 32:5, Dan 9:4, 1Ki 8:33

### mti:5990 H4210 miz.mor [melody] — 57 verses

**Reading summary:** The term *miz.mor* is the technical Psalm superscription word — "a psalm" or "melody." All 57 verses are Psalm titles (e.g., "A Psalm of David," "A Psalm of Asaph," "A Psalm of the Sons of Korah"), identifying the poem-song genre.

**§3.5 / Filter assessment:** The term in these 57 verses functions as a genre label in the superscription. The question is whether *miz.mor* as a genre designation engages the inner being through the term itself. Removing it from each superscription: the inner-being content of the Psalm's body does not change through *miz.mor* itself — the term is a formal category marker ("this is a psalm/song"). Per §3.5, a grammatical or functional term that serves as a formal/procedural function does not pass.

However: *miz.mor* as a genre designation is not purely syntactic — it signals that what follows is a composed musical-spiritual expression, and that the composition arises from an inner-being act of devotion, lament, or praise. This is a borderline case: the term itself names the form of the inner-being expression.

**Decision:** Apply §3.3 (retain in uncertainty) — the term names the form of inner expression (a song-poem offered to God), and removing it would remove the identification of this text as a deliberate inner-being musical act. **Relevant** — classified as a single group.

**Group formation:**
**5990-001:** Term names the psalm/song as a designated form of inner-being expression — the compositional act of directing one's whole inner life toward God in structured musical-poetic form.
Verses: All 57 Psalm title verses.
Anchor: **Psa 22:1** ("A Psalm of David. My God, my God, why have you forsaken me?" — the archetypal psalm of inner-being anguish directed toward God); **Psa 23:1** ("A Psalm of David. The Lord is my shepherd; I shall not want" — the archetypal psalm of trust).

SUMMARY: mti:5990 H4210 miz.mor — 57 verses | Relevant: 57 | Set aside: 0 | Groups: 1 (5990-001) | Anchors: Psa 22:1, Psa 23:1

### mti:1027 H8416 te.hil.lah [praise] — 57 verses

**Reading summary:** The primary Hebrew noun for praise — *tehillah*. Covers: God as the praise of his people (Deu 10:21); Israel set as praise for God (Deu 26:19; Jer 13:11); "praise is due to you" (Psa 65:1); God enthroned on the praises of Israel (Psa 22:3); praise as the continual content of the mouth (Psa 34:1; 71:6/8; 145:21); the garment of praise replacing the faint spirit (Isa 61:3); praise as God's exclusive property (Isa 42:8); the people formed to declare God's praise (Isa 43:21); Jerusalem as a praise in the earth (Isa 62:7; Jer 33:9); God as "your praise" (Deu 10:21; Jer 17:14); the Hallel-Psalms cluster (Psa 146-150 series via headings and bodies); praise unable to describe God's greatness (Psa 106:2; 145:3); praise enduring forever (Psa 111:10); the garment of praise (Isa 61:3); the silencing of praise in death/Sheol (indirect).

**Filter decisions:** All 57 verses are relevant — *tehillah* is the noun of praise directed toward God, and every use either names the act, the content, the proper object, or the condition of praise as an inner-being expression.

**Key verses:**
- Psa 22:3 — "Yet you are holy, enthroned on the praises of Israel." God dwelling in the praise of his people — the inner-being act of praise as God's dwelling place. **Strong.**
- Psa 34:1 — "His praise shall continually be in my mouth." Sustained inner orientation.
- Isa 61:3 — "The garment of praise instead of a faint spirit." Praise replacing inner spiritual depletion. **Strong.**
- Deu 10:21 — "He is your praise. He is your God, who has done for you these great and terrifying things." God himself as the object and content of praise. **Strong.**
- Jer 17:14 — "You are my praise." God as the personal praise-object of the prophet.
- Isa 43:21 — "The people whom I formed for myself that they might declare my praise." Human purpose defined by praise.
- Psa 22:25 — "From you comes my praise in the great congregation." Praise originating in God, returned to God.
- Isa 48:9 — "For the sake of my praise I restrain it for you." God's own restraint motivated by the desire that his praise not be compromised.

**Group formation:**

**1027-001:** Term names praise as the defining inner orientation of the person before God — the mouth and heart continually directed toward declaring God's worth.
Verses: Psa 34:1; Psa 71:6/8/14; Psa 145:2/21; Psa 66:2/8; Psa 79:13; Psa 100:4; Psa 102:21; Psa 106:12; Psa 109:1; Psa 111:10; Psa 119:171; Psa 145:1; Psa 147:1; Psa 148:14; Psa 149:1; 2Ch 20:22; Neh 9:5; Neh 12:46; 1Ch 16:35.
Anchor: **Psa 34:1** ("his praise shall continually be in my mouth"); **Psa 22:3** ("yet you are holy, enthroned on the praises of Israel").

**1027-002:** Term names God himself as the content and source of praise — what the inner life is oriented toward and what enables praise to rise.
Verses: Deu 10:21; Jer 17:14; Psa 22:25; Psa 40:3; Isa 42:8; Isa 43:21; Isa 48:9; Isa 62:7; Jer 13:11; Jer 33:9; Hab 3:3; Deu 26:19.
Anchor: **Deu 10:21** ("He is your praise. He is your God, who has done for you these great and terrifying things"); **Isa 43:21** ("the people whom I formed for myself that they might declare my praise").

**1027-003:** Term names praise as a transforming garment — replacing the faint spirit with the inner orientation of worship, or eschatologically restoring shame to honour.
Verses: Isa 61:3; Zep 3:19; Zep 3:20; Exo 15:11; Psa 9:14; Psa 48:10; Psa 65:1; Psa 78:4; Psa 106:2/47; Isa 60:6/18; Isa 61:11; Isa 42:10/12; Isa 60:6; Jer 48:2; Jer 49:25; Jer 51:41; Psa 33:1; Psa 35:28; Psa 51:15; Psa 66:2; Psa 84:4; Psa 86:12 *(some of these overlap 1027-001 — note: verses are assigned uniquely; borderline verses assigned here if they emphasise the transforming/declaring dimension)*.
Anchor: **Isa 61:3** ("the garment of praise instead of a faint spirit, that they may be called oaks of righteousness"); **Psa 22:3** already anchoring 1027-001 — use **Psa 65:1** ("Praise is due to you, O God, in Zion") as secondary anchor for 1027-003.

Note: With 57 verses across 3 groups, some overlap in assignment. The patch builder will treat these as distinct groups; verses are assigned to their primary thematic group.

SUMMARY: mti:1027 H8416 te.hil.lah — 57 verses | Relevant: 57 | Set aside: 0 | Groups: 3 (1027-001 through 1027-003) | Anchors: Psa 34:1, Psa 22:3, Deu 10:21, Isa 43:21, Isa 61:3, Psa 65:1

### mti:1039 H8426 to.dah [thanksgiving] — 30 verses

**Reading summary:** The noun meaning "thanksgiving, thank offering." Covers: thanksgiving sacrifices (Lev 7:12/13/15; 22:29; Psa 50:14/23; 56:12; 107:22; 116:17; 2Ch 29:31; 33:16; Amo 4:5); the thank-offering confession (Jos 7:19 — "give praise to him. And tell me now what you have done"; Ezr 10:11 — confession to God); songs of thanksgiving (Neh 12:27/31/38/40; Jer 30:19; 33:11; Isa 51:3; Psa 26:7; 42:4; 95:2; 100:1/4; 147:7); Jonah's thanksgiving prayer (Jon 2:9); Psa 50:23 ("the one who offers thanksgiving as his sacrifice glorifies me").

**Filter decisions:** All 30 verses relevant — *todah* consistently names an inner-being act of thanksgiving offered to God, whether as sacrifice, song, confession, or prayer. Two standout verses:
- Psa 50:23 — "The one who offers thanksgiving as his sacrifice glorifies me; to one who orders his way rightly I will show the salvation of God!" Thanksgiving as the inner-being disposition that glorifies God. **Strong.**
- Jon 2:9 — "But I with the voice of thanksgiving will sacrifice to you; what I have vowed I will pay." Thanksgiving from the belly of the fish — inner-being orientation maintained in extremity. **Strong.**
- Jos 7:19 — "Give glory to the Lord God of Israel and give praise to him. And tell me now what you have done; do not hide it from me." The todah here carries the confession dimension — thanking/acknowledging God by truthful disclosure. **Strong.**

**Group formation:**

**1039-001:** Term names the thanksgiving sacrifice as an inner-being act of worship — the offering that glorifies God and expresses the grateful orientation of the whole person.
Verses: Lev 7:12/13/15; Lev 22:29; Psa 50:14/23; Psa 56:12; Psa 107:22; Psa 116:17; 2Ch 29:31; 2Ch 33:16; Amo 4:5; Jon 2:9; Jos 7:19; Ezr 10:11.
Anchor: **Psa 50:23** ("the one who offers thanksgiving as his sacrifice glorifies me"); **Jon 2:9** ("with the voice of thanksgiving will sacrifice to you").

**1039-002:** Term names thanksgiving as song and communal expression — the inner-being of gratitude voiced in congregation, procession, and restored community.
Verses: Neh 12:27/31/38/40; Jer 30:19; Jer 33:11; Isa 51:3; Psa 26:7; Psa 42:4; Psa 95:2; Psa 100:1/4; Psa 147:7.
Anchor: **Psa 100:4** ("Enter his gates with thanksgiving, and his courts with praise!"); **Isa 51:3** ("joy and gladness will be found in her, thanksgiving and the voice of song").

SUMMARY: mti:1039 H8426 to.dah — 30 verses | Relevant: 30 | Set aside: 0 | Groups: 2 (1039-001, 1039-002) | Anchors: Psa 50:23, Jon 2:9, Psa 100:4, Isa 51:3

### mti:1042 H8462 te.chil.lah [beginning] — 12 verses

**Reading summary:** The term means "beginning, first." Verses: Gen 13:3; 41:21; 43:18/20; Judg 1:1; 20:18; Neh 11:17; Isa 1:26; Dan 8:1; 9:21/23; Hos 1:2.

**§3.5 / Filter assessment:** *Te.chil.lah* is a temporal marker ("at the beginning," "the first time," "first"). Per §3.5 mental-removal test: does the "beginning/first" qualifier shape or change the inner-being content meaningfully?

- Gen 13:3 — "The place where his tent had been at the beginning." Geographical/temporal. **Set aside.**
- Gen 41:21 — "As ugly as at the beginning." Physical appearance comparison. **Set aside.**
- Gen 43:18 — "Because of the money, which was replaced in our sacks the first time, that we are brought in, so that he may assault us." The "first time" is temporal context for their fear. The inner-being state (fear, anxiety) is present but through the situation, not through *te.chil.lah* itself. **Set aside.**
- Gen 43:20 — "We came down the first time to buy food." Temporal narrative. **Set aside.**
- Judg 1:1 — "Who shall go up first for us against the Canaanites?" The "first" here is procedural/military. **Set aside.**
- Judg 20:18 — "Who shall go up first for us to fight against the people of Benjamin?" Same. **Set aside.**
- Neh 11:17 — "Mattaniah, the son of Mica, son of Zabdi, son of Asaph, who was the leader of the praise, who gave thanks." The target_word is "praise" — but the term is *te.chil.lah* (beginning/leader). Here it appears to render the "leader" sense (leader/beginning of praise). The inner-being engagement is through the praise-leading role — borderline. **Relevant** (borderline — the term here names the leader of the inner-being act of praise; retain §3.3).
- Isa 1:26 — "I will restore your judges as at the first, and your counselors as at the beginning." The restoration of governance to its original state; no inner-being through *te.chil.lah* directly. **Set aside.**
- Dan 8:1 — "A vision appeared to me, Daniel, after that which appeared to me at the first." Temporal reference. **Set aside.**
- Dan 9:21 — "The man Gabriel, whom I had seen in the vision at the first, came to me." Same. **Set aside.**
- Dan 9:23 — "At the beginning of your pleas for mercy a word went out, and I have come to tell it to you, for you are greatly loved." The "beginning of your pleas" — the moment prayer began, God responded. **Relevant** — the temporal marker here directly shapes the inner-being content: the prayer's beginning is the moment of divine response, disclosing the intimacy of the relationship ("you are greatly loved"). The "beginning" here intensifies the inner-being weight — God's response was instantaneous from the first word.
- Hos 1:2 — "When the Lord first spoke through Hosea." Temporal marker for prophetic reception. **Set aside.**

**Group formation:**

**1042-001:** Term names the "beginning" that discloses an inner-being condition — either the moment when prayer begins (and God responds immediately) or the role of leadership in praise.
Verses: Dan 9:23; Neh 11:17.
Anchor: **Dan 9:23** ("at the beginning of your pleas for mercy a word went out... for you are greatly loved").

**All-verses-fail note:** Not triggered — 2 verses pass.

SUMMARY: mti:1042 H8462 te.chil.lah — 12 verses | Relevant: 2 | Set aside: 10 | Groups: 1 (1042-001) | Anchor: Dan 9:23

## Registry 122 — prayer

### mti:1054 G1162 deēsis [petition] — 16 verses

**Reading summary:** *Deēsis* means "petition, supplication, prayer." All 16 verses involve prayer as an inner-being act. Covers: Zechariah's prayer answered (Luk 1:13); Anna's night-and-day prayer (Luk 2:37); Paul's heart's desire and prayer for Israel (Rom 10:1); Jesus's prayers and supplications with loud cries and tears (Heb 5:7); the prayer of a righteous person having great power (Jam 5:16); prayers ascending as God's ears open to the righteous (1Pe 3:12); widows continuing in prayer (1Ti 5:5); Paul's prayers with clear conscience (2Ti 1:3); the Cornelius passage; supplications for all people (1Ti 2:1).

**Filter decisions:** All 16 verses relevant — each names an inner-being act of petition to God, with several explicitly linking inner state to prayer (Rom 10:1 — "my heart's desire and prayer"; Heb 5:7 — "with loud cries and tears"; Jam 5:16 — "the prayer of a righteous person").

**Group formation:**

**1054-001:** Term names petition as the inner-being act of bringing specific need before God — the orientation of the whole person toward God in earnest, sometimes anguished, request.
Verses: Luk 1:13; Luk 2:37; Luk 5:33; Rom 10:1; Heb 5:7; Jam 5:16; 1Pe 3:12; 2Cor 1:11; 2Cor 9:14; Phili 1:4/19; Phili 4:6; 1Ti 2:1; 1Ti 5:5; 2Ti 1:3; Eph 6:18.
Anchor: **Heb 5:7** ("Jesus offered up prayers and supplications, with loud cries and tears, to him who was able to save him from death, and he was heard because of his reverence"); **Rom 10:1** ("my heart's desire and prayer to God for them is that they may be saved").

SUMMARY: mti:1054 G1162 deēsis — 16 verses | Relevant: 16 | Set aside: 0 | Groups: 1 (1054-001) | Anchors: Heb 5:7, Rom 10:1

---

### mti:2336 G1189 deomai [to pray] — 22 verses

**Reading summary:** The verb "to pray, beg, entreat." Several uses are direct prayer to God; others are earnest human-to-human entreating. Some are the desperate pleas of people to Jesus.

**Filter decisions:**

- Mat 9:38 / Luk 10:2 — "Pray earnestly to the Lord of the harvest." Inner orientation of petition to God. **Relevant.**
- Luk 5:12 — "He begged him, 'Lord, if you will, you can make me clean.'" The leper's desperate plea — inner state of need, humility, faith directed to Jesus. **Relevant.**
- Luk 8:28 — "I beg you, do not torment me." Demoniac's cry — inner-being speech of the possessing spirit. **Relevant** (the cry reveals the inner orientation of the spiritual being toward Jesus).
- Luk 8:38 — "The man... begged that he might be with him." The healed man's inner desire for Jesus's presence. **Relevant.**
- Luk 9:38/40 — Father begging for his epileptic son. Inner anguish of a parent. **Relevant.**
- Luk 21:36 — "Praying that you may have strength to escape." Eschatological petition. **Relevant.**
- Luk 22:32 — "I have prayed for you that your faith may not fail." Jesus's intercession for Peter's inner-being (faith). **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Act 4:31 — "When they had prayed, the place was shaken." Corporate prayer. **Relevant.**
- Act 8:22 — "Pray to the Lord that, if possible, the intent of your heart may be forgiven you." Prayer directed at the inner state (intent of heart). **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Act 8:24 — "Pray for me to the Lord." Simon's request for intercession. **Relevant.**
- Act 8:34 — "I ask you, does the prophet say this about himself?" Interpretive question — not a prayer. **Set aside** (the term here is used in the social sense of asking, not petition to God).
- Act 10:2 — Cornelius "prayed continually to God." **Relevant.**
- Act 21:39 — "I beg you, permit me to speak." Social appeal to authority. **Set aside.**
- Act 26:3 — "I beg you to listen to me patiently." Social appeal. **Set aside.**
- Rom 1:10 — "Asking that somehow... I may succeed in coming to you." Prayer-petition combined with desire. **Relevant.**
- 2Cor 5:20 — "We implore you on behalf of Christ, be reconciled to God." Apostolic entreaty — the inner-being call to reconciliation. **Relevant.**
- 2Cor 8:4 — "Begging us earnestly for the favor of taking part in the relief." Social entreaty (Macedonians). **Set aside** (social begging for participation in relief, not prayer).
- 2Cor 10:2 — "I beg of you that when I am present I may not have to show boldness." Personal social appeal. **Set aside.**
- Gal 4:12 — "I entreat you, become as I am." Apostolic appeal — inner-being call. Borderline. **Relevant** (the entreaty calls to an inner-being transformation — "become as I am").
- 1Th 3:10 — "We pray most earnestly night and day that we may see you face to face and supply what is lacking in your faith." Direct prayer to God for another's inner-being (faith). **Relevant.**

**Group formation:**

**2336-001:** Term names earnest petition to God — the inner-being act of urgent, sometimes desperate, prayer directed toward God or Jesus.
Verses: Mat 9:38; Luk 10:2; Luk 21:36; Luk 22:32; Act 4:31; Act 8:22; Act 10:2; Rom 1:10; 1Th 3:10; Luk 5:12; Luk 8:28; Luk 8:38; Luk 9:38/40.
Anchor: **Luk 22:32** ("I have prayed for you that your faith may not fail"); **Act 8:22** ("pray to the Lord that, if possible, the intent of your heart may be forgiven you").

**2336-002:** Term names apostolic entreaty — the earnest inner-being appeal from one person to another calling them toward God, reconciliation, or transformation.
Verses: 2Cor 5:20; Gal 4:12.
Anchor: **2Cor 5:20** ("we implore you on behalf of Christ, be reconciled to God").

SUMMARY: mti:2336 G1189 deomai — 22 verses | Relevant: 17 | Set aside: 5 | Groups: 2 (2336-001, 2336-002) | Anchors: Luk 22:32, Act 8:22, 2Cor 5:20

### mti:1059 G2171 euchē [a vow/prayer] — 3 verses

**Filter decisions:**
- Act 18:18 — Paul under a vow (Nazirite-type). The vow is an inner commitment before God — a binding of the will to God. **Relevant.**
- Act 21:23 — "Four men who are under a vow." Same inner-being commitment. **Relevant.**
- Jam 5:15 — "The prayer of faith will save the one who is sick." Prayer of faith as an inner-being act of trust directed toward God. **Relevant** — strong verse.
