### mti:1053 G4335 proseuchē [prayer] — 36 verses

**Reading summary:** The primary NT prayer noun. All 36 verses involve prayer as an inner-being act — no non-prayer uses. Covers: the house of prayer (Mat/Mar/Luk cleansing of temple); Jesus's all-night prayer (Luk 6:12); prayer and faith (Mat 21:22; Mar 11:24); prayer and forgiveness (Mar 11:25); prayers of the saints as incense before the throne (Rev 5:8; 8:3/4); Cornelius's prayers ascending before God (Act 10:4/31); earnest prayer by the church for Peter (Act 12:5); prayer before sending missionaries (Act 13:3; 14:23); Paul and Silas praying at midnight (Act 16:25); constant prayer (Rom 12:12); striving in prayer (Rom 15:30); prayer and self-control (1Cor 7:5); Paul's ceaseless thanksgiving and prayer (Eph 1:16; 1Th 1:2; Phile 4); prayer in the Spirit (Eph 6:18); the prayer that guards against anxiety (Phili 4:6); steadfastness in prayer (Col 4:2); struggling in prayer (Col 4:12); praying for self-control to guard prayer (1Pe 4:7); prayer hindered by relational sin (1Pe 3:7).

**Filter decisions:** All 36 verses are relevant — the term consistently names prayer as an inner-being act with explicit or implied inner-being dimensions.

**Key anchors:**
- Rev 5:8/8:3/4 — The prayers of the saints as golden bowls of incense rising before God — the ultimate image of prayer as inner-being worship ascending to the divine presence.
- Phili 4:6 — "In everything by prayer and supplication with thanksgiving let your requests be made known to God" — prayer as the inner-being alternative to anxiety.
- 1Pe 3:7 — Relational sin hindering prayer — the inner-being condition of the relationship directly affecting the prayer connection.
- Mar 11:25 — Standing in prayer and the condition of forgiveness — inner state (unforgiveness) blocking prayer's effectiveness.
- 1Cor 7:5 — Mutual agreement for prayer — the deliberate inner-being discipline of setting aside other goods for prayer.
- Col 4:12 — Struggling in prayer — prayer as an act of inner exertion.

**Group formation:**

**1053-001:** Term names prayer as the sustained inner orientation of the person toward God — the discipline, posture, and practice of bringing the whole self before God.
Verses: Mat 21:13; Mar 11:17; Luk 19:46 (house of prayer — the space designed for this inner act); Luk 6:12; Luk 22:45; Act 1:14; Act 2:42; Act 3:1; Act 6:4; Act 16:25; Rom 12:12; Eph 1:16; Col 4:2; 1Th 1:2; Phile 4; Phile 22; 1Ti 2:1; 1Ti 5:5.
Anchor: **Act 2:42** ("they devoted themselves to the apostles' teaching and the fellowship, to the breaking of bread and the prayers"); **Luk 6:12** ("all night he continued in prayer to God").

**1053-002:** Term names prayer as the inner-being medium of access and petition — through which faith receives, the saints' needs ascend, and God responds.
Verses: Mat 21:22; Mar 11:24; Mar 11:25; Rev 5:8; Rev 8:3; Rev 8:4; Act 10:4/31; Act 12:5; Act 14:23; Act 16:13/16; Phili 4:6; Col 4:12; 1Pe 3:7; 1Pe 4:7; Mar 9:29; 1Cor 7:5; Rom 15:30; Jam 5:17.
Anchor: **Rev 8:3** ("the prayers of all the saints on the golden altar before the throne" — prayer as incense ascending to God); **Phili 4:6** ("by prayer and supplication with thanksgiving let your requests be made known to God").

SUMMARY: mti:1053 G4335 proseuchē — 36 verses | Relevant: 36 | Set aside: 0 | Groups: 2 (1053-001, 1053-002) | Anchors: Act 2:42, Luk 6:12, Rev 8:3, Phili 4:6

---

### mti:1056 G4336 proseuchomai [to pray] — 81 verses

**Reading summary:** The primary NT prayer verb — by far the largest term in Registry 122. All 81 verses involve the act of praying. The corpus includes: Jesus's prayer at Gethsemane (Mat 26:36/39/41/42/44; Mar 14:32/35/38/39; Luk 22:41/44/46) — the most anguished prayer in the canon; Jesus praying alone on mountains (Mat 14:23; Mar 1:35; 6:46; Luk 5:16; 6:12; 9:28/29); Jesus's transfiguration prayer (Luk 9:28/29); the Sermon on the Mount instructions on prayer (Mat 6:5/6/7/9); prayer for enemies (Mat 5:44; Luk 6:28); the Lord's Prayer structure; prayer for watchfulness (Mat 26:41; Luk 21:36; 22:40/46); the Pharisee and tax collector (Luk 18:10/11); Jesus teaching on persistence in prayer (Luk 18:1); prayer in tongues vs. mind (1Cor 14:13/14/15); prayer in the Spirit (Eph 6:18; Jude 20); praying without ceasing (1Th 5:17); the early church in corporate prayer throughout Acts; Paul's prayers for communities (Col 1:3/9; 4:3; Eph 6:18; Phili 1:9; 2Th 1:11; 3:1; Heb 13:18); James on prayer in suffering and joy (Jam 5:13/14/17/18); the Spirit's intercession in our weakness (Rom 8:26).

**Filter decisions:** All 81 verses are relevant — prayer is inherently an inner-being act throughout this corpus.

**Key anchors:**
- Mat 26:39 — "My Father, if it be possible, let this cup pass from me; nevertheless, not as I will, but as you will." The archetypal prayer of inner-being surrender — the will fully disclosed and submitted. **Strong.**
- Rom 8:26 — "The Spirit himself intercedes for us with groanings too deep for words." The Spirit's inner prayer when the human inner being cannot form words. **Strong.**
- Mat 6:6 — "When you pray, go into your room and shut the door and pray to your Father who is in secret." The inner-being posture of prayer — secret, unperformed, directed to the Father who sees the hidden life. **Strong.**
- Luk 18:1 — "They ought always to pray and not lose heart." Prayer as the inner-being discipline that sustains hope. **Strong.**
- 1Cor 14:14/15 — "If I pray in a tongue, my spirit prays but my mind is unfruitful... I will pray with my spirit, but I will pray with my mind also." The integration of spirit and mind in prayer. **Strong.**
- 1Th 5:17 — "Pray without ceasing." Prayer as continuous inner orientation. **Strong.**
- Jude 20 — "Praying in the Holy Spirit" — the Spirit-enabled dimension of prayer. **Strong.**

**Group formation:**

**4336-001:** Term names prayer as the inner-being act of bringing the will before God — including surrender, petition, and watchfulness; modelled supremely in Jesus's Gethsemane prayers.
Verses: Mat 26:36/39/41/42/44; Mar 14:32/35/38/39; Luk 22:41/44/46; Mat 14:23; Mar 1:35; 6:46; Luk 5:16; 6:12; 9:28/29; Luk 22:40; Mat 24:20; Mat 19:13; Act 9:40; Act 20:36; Act 21:5; Act 22:17; Act 28:8; Mar 9:29; Jam 5:14.
Anchor: **Mat 26:39** ("My Father, if it be possible, let this cup pass from me; nevertheless, not as I will, but as you will"); **Luk 22:44** ("being in agony he prayed more earnestly; and his sweat became like great drops of blood").

**4336-002:** Term names prayer as the instructed inner-being discipline — the shape, posture, and conditions of authentic prayer taught by Jesus.
Verses: Mat 5:44; Mat 6:5/6/7/9; Luk 6:28; Luk 11:1/2; Luk 18:1/10/11; Luk 20:47; Mar 12:40; Mat 26:41; Mar 13:18; Mar 11:24/25; Luk 21:36; Luk 22:46; 1Ti 2:8; Jam 5:13.
Anchor: **Mat 6:6** ("when you pray, go into your room and shut the door and pray to your Father who is in secret"); **Luk 18:1** ("they ought always to pray and not lose heart").

**4336-003:** Term names corporate and intercessory prayer — the community's inner-being act of praying together, or one person's inner orientation toward another in prayer.
Verses: Act 1:24; Act 4:31 (under G1189); Act 6:6; Act 8:15; Act 9:11; Act 9:40; Act 10:9/30; Act 11:5; Act 12:12; Act 13:3; Act 14:23; Act 16:25; Rom 8:26; 1Cor 11:4/5/13; 1Cor 14:13/14/15; Eph 6:18; Phili 1:9; Col 1:3/9; Col 4:3; 1Th 5:17/25; 2Th 1:11; 3:1; Heb 13:18; Jam 5:17/18; Jude 20; Act 28:8; Luk 1:10.
Anchor: **Rom 8:26** ("the Spirit himself intercedes for us with groanings too deep for words"); **1Th 5:17** ("pray without ceasing").

SUMMARY: mti:1056 G4336 proseuchomai — 81 verses | Relevant: 81 | Set aside: 0 | Groups: 3 (4336-001 through 4336-003) | Anchors: Mat 26:39, Luk 22:44, Mat 6:6, Luk 18:1, Rom 8:26, 1Th 5:17

---

### mti:1057 H3908 la.chash [charm] — 4 verses

**Filter decisions:**
- Isa 3:3 — "The skillful magician and the expert in charms." Social listing of skilled persons in a community — the "expert in charms" is named as a type of person, but no inner-being engagement through *la.chash* directly. **Set aside** (the term names a practitioner role, not an inner-being act).
- Isa 3:20 — "The amulets." Physical objects worn. **Set aside.**
- Isa 26:16 — "They poured out a whispered prayer when your discipline was upon them." The whispered prayer (*la.chash*) in distress — an inner-being cry under divine discipline. **Relevant** — the term names a form of desperate, intimate prayer; the inner-being state (distress under God's hand) directly motivates the prayer-form.
- Jer 8:17 — "Adders that cannot be charmed." Serpents beyond the power of charming. No inner-being engagement. **Set aside.**

**Group formation:**
**1057-001:** Term names the whispered prayer — the desperate, intimate inner-being cry poured out when under divine discipline.
Verses: Isa 26:16.
Anchor: **Isa 26:16** ("in distress they sought you; they poured out a whispered prayer when your discipline was upon them").

SUMMARY: mti:1057 H3908 la.chash — 4 verses | Relevant: 1 | Set aside: 3 | Groups: 1 (1057-001) | Anchor: Isa 26:16

### mti:26 G2744 kauchaomai [to boast] — 32 verses

**Reading summary:** The primary NT boasting verb. The corpus has two distinct semantic streams: (A) legitimate boasting in God, grace, and weakness (Paul's theology of boasting — Rom 5:2/3/11; 1Cor 1:29/31; Gal 6:14; Phili 3:3; Jam 1:9; 2Th 1:4); (B) wrong or hypocritical boasting — in law, in flesh, in outward appearance (Rom 2:17/23; 1Cor 3:21; 4:7; Gal 6:13; Jam 4:16); (C) Paul's extended "foolish boasting" in 2 Corinthians (10:8/13/15/16/17; 11:12/16/18/30; 12:1/5/6/9) — where boasting in weakness becomes the paradox.

**Filter decisions:** All 32 verses relevant — boasting is always an inner-being orientation (whether rightly or wrongly directed). Three verse records appear to be duplicates (5946/186829 Phili 3:3; 5789/186831 Phili 1:26; 5790/186832 Phili 2:16 — all have "None" target_words in the first record). Classify once; patch uses confirmed verse_record_ids.

**Group formation:**

**26-001:** Term names legitimate boasting — the inner-being orientation of glorying in God, grace, weakness, and the cross; the proper direction of human boasting.
Verses: Rom 5:2; Rom 5:3; Rom 5:11; 1Cor 1:29; 1Cor 1:31; Gal 6:14; Phili 3:3; Jam 1:9; 2Th 1:4; 2Cor 12:9.
Anchor: **Gal 6:14** ("far be it from me to boast except in the cross of our Lord Jesus Christ, by which the world has been crucified to me, and I to the world"); **2Cor 12:9** ("therefore I will boast all the more gladly of my weaknesses, so that the power of Christ may rest upon me").

**26-002:** Term names illegitimate boasting — the inner orientation of pride that asserts itself in law, flesh, or outward appearance rather than in God.
Verses: Rom 2:17; Rom 2:23; 1Cor 3:21; 1Cor 4:7; Gal 6:13; Jam 4:16; 2Cor 5:12 (those who boast in outward appearance, not in the heart).
Anchor: **1Cor 4:7** ("if then you received it, why do you boast as if you did not receive it?"); **2Cor 5:12** ("those who boast about outward appearance and not about what is in the heart").

**26-003:** Term names Paul's paradoxical boasting in weakness — the sustained inner-being act of turning normal pride on its head, boasting of what brings shame in order to reveal divine power.
Verses: 2Cor 10:8/13/15/16/17; 11:12/16/18/30; 12:1/5/6; 2Cor 7:14; 2Cor 9:2; 2Cor 11:12.
Anchor: **2Cor 11:30** ("if I must boast, I will boast of the things that show my weakness").

SUMMARY: mti:26 G2744 kauchaomai — 32 verses | Relevant: 32 | Set aside: 0 | Groups: 3 (26-001 through 26-003) | Anchors: Gal 6:14, 2Cor 12:9, 1Cor 4:7, 2Cor 5:12, 2Cor 11:30

---

### mti:27 G2745 kauchēma [pride] — 11 verses

**Note:** Several verse records with target_word "None" (5789/186831; 5790/186832) appear to be duplicates. Classify the distinct verses.

**Filter decisions:** All 11 verses relevant — the noun of boasting always engages inner-being orientation.

**Key verses:**
- Rom 4:2 — Abraham's potential boast before men, but not before God. **Strong** (the inner-being distinction between human and divine assessment).
- 1Cor 5:6 — "Your boasting is not good. Do you not know that a little leaven leavens the whole lump?" Boasting in the face of sin — inner corruption of the community. **Strong.**
- Heb 3:6 — "If indeed we hold fast our confidence and our boasting in our hope." Boasting in hope as an inner posture to be maintained. **Strong.**
- 2Cor 5:12 — Boasting about what is in the heart vs. outward appearance. **Strong.**

**Group formation:**
**27-001:** Term names the ground of legitimate boasting — what one may rightly claim before God or others, and the contrast between human and divine standards.
Verses: Rom 4:2; 1Cor 9:15/16; 2Cor 1:14; 2Cor 5:12; Gal 6:4; Phili 1:26; Phili 2:16; Heb 3:6.
Anchor: **Heb 3:6** ("we hold fast our confidence and our boasting in our hope"); **2Cor 5:12** (boasting about what is in the heart, not outward appearance).

**27-002:** Term names the corrupted boasting that undermines community — pride in the face of sin.
Verses: 1Cor 5:6; 2Cor 9:3.
Anchor: **1Cor 5:6** ("your boasting is not good; do you not know that a little leaven leavens the whole lump?").

SUMMARY: mti:27 G2745 kauchēma — 11 verses | Relevant: 11 | Set aside: 0 | Groups: 2 (27-001, 27-002) | Anchors: Heb 3:6, 2Cor 5:12, 1Cor 5:6

### mti:6016 G5188 tufō [to smoulder] — 1 verse

**Filter decision:**
- Mat 12:20 — "A bruised reed he will not break, and a smoldering wick he will not quench, until he brings justice to victory." The smoldering wick is an image of fragile, barely-surviving inner life. The verse discloses God's inner orientation (compassion toward the barely surviving) — the term names the condition of the vulnerable inner being. **Relevant** (§3.4 — the smoldering wick names a state of near-extinguished inner spiritual life; God's response is the inner-being disclosure).

**Group formation:**

### mti:6040 H1358 gov [den] — 8 verses

**Reading summary:** All 8 verses = the den of lions in Daniel 6 (Dan 6:7/12/16/17/19/20/23/24).

**Filter decisions:**

The lion's den is the setting for Daniel's deliverance — a test of faith and trust. The question is whether *gov* (den) as a spatial term engages the inner being through the term itself.

Mentally removing "den" from each verse: the inner-being content (Daniel's trust in God, the king's distress, Daniel's deliverance) does not change through the term *gov* — the "den" is the spatial setting for an inner-being narrative, but the term itself names the location, not the inner-being.

**However:** Dan 6:20 is notable — "As he came near to the den where Daniel was, he cried out in a tone of anguish. The king declared to Daniel, 'O Daniel, servant of the living God, has your God, whom you serve continually, been able to deliver you from the lions?'" The king's anguish and the question about deliverance are inner-being rich — but the anguish is in the king's cry, not in *gov*.

**Decision:** All 8 verses set aside. The term names the physical space. **Set aside.**

⚠ **ALL-VERSES-FAIL FLAG — mti:6040 H1358 gov [den]**
- 8 verses: All name the physical lion's den in Daniel 6.
- **Claude AI assessment:** The term is a geographical/spatial descriptor throughout. The inner-being richness of the Daniel 6 narrative is carried by other terms, not by *gov*. All-verses-fail is analytically clear.
- **Awaiting researcher decision.**

### mti:165 H4791 ma.rom [height] — 52 verses

**Reading summary:** The term means "height, on high." Verses divide between: (A) God dwelling "on high" / acting "from on high" — his transcendent position and action (Psa 7:7; 18:16; 68:18; 71:19; 92:8; 93:4; 102:19; Job 16:19; 25:2; Isa 32:15; 33:5/16; Isa 40:26; 57:15; Jer 17:12; 25:30; 31:12; Mic 6:6; Hab 2:9; many Psalms "from on high" rescue passages); (B) human pride/height used against God (2Ki 19:22/23; Isa 37:23/24 — Sennacherib's arrogant heights; Isa 24:21 — host of heaven punished; Jer 49:16; Jer 51:53 — Babylon mounting to heaven; Obd 3; Eze 17:23; 20:40; 34:14 — mountain heights of Israel); (C) spatial/geographical uses (Judg 5:18 — heights of the field; Isa 22:16; 24:4; 24:18; 40:26; various geographical); (D) wisdom on heights (Pro 8:2; 9:3/14 — Wisdom and Folly calling from the heights); (E) human arrogance "speaking loftily" (Psa 56:2; 73:8; 75:5; Psa 10:5; Ecc 10:6).

**Filter decisions:**

*Set aside — purely spatial/geographical:*
Judg 5:18 (heights of the field — military geography); Job 39:18 (ostrich flees — physical); Isa 22:16 (tomb carved at height — physical); Isa 24:4 (highest people languish — sociological but not inner-being through this term); Isa 24:18 (windows of heaven — cosmic/physical); Isa 24:21 (host of heaven punished — cosmic-political); Isa 40:26 (lift eyes to the heights and see stars — observational); Pro 8:2 (Wisdom on heights calling — spatial position of Wisdom); Pro 9:3/14 (Wisdom and Folly on heights — spatial); Ecc 10:6 (folly set in high places — social/political); Psa 144:7 (hand from on high for physical rescue); Psa 148:1 (praise from the heights — spatial); Jer 25:30 (Lord roaring from on high — metaphor of judicial speech, not inner-being through *ma.rom*); Jer 51:53 (Babylon mounts to heaven — hypothetical spatial); Eze 17:23 (mountain height of Israel — geographical); Eze 20:40 (holy mountain of Israel — spatial); Eze 34:14 (mountain heights of Israel — pastoral geography); Obd 3 (height of the hill — geographical, inner-being is through the heart of pride, not *ma.rom*); Isa 49:11 (highways raised up — physical); Isa 62:10 (highway — physical); Isa 58:4 (voice not heard on high — liturgical/practical).

*Relevant — inner-being engagement through this term:*

- 2Sa 22:17 / Psa 18:16 — "He sent from on high, he took me." God's rescue from the inner-being position of distress. **Relevant** (God's inner orientation of care expressed through "from on high").
- 2Ki 19:22 — "Against whom have you raised your voice and lifted your eyes to the heights? Against the Holy One of Israel!" Sennacherib's inner arrogance directed against God. **Relevant.**
- 2Ki 19:23 — Same — "I have gone up the heights of the mountains... I entered its farthest lodging place." Inner arrogance expressed in claims of conquest. **Relevant.**
- Job 5:11 — "He sets on high those who are lowly." God's action on behalf of the humble — inner-being reversal. **Relevant.**
- Job 16:19 — "My witness is in heaven, and he who testifies for me is on high." Job's inner-being assurance of divine advocacy. **Relevant.**
- Job 25:2 — "He makes peace in his high heaven." God's sovereign inner-being expressed as peace in his heights. **Relevant.**
- Job 31:2 — "What would be my portion from God above and my heritage from the Almighty on high?" Job's inner-being assessment of divine judgment. **Relevant.**
- Psa 7:7 — "Over it return on high." Appeal to God's transcendent justice. **Relevant.**
- Psa 10:5 — "Your judgments are on high, out of his sight." The wicked's inner state — God's judgment beyond their perception. **Relevant.**
- Psa 18:16 — As above. **Relevant.**
- Psa 56:2 — "Many attack me proudly." Pride-height as inner-being attack. **Relevant.**
- Psa 68:18 — "You ascended on high, leading a host of captives." God's triumphant inner-being expressed in ascent. **Relevant.**
- Psa 71:19 — "Your righteousness, O God, reaches the high heavens." God's righteousness at the height of his being. **Relevant.**
- Psa 73:8 — "Loftily they threaten oppression." The arrogant inner orientation of oppressors. **Relevant.**
- Psa 75:5 — "Do not lift up your horn on high, or speak with haughty neck." Inner-being warning against pride. **Relevant.**
- Psa 92:8 — "But you, O Lord, are on high forever." God's eternal position. **Relevant.**
- Psa 93:4 — "The Lord on high is mighty." God's inner-being of might from his height. **Relevant.**
- Psa 102:19 — "He looked down from his holy height." God's inner attention from on high. **Relevant.**
- Isa 26:5 — "He has humbled the inhabitants of the height, the lofty city." Pride humbled. **Relevant.**
- Isa 32:15 — "Until the Spirit is poured upon us from on high." God's Spirit given from his transcendent position — direct inner-being impartation. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Isa 33:5 — "The Lord is exalted, for he dwells on high." **Relevant.**
- Isa 33:16 — "He will dwell on the heights; his place of defense will be the fortresses of rocks." Righteous person's security from God's height. **Relevant.**
- Isa 37:23/24 — Parallel to 2Ki 19. **Relevant.**
- Isa 38:14 — "My eyes are weary with looking upward. O Lord, I am oppressed; be my pledge of safety!" Inner-being distress looking upward for God. **Relevant.**
- Isa 40:26 — Set aside above (observational).
- Isa 57:15 — "For thus says the One who is high and lifted up, who inhabits eternity, whose name is Holy: I dwell in the high and holy place, and also with him who is of a contrite and lowly spirit, to revive the spirit of the lowly, and to revive the heart of the contrite." **Relevant** — strong verse (God's heights directly linked to the lowly spirit and contrite heart).
- Jer 17:12 — "A glorious throne set on high from the beginning is the place of our sanctuary." The sanctuary on high as the inner-being dwelling place of God's glory. **Relevant.**

- Jer 49:16 — "The pride of your heart, you who hold the height of the hill." Height as the location of pride — the term here modifies the geographical pride-position. **Relevant** (the "height" intensifies the inner-being pride).

- Mic 6:6 — "With what shall I come before the Lord, and bow myself before God on high?" Inner-being posture of approaching the transcendent God. **Relevant.**
- Hab 2:9 — "To set his nest on high, to be safe from the reach of harm." The inner motivation of evil gain (pride of self-protection). **Relevant.**
- Psa 138:6 — "For though the Lord is high, he regards the lowly, but the haughty he knows from afar." Inner-being contrast: lowly vs. haughty, both seen by the high God. **Relevant.**

**Group formation:**

**165-001:** Term names God's transcendent position on high — from which he acts, rescues, and pours out his Spirit on the lowly; the height of God as the origin of his inner-being engagement with the world.
Verses: 2Sa 22:17/Psa 18:16; Job 5:11; Job 16:19; Job 25:2; Job 31:2; Psa 7:7; Psa 68:18; Psa 71:19; Psa 92:8; Psa 93:4; Psa 102:19; Isa 32:15; Isa 33:5; Isa 33:16; Isa 57:15; Isa 38:14; Jer 17:12; Mic 6:6; Psa 138:6; Lam 1:13.

### mti:6007 H4805H me.ri [rebellion] — 21 verses

**Reading summary:** The term means "rebellion, obstinacy." Primarily appears in Ezekiel as the repeated descriptor "rebellious house" for Israel. Also: Num 17:10 (rebels/sign for the grumblers); Deu 31:27 (rebellious and stubborn); 1Sa 15:23 (rebellion as sin of divination); Neh 9:17 (stiffened neck, appointed leader to return to Egypt); Job 23:2 (complaint described as bitter — this is an anomalous rendering of Job 23:2 under *me.ri*); Pro 17:11 (evil man seeks only rebellion); Isa 30:9 (rebellious people).

**Filter decisions:**

- Num 17:10 — "Put back the staff of Aaron before the testimony, to be kept as a sign for the rebels." The rebels here are those who grumbled; the sign for the inner-being orientation of rebellion. **Relevant.**
- Deu 31:27 — "I know how rebellious and stubborn you are." Rebellion and stubbornness as inner-being character indictment. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- 1Sa 15:23 — "Rebellion is as the sin of divination, and presumption is as iniquity and idolatry." Rebellion equated to profound inner-being sin. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Neh 9:17 — "Egypt" (target_word) — this appears to be a STEP span artefact where the term *me.ri* is associated with "Egypt" in the phrase "appointed a leader to return to their slavery in Egypt." The sentence is about rebellion, but the target_word "Egypt" is not the inner-being engagement. **Set aside** (the inner-being content is in the rebellion, not in "Egypt" as the target word for this term).
- Job 23:2 — "My complaint is bitter" — the target_word is "bitter." This is likely a homograph or STEP span issue — H4805H (*me.ri* = rebellion/bitterness) here rendering Job's bitterness. **Relevant** (Job's inner condition of bitterness/contention is directly named).
- Pro 17:11 — "An evil man seeks only rebellion, and a cruel messenger will be sent against him." Rebellion as the inner-being desire of the evil person. **Relevant.**
- Isa 30:9 — "They are a rebellious people, lying children, children unwilling to hear the instruction of the Lord." Rebellion and unwillingness as inner-being orientation. **Relevant.**
- Eze 2:5/6/7/8 — The "rebellious house" refrain. Each use names Israel's inner-being orientation of persistent rebellion against God. **Relevant** — all 4.
- Eze 3:9 — "For they are a rebellious house." Same. **Relevant.**
- Eze 3:26/27 — "Rebellious house" — the characterisation that governs Ezekiel's prophetic context. **Relevant** (both).
- Eze 12:2/3/9/25 — "Rebellious house" refrain. **Relevant** (all 4).
- Eze 17:12 — "Say now to the rebellious house." **Relevant.**
- Eze 24:3 — "Utter a parable to the rebellious house." **Relevant.**
- Eze 44:6 — "Say to the rebellious house, to the house of Israel." **Relevant.**

**Group formation:**

**6007-001:** Term names rebellion as an inner-being condition of the community before God — the persistent, characterising orientation of wilful defiance, stubbornness, and unwillingness to hear God's word.
Verses: Num 17:10; Deu 31:27; 1Sa 15:23; Pro 17:11; Isa 30:9; Eze 2:5/6/7/8; Eze 3:9/26/27; Eze 12:2/3/9/25; Eze 17:12; Eze 24:3; Eze 44:6; Job 23:2.
Anchor: **1Sa 15:23** ("rebellion is as the sin of divination, and presumption is as iniquity and idolatry"); **Deu 31:27** ("I know how rebellious and stubborn you are").

### mti:6025 H7311A rum [to exalt] — 184 verses

**Data note:** H7311A rum and H7311B ra.mam are separate entries with distinct verse_record_id sets (confirmed 0 overlap). Both share the same root and semantic range. Classified independently.

**Reading summary:** The root *rum* in its exalt/lift-up sense covers an enormous range: physical lifting of objects/persons (many Lev/Num/Exo contribution-lifting verses); physical height descriptions (tall people — Deu; trees — Eze 31); positional lifting (stones, cloak, etc.); God exalting persons and nations; persons exalting God; pride expressed as self-lifting; the Spirit going up; the king's heart being lifted up (Deu 17:20; Dan 11:12); God's name exalted (Neh 9:5); and the critical set of exalt/extol verses in Psalms.

**Filter approach:** Apply §3 term-level filter systematically. This is a large corpus with many spatial/physical uses. I will classify by category.

**Set aside — purely physical lifting/height/spatial:**
Gen 7:17 (ark rose high — physical); Gen 31:45 (stone set up — physical); Gen 39:15/18 (voice lifted — §3.4 below); Gen 41:44 (lift hand or foot — physical gesture); Exo 7:20 (staff lifted up — physical action); Exo 14:16 (lift staff — physical); Exo 17:11 (Moses held up hand — physical); Exo 29:27 (wave offering — liturgical ritual); Exo 35:24 (contribution of silver/bronze — material); Lev 2:9; 4:8/10/19; 6:10/15 (priest taking portions — liturgical); Lev 22:15 (contribute holy things — liturgical); Num 15:19/20 (present contribution — liturgical); Num 16:37 (take up censers — physical); Num 18:19/24/26/28/29/30/32 (present contributions — liturgical; inner-being of the offering is in the act of giving, but the term here is the physical presentation — borderline); Num 20:11 (Moses lifted hand — physical); Num 24:7 (kingdom exalted — political); Num 31:28/52 (levy/tribute — fiscal); Num 33:3 (went out triumphantly — march); Jos 4:5 (take up stones — physical); 1Sa 9:24 (cook took up — physical); 2Ki 2:13 (took up cloak — physical); 2Ki 6:7 (take it up — physical); 1Ch 15:16 (raise sounds of joy — musical); 2Ch 30:24; 35:7/8/9 (gave/contributed — fiscal); Ezr 3:12 (shout aloud — vocal); Ezr 8:25 (weighed out/offered — fiscal); Ezr 9:9 (set up house — construction); Neh 9:5 (exalted name — see below); Eze 10:4/16/17 (glory/wings going up — visionary/physical); Eze 17:22 (cedar top — botanical); Eze 20:28/34:6 (high hill — geographical); Eze 21:22/26 (battering rams; turban removed — military/physical); Eze 31:4 (waters making grow tall — natural); Eze 45:1/9/13; 48:8/9/20 (set apart portions — territorial/liturgical); Dan 8:11 (regular offering taken away — liturgical-political); Dan 12:7 (raised hand to swear — oath gesture); Deu 1:28; 2:10/21; 9:2 (tall people — physical height); Deu 12:2 (high mountains — geographical); Deu 27:14 (loud voice — volume); Deu 32:27 (triumphant — political boast); Isa 1:2 (children reared up — parenting); Isa 2:12/13/14 (lofty mountains, trees — natural height); Isa 10:15 (rod lifts — mechanical); Isa 10:33 (great in height — physical); Isa 13:2 (cry aloud — vocal); Isa 23:4 (brought up — parenting); Isa 40:9 (up to high mountain — geographical); Isa 49:11 (highways raised — construction); Isa 49:22 (signal raised — political); Isa 57:14/58:1 (build up/cry up — construction/vocal); Isa 62:10 (highway; signal — construction/political); Lam 2:17 (enemy's might exalted — political result); Eze 6:13 (high hill — geographical); Eze 34:6; Eze 45 series; Mic 5:9 (hand lifted over adversaries — military); Hos 11:4 (yoke eased — physical); Job 17:4 (triumph closed — judicial); Job 21:22; 22:12; 38:15/34 (high/lofty — spatial); Job 39:27 (eagle nests high — natural); Pro 3:35 (get disgrace — result); Pro 24:7 (wisdom too high — metaphorical but not inner-being through this term); Pro 30:13 (lofty eyes — §3.4 below); Psa 74:3; Psa 78:69/89:13; 92:8 — already assessed; Isa 6:1 (Lord on throne high — see below); 2Ch 5:13 (song raised — musical performance).

*Assess further:*

- Gen 39:15/18 — "I lifted up my voice and cried out." Crying out as an expression of inner-being distress (§3.4 — the lifting of the voice is the expression of inner distress/alarm). **Relevant.**
- Exo 14:8 — "The people of Israel were going out defiantly." The term here = "with a high hand" = defiantly — the inner-being posture of boldness or defiance. **Relevant.**
- Exo 15:2 — "I will exalt him." Worship-exaltation of God. **Relevant.**
- 1Sa 2:1 — Hannah: "My heart exults in the Lord; my horn is exalted in the Lord." Heart and horn explicitly named. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- 1Sa 2:7 — "He brings low and he exalts." God's inner-being sovereignty over human status. **Relevant.**
- 1Sa 2:8 — "He lifts the needy from the ash heap." God's inner-being compassion expressed in social reversal. **Relevant.**
- 1Sa 2:10 — "He will exalt the horn of his anointed." God's favour. **Relevant.**
- 1Ki 11:26/27 — Jeroboam "lifted up his hand against the king." Rebellion — inner-being act of defiance. **Relevant** (§3.4 — the lifted hand is the outward expression of inner defiance).
- 1Ki 14:7 / 1Ki 16:2 — "Because I exalted you from among the people and made you leader." God's inner act of elevation. **Relevant.**
- 2Sa 22:28 — "The haughty eyes you bring down." Pride of the eyes — inner-being. **Relevant.**
- 2Sa 22:47/49 — "Exalted be my God... you exalted me above those who rose against me." Worship and divine elevation. **Relevant.**
- 2Ch 5:13 — song raised — already set aside above as musical performance. **Set aside.**
- 1Ch 25:5 — "The promise of God to exalt him." Divine promise to honour. **Relevant.**
- Neh 9:5 — "Your glorious name, which is exalted above all blessing and praise." God's name exalted — inner-being act of worship. **Relevant.**
- Ezr 9:6 — "I am ashamed and blush to lift my face to you, my God." Inner-being of shame preventing the lifting of the face before God. **Relevant** — strong inner-being verse.
- Dan 11:12 — "His heart shall be exalted." Exaltation of inner-being producing overreaching. **Relevant.**

### mti:6026 H8641 te.ru.mah [contribution] — 63 verses

**Reading summary:** The term means "contribution, offering, portion set apart." The large corpus covers: Exodus freewill offerings for the tabernacle (Exo 25:2/3; 29:27/28; 30:13/14/15; 35:5/21/24; 36:3/6); Levitical priestly portions (Lev 7:14/32/34; 10:14/15; 22:12); various Num 15/18 contribution laws; Deut 12 tithing; 2Sa 1:21 (fields of offerings); 2Ch 31 Hezekiah's contribution reform; Ezra 8:25; Neh 10:37/39; 12:44; 13:5; Pro 29:4 (king who exacts gifts); Isa 40:20 (impoverished offering); Eze 20:40 (contributions accepted on holy mountain); Eze 44:30 (firstfruits and blessing); Eze 45 and 48 series (holy portion/district); Mal 3:8 (robbing God of contributions).

**Filter decisions:**

The term *te.ru.mah* (contribution/offering) names a liturgical-economic act — presenting something set apart to God. The inner-being question: does the act of contributing/offering engage the inner being through this term?

The key issue is that *te.ru.mah* in many of its uses is a technical term for the category of contribution (a portion set aside for God or priests) — similar to H5207 *nicho'ach* (pleasing aroma). In those cases, the term functions as a regulatory label rather than a direct inner-being descriptor.

**However**, the following verses carry direct inner-being engagement through *te.ru.mah*:

- Exo 25:2 — "From every man **whose heart moves him** you shall receive the contribution for me." The contribution is explicitly grounded in the inner-being motivation of the heart. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Exo 35:5 — "Whoever is of a **generous heart**, let him bring the Lord's contribution." Same pattern. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Exo 35:21 — "Everyone **whose heart stirred him**, and everyone **whose spirit moved him**, and brought the Lord's contribution." Heart and spirit explicitly named as the motivating inner-being. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Mal 3:8 — "Will man rob God? Yet you are robbing me... in your tithes and contributions." The inner moral failure of withholding what belongs to God. **Relevant.**
- Eze 20:40 — "There I will require your contributions and the choicest of your gifts, with all your sacred offerings." God's inner-being demand for the restored Israel's offerings. **Relevant** (God's inner orientation toward receiving the people's contribution).
- Eze 44:30 — "That a blessing may rest on your house." The contribution as the condition for divine blessing — the inner orientation of giving producing the inner blessing. **Relevant.**
- 2Ch 31:10 — "Since they began to bring the contributions into the house of the Lord, we have eaten and had enough and have plenty left, for the Lord has blessed his people." The act of contribution producing inner and material blessing. **Relevant.**
- Pro 29:4 — "A king who exacts gifts tears it down." The inner-being of unjust extraction destroying the community. **Relevant.**
- Num 31:29 (levy as contribution) — administrative/military. **Set aside.**

*The remaining bulk of the Levitical/Numbers/Deuteronomy/Ezekiel-land-portion verses* function as regulatory specifications for what constitutes a *te.ru.mah* and who receives it. These are closer to legal/procedural usage. Applying §3.3 (retain in uncertainty): the act of presenting a contribution to God is always potentially an inner-being act (the orientation of giving to God), but applied as a formula across 40+ regulatory verses, the incremental inner-being content is minimal per verse. I will include a representative set anchoring the theological meaning and set aside the purely procedural iterations.

**Decision:** Retain all verses where the motivation (heart, spirit) or consequence (blessing, relationship with God) is named; retain formula instances that establish the theological inner-being meaning of contribution; set aside purely procedural measurement/specification verses (especially the Eze 45/48 land-portion series).

*Set aside — purely procedural/territorial:*
Eze 45:1/6/7/13/16; 48:8/9/10/12/18/20/21 (land-portion specifications — these are architectural/territorial, not contribution in the inner-being sense); Num 31:29/41/52 (military levy — fiscal); Num 18:8/11/19/24/26/27/28/29/30 (priestly portion specifications — regulatory); 2Sa 1:21 (fields of offerings — land imagery); Isa 40:20 (impoverished offering — physical material issue); Num 15:19/20/21 (threshing-floor contribution — agricultural/regulatory); Lev 22:12 (priestly daughter — legal/social); Lev 7:14 (one loaf as gift — ritual specification); Ezr 8:25 (silver weighed out — fiscal transaction).

*Relevant:*
Exo 25:2; Exo 25:3; Exo 29:27/28; Exo 30:13/14/15; Exo 35:5/21/24; Exo 36:3/6; Lev 7:32/34; Lev 10:14/15; 2Ch 31:10/12/14; Neh 10:37/39; Neh 12:44; Neh 13:5; Eze 20:40; Eze 44:30; Mal 3:8; Pro 29:4; Deu 12:6/11/17; 2Ch 35:7/8/9 (willing contribution to the Passover); Num 18:8 (borderline — retain as establishing the priestly share).

**Group formation:**

**6026-001:** Term names the contribution that arises from the stirred heart and moving spirit — the inner-being act of giving to God from personal devotion.
Verses: Exo 25:2; Exo 35:5; Exo 35:21; Exo 36:3; Exo 36:6; 2Ch 35:7/8/9.
Anchor: **Exo 35:21** ("everyone whose heart stirred him, and everyone whose spirit moved him, and brought the Lord's contribution"); **Exo 25:2** ("from every man whose heart moves him you shall receive the contribution").

**6026-002:** Term names the contribution as the condition of divine blessing and the measure of faithfulness — giving to God as the inner-being orientation of covenant loyalty.
Verses: Mal 3:8; Eze 44:30; 2Ch 31:10/12/14; Neh 10:37/39; Neh 12:44; Eze 20:40; Pro 29:4; Deu 12:6/11/17.
Anchor: **Mal 3:8** ("will man rob God? Yet you are robbing me... in your tithes and contributions"); **Eze 44:30** ("the first of all the firstfruits... shall belong to the priests... that a blessing may rest on your house").

SUMMARY: mti:6026 H8641 te.ru.mah — 63 verses | Relevant: ~30 | Set aside: ~33 | Groups: 2 (6026-001, 6026-002) | Anchors: Exo 35:21, Exo 25:2, Mal 3:8, Eze 44:30

---

### mti:100 H1361 ga.vah [to exult] — 33 verses

**Reading summary:** The verb "to be/become high, exalted; to be haughty." Covers: physical tallness (1Sa 10:23 — Saul taller; Deu related); courage/lifted heart (2Ch 17:6 — Jehoshaphat courageous); pride-to-destruction (2Ch 26:16; 32:25; Eze 28:2/5/17; Eze 16:50; 31:10; Zep 3:11); positive exaltation/lifting (Job 36:7; 1Sa 10:23 borderline; Isa 5:16; 52:13; 55:9; Psa 103:11; 113:5; 131:1); physical/natural height (Job 5:7; 35:5; 39:27; Eze 17:24; 19:11; 21:26; 31:5/14; Job 5:7); contextual (Pro 17:19; 18:12; Eze 28:2/5/17 — Tyre's pride; Jer 13:15; 49:16; Eze 16:50; 31:10; Obd 4; Zep 3:11).

**Filter decisions:**

- 1Sa 10:23 — Saul taller than any. Physical height. **Set aside.**
- 2Ch 17:6 — "His heart was courageous in the ways of the Lord." Inner-being courage directed toward God. **Relevant** — the term here means his heart was "lifted high" = courageous/devoted.
- 2Ch 26:16 — "He grew proud, to his destruction. For he was unfaithful to the Lord." Heart-pride causing spiritual unfaithfulness. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- 2Ch 32:25 — "His heart was proud. Therefore wrath came upon him." Heart-pride named. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- 2Ch 33:14 — "Raised it to a very great height." Construction/physical. **Set aside.**
- Job 5:7 — "Sparks fly upward." Natural/physical. **Set aside.**
- Job 35:5 — "The clouds, which are higher than you." Natural. **Set aside.**
- Job 36:7 — "With kings on the throne he sets them forever, and they are exalted." God's exaltation of the righteous. **Relevant.**
- Job 39:27 — "The eagle mounts up and makes his nest on high." Natural. **Set aside.**
- Psa 103:11 — "As high as the heavens are above the earth, so great is his steadfast love." The height metaphor measures God's inner-being of steadfast love. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Psa 113:5 — "Who is like the Lord our God, who is seated on high." God's transcendent position. **Relevant.**
- Psa 131:1 — "My heart is not lifted up; my eyes are not raised too high." Inner-being humility. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Pro 17:19 — "He who makes his door high seeks destruction." Pride expressed in ostentation. **Relevant** (borderline — retain §3.3).
- Pro 18:12 — "Before destruction a man's heart is haughty, but humility comes before honor." Heart-pride named. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Isa 3:16 — "The daughters of Zion are haughty and walk with outstretched necks." Inner-being of pride expressed in posture. **Relevant** (§3.4).
- Isa 5:16 — "The Lord of hosts is exalted in justice." God's inner-being of justice expressed in exaltation. **Relevant.**
- Isa 7:11 — "Let it be deep as Sheol or high as heaven." Range of possibility — spatial. **Set aside.**
- Isa 52:13 — "He shall be high and lifted up, and shall be exalted." Servant's exaltation. **Relevant.**
- Isa 55:9 — "My ways are higher than your ways and my thoughts than your thoughts." God's inner-being transcends human inner-being. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Jer 13:15 — "Be not proud, for the Lord has spoken." Direct inner-being warning. **Relevant.**
- Jer 49:16 — "The pride of your heart, you who hold the height of the hill." Heart named. **Relevant.**
- Eze 16:50 — "They were haughty and did an abomination before me." Inner-being of haughtiness. **Relevant.**
- Eze 17:24 — "I bring low the high tree, and make high the low tree." God's sovereign reversal — inner-being of divine justice. **Relevant.**
- Eze 19:11 — "It towered aloft among the thick boughs." Physical/botanical (vine metaphor). **Set aside.**
- Eze 21:26 — "Exalt that which is low, and bring low that which is exalted." God's sovereign reversal. **Relevant.**
- Eze 28:2 — "Because your heart is proud, and you have said, 'I am a god.'" Heart of pride explicitly named. **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Eze 28:5 — "Your heart has become proud in your wealth." **Relevant.**
- Eze 28:17 — "Your heart was proud because of your beauty." **Relevant.**
- Eze 31:5 — "It towered high above all the trees." Botanical/physical (cedar metaphor). **Set aside.**
- Eze 31:10 — "Its heart was proud of its height." Pride as inner condition. **Relevant.**
- Eze 31:14 — "No trees... may grow to towering height." Botanical instruction from judgment. **Set aside.**
- Obd 4 — "Though you soar aloft like the eagle, though your nest is set among the stars, from there I will bring you down." Inner-being of self-exaltation and divine judgment. **Relevant.**
- Zep 3:11 — "You shall no longer be haughty in my holy mountain." **Relevant.**

**Group formation:**

**100-001:** Term names the proud heart — the inner-being of self-exaltation that leads to unfaithfulness, destruction, or divine judgment.
Verses: 2Ch 26:16; 2Ch 32:25; Pro 18:12; Eze 28:2; Eze 28:5; Eze 28:17; Eze 31:10; Eze 16:50; Eze 21:26; Obd 4; Zep 3:11; Isa 3:16; Jer 13:15; Jer 49:16; Pro 17:19.
Anchor: **Eze 28:2** ("because your heart is proud, and you have said, 'I am a god'"); **Pro 18:12** ("before destruction a man's heart is haughty, but humility comes before honor").

**100-002:** Term names God's exalted inner-being and his sovereign reversals — the divine transcendence and the justice by which the high are brought low and the low are lifted.
Verses: 2Ch 17:6; Job 36:7; Psa 103:11; Psa 113:5; Psa 131:1; Isa 5:16; Isa 52:13; Isa 55:9; Eze 17:24; Eze 21:26 (overlaps 100-001 as reversal); Job 36:7.
Anchor: **Isa 55:9** ("my ways are higher than your ways and my thoughts than your thoughts"); **Psa 103:11** ("as high as the heavens are above the earth, so great is his steadfast love").

SUMMARY: mti:100 H1361 ga.vah — 33 verses | Relevant: ~22 | Set aside: ~11 | Groups: 2 (100-001, 100-002) | Anchors: Eze 28:2, Pro 18:12, Isa 55:9, Psa 103:11

### mti:101 H1363 go.vah [height] — 16 verses

**Filter decisions:**

- 1Sa 17:4 — Goliath's height in cubits. Physical measurement. **Set aside.**
- 2Ch 3:4 — Temple vestibule height 120 cubits. Physical measurement. **Set aside.**
- 2Ch 32:26 — "Hezekiah humbled himself for the pride of his heart, both he and the inhabitants of Jerusalem." Inner-being humbling of pride. **Relevant** — strong verse (heart named).
- Job 11:8 — "It is higher than heaven — what can you do?" God's wisdom compared to cosmic height. **Relevant** (inner-being of God's wisdom beyond human reach).
- Job 22:12 — "Is not God high in the heavens?" God's transcendent position. **Relevant.**
- Job 40:10 — "Adorn yourself with majesty and dignity." God's challenge to Job — naming divine inner-being attributes. **Relevant.**
- Psa 10:4 — "In the pride of his face the wicked does not seek him; all his thoughts are, 'There is no God.'" Pride of face leading to atheism — inner-being of pride. **Relevant** — strong verse (thoughts named).
- Pro 16:18 — "Pride goes before destruction, and a haughty spirit before a fall." **Relevant** — strong verse.
- Jer 48:29 — "The haughtiness of his heart." Heart named. **Relevant.**
- Eze 1:18 — "Their rims were tall and awesome." Physical/visionary description. **Set aside.**
- Eze 19:11 — "Its height" (vine metaphor). Physical/botanical. **Set aside.**
- Eze 31:10 — "Its heart was proud of its height." Already under H1361 ga.vah — this term (go.vah) here is the "height" that the heart is proud of. **Relevant** (the pride-of-height is through this term).
- Eze 31:14 — "No trees... may grow to towering height." Instruction from judgment. **Set aside.**
- Eze 40:42 — "One cubit high." Physical measurement. **Set aside.**
- Eze 41:8 — "The temple had a raised platform." Architectural. **Set aside.**
- Amo 2:9 — "Whose height was like the height of the cedars." Physical stature comparison. **Set aside.**

**Group formation:**

**101-001:** Term names pride-of-heart as an inner-being condition leading to destruction — the height of self-regard that draws God's judgment.
Verses: 2Ch 32:26; Psa 10:4; Pro 16:18; Jer 48:29; Eze 31:10.
Anchor: **Pro 16:18** ("pride goes before destruction, and a haughty spirit before a fall"); **Psa 10:4** ("in the pride of his face the wicked does not seek him; all his thoughts are, 'There is no God'").

**101-002:** Term names God's transcendent inner-being height — the majesty of God that exceeds all human reach and comprehension.
Verses: Job 11:8; Job 22:12; Job 40:10.
Anchor: **Job 11:8** ("it is higher than heaven — what can you do?").

SUMMARY: mti:101 H1363 go.vah — 16 verses | Relevant: 8 | Set aside: 8 | Groups: 2 (101-001, 101-002) | Anchors: Pro 16:18, Psa 10:4, Job 11:8

## Registry 124 — prophecy

### mti:1060 G4394 profēteia [prophecy] — 19 verses

**Reading summary:** The noun "prophecy." Covers: fulfilment of Isaiah's prophecy about the hardened heart (Mat 13:14); prophecy as a spiritual gift (Rom 12:6; 1Cor 12:10; 13:2/8; 14:6/22); the instruction not to despise prophecy (1Th 5:20); prophecies that guided Timothy (1Ti 1:18); the gift given through prophecy (1Ti 4:14); the origin of prophecy — not from human will but from the Holy Spirit (2Pe 1:20/21); the prophecy of Revelation (Rev 1:3; 11:6; 19:10; 22:7/10/18/19).

**Filter decisions:** All 19 verses relevant. Prophecy is inherently an inner-being phenomenon — it engages the capacity of the person to receive divine speech, and the inner state of those who hear. Key distinctions:

- 2Pe 1:20/21 — "No prophecy was ever produced by the will of man, but men spoke from God as they were carried along by the Holy Spirit." The inner-being origin of prophecy distinguished from human will. **Strong.**
- 1Cor 13:2 — "If I have prophetic powers... but have not love, I am nothing." Prophecy assessed against the inner-being criterion of love. **Strong.**
- Rev 19:10 — "The testimony of Jesus is the spirit of prophecy." The inner-being essence of prophecy. **Strong.**
- 1Ti 1:18 — "The prophecies previously made about you, that by them you may wage the good warfare." Prophecy as inner-being orientation for spiritual warfare. **Strong.**

**Group formation:**

**1060-001:** Term names prophecy as a spiritual gift given through the Spirit — the capacity to receive and speak divine disclosure, distinct from human will and assessed against love.
Verses: Rom 12:6; 1Cor 12:10; 1Cor 13:2; 1Cor 13:8; 1Cor 14:6; 1Cor 14:22; 1Th 5:20; 1Ti 1:18; 1Ti 4:14; 2Pe 1:20; 2Pe 1:21.
Anchor: **2Pe 1:21** ("no prophecy was ever produced by the will of man, but men spoke from God as they were carried along by the Holy Spirit"); **1Cor 13:2** ("if I have prophetic powers... but have not love, I am nothing").

**1060-002:** Term names prophecy as the revelatory word preserved in Scripture and Revelation — the divinely authorised word to which faithful response is required.
Verses: Mat 13:14; Rev 1:3; Rev 11:6; Rev 19:10; Rev 22:7; Rev 22:10; Rev 22:18; Rev 22:19.
Anchor: **Rev 19:10** ("the testimony of Jesus is the spirit of prophecy"); **Rev 22:7** ("blessed is the one who keeps the words of the prophecy of this book").

SUMMARY: mti:1060 G4394 profēteia — 19 verses | Relevant: 19 | Set aside: 0 | Groups: 2 (1060-001, 1060-002) | Anchors: 2Pe 1:21, 1Cor 13:2, Rev 19:10, Rev 22:7

---

### mti:6045 G4395 profēteuō [to prophesy] — 27 verses

**Reading summary:** The verb "to prophesy." Covers: prophesying as claim or mockery directed at Jesus (Mat 26:68; Mar 14:65; Luk 22:64); Isaiah prophesying of the hypocrites (Mat 15:7; Mar 7:6); Caiaphas prophesying unwittingly (Joh 11:51); Zechariah filled with the Spirit and prophesying (Luk 1:67); the outpouring of the Spirit enabling prophecy (Act 2:17/18; 19:6); Philip's daughters who prophesied (Act 21:9); extensive 1Cor 14 community-prophecy discourse; 1Pe 1:10 (prophets who prophesied about grace); Jude 14 (Enoch's prophecy); Rev 10:11 and 11:3 (commissioned prophesying).

**Filter decisions:** All 27 verses relevant — prophesying is an inner-being act of reception and declaration. Key distinctions:

- Luk 1:67 — "His father Zechariah was filled with the Holy Spirit and prophesied." Spirit-filling as the inner condition enabling prophecy. **Strong.**
- Act 2:17/18 — "Your sons and your daughters shall prophesy... they shall prophesy." The Spirit poured out enabling the inner capacity for prophecy universally. **Strong.**
- 1Cor 14:3 — "The one who prophesies speaks to people for their upbuilding and encouragement and consolation." The inner-being effect of prophecy on others. **Strong.**
- 1Cor 14:31 — "You can all prophesy one by one, so that all may learn and all be encouraged." Prophecy as communal inner-being formation. **Strong.**
- 2Pe 2:16 (the donkey restraining the prophet's madness) — the prophet's inner state of madness/presumption rebuked. **Strong.**
- Joh 11:51 — "He did not say this of his own accord, but being high priest that year he prophesied." Prophecy coming from beyond the speaker's own understanding. **Strong.**
- Mat 26:68 / Mar 14:65 / Luk 22:64 — mockery of Jesus's prophetic capacity during trial. Borderline — the term is used as a taunt, testing the inner prophetic capacity. **Relevant** (the mockery reveals what prophecy was understood to entail — inner perception of what is hidden).

**Group formation:**

**6045-001:** Term names prophesying as Spirit-enabled inner-being speech — the act of declaring divine truth through the Holy Spirit's movement on and in the person.
Verses: Luk 1:67; Act 2:17; Act 2:18; Act 19:6; Act 21:9; 1Pe 1:10; Joh 11:51; Jude 14; Rev 10:11; Rev 11:3.
Anchor: **Luk 1:67** ("his father Zechariah was filled with the Holy Spirit and prophesied"); **Act 2:17** ("your sons and your daughters shall prophesy").

**6045-002:** Term names the communal exercise of prophecy — its purpose, order, and effect in building up the inner life of the congregation.
Verses: 1Cor 11:4; 1Cor 11:5; 1Cor 13:9; 1Cor 14:1; 1Cor 14:3; 1Cor 14:4; 1Cor 14:5; 1Cor 14:24; 1Cor 14:31; 1Cor 14:39.
Anchor: **1Cor 14:3** ("the one who prophesies speaks to people for their upbuilding and encouragement and consolation"); **1Cor 14:31** ("you can all prophesy one by one, so that all may learn and all be encouraged").

**6045-003:** Term names the fulfilment and testing of prophetic speech — both the historical fulfilment of prophetic words and the mockery that tests what prophecy truly is.
Verses: Mat 7:22; Mat 11:13; Mat 15:7; Mat 26:68; Mar 7:6; Mar 14:65; Luk 22:64; Act 19:6 (already in 6045-001).
Anchor: **Mat 15:7** ("well did Isaiah prophesy of you hypocrites"); **Mat 26:68** ("prophesy to us, you Christ! Who is it that struck you?" — the mockery revealing prophecy as inner perception of the hidden).

SUMMARY: mti:6045 G4395 profēteuō — 27 verses | Relevant: 27 | Set aside: 0 | Groups: 3 (6045-001 through 6045-003) | Anchors: Luk 1:67, Act 2:17, 1Cor 14:3, 1Cor 14:31, Mat 15:7, Mat 26:68

---

### mti:6044 G4396 profētēs [prophet] — 87 verses

**Reading summary:** The largest term in Registry 124. Covers: references to OT prophets as vehicles of fulfilment-prophecy (the many "spoken by the prophet Isaiah/Jeremiah" formulas in Matthew); Jesus identified as/compared to a prophet (Mat 13:57; 21:11; Mar 6:4; Luk 4:24; 7:16/26/39; 13:33); John the Baptist as more than a prophet (Mat 11:9; Luk 7:26); the Law and the Prophets as scriptural canon (Mat 5:17; 7:12; 11:13; 22:40; Luk 16:16/29); prophets as a charismatic office in the NT church (1Cor 12:28/29; 14:29/32/37; Eph 2:20; 3:5; 4:11); the prophets as those who suffered for speaking God's word (Mat 5:12; 23:29-37; Luk 6:23; 11:47-50; 13:34; 1Th 2:15; Jam 5:10; Rev 11:10; 16:6; 18:20/24); prophetic figures in Revelation (Rev 10:7; 22:6/9); the Cretan prophet (Tit 1:12); and Elijah-as-prophet.

**Filter decisions:**

The large majority are relevant through one of three inner-being dimensions:
(A) The prophet as one whose inner being is specially oriented toward God for reception and declaration of his word;
(B) The community's inner-being response to prophets — reception, rejection, longing;
(C) The prophet's suffering as inner-being testimony.

*Set aside — purely fulfilment-formula uses (narrative without inner-being engagement through "prophet" specifically):*
Mat 1:22; 2:5/15/17/23; 3:3; 4:14; 8:17; 12:17; 13:35; 21:4; 24:15; 27:9 — these quote "spoken by the prophet" as a narrator's attribution formula. The inner-being content is in the prophecy itself, not in "prophet" as the term at term level. **Set aside** (13 verses).

*Set aside — Caiaphas (Joh 11:51 classified under G4395 above); 2Pe 2:16 (donkey and prophet's madness — already classified under G4395 above).*

*Relevant — all remaining:*

Key strong verses:
- Luk 1:76 — "You, child, will be called the prophet of the Most High; for you will go before the Lord to prepare his ways." John the Baptist's prophetic vocation named at birth — inner calling. **Strong.**
- Luk 4:24 — "No prophet is acceptable in his hometown." The prophet's inner condition of rejection in his own community. **Strong.**
- Mar 7:6 / Mat 15:7 — Isaiah prophesying about the hypocrites whose heart is far from God — the prophetic word penetrating to the inner condition. Already classified under G4395.
- 1Cor 14:32 — "The spirits of prophets are subject to prophets." The self-regulatory inner-being of the prophetic spirit. **Strong.**
- 1Cor 14:37 — "If anyone thinks that he is a prophet, or spiritual, he should acknowledge that the things I am writing to you are a command of the Lord." The test of true inner prophetic understanding. **Strong.**
- Rev 22:6 — "The God of the spirits of the prophets." The prophets' inner spirits in relation to God. **Strong.**
- 1Pe 1:10 — Already classified under G4395 but relevant here too: "The prophets who prophesied about the grace that was to be yours searched and inquired carefully." The inner-being search and inquiry of the prophets. **Strong.**
- Jam 5:10 — "Take the prophets who spoke in the name of the Lord as an example of suffering and patience." The inner-being of prophetic endurance. **Strong.**

**Group formation:**

**6044-001:** Term names the prophet as one specially oriented toward God — called to receive and declare his word, with an inner orientation that precedes and shapes their speech.
Verses: Luk 1:70; Luk 1:76; Mat 11:9; Mat 13:17; Luk 7:16; Luk 7:26; Luk 7:39; Luk 13:33; Mar 6:4; Luk 4:24; Heb 1:1; Heb 11:32; Rev 22:6; Rev 10:7; 1Cor 14:29; 1Cor 14:32; 1Cor 14:37; Eph 2:20; Eph 3:5; Eph 4:11; 1Cor 12:28; 1Cor 12:29; Tit 1:12; Act 19:6 (classified under G4395).
Anchor: **Rev 22:6** ("the God of the spirits of the prophets, has sent his angel to show his servants what must soon take place"); **1Cor 14:37** ("if anyone thinks that he is a prophet, or spiritual, he should acknowledge that the things I am writing to you are a command of the Lord").

**6044-002:** Term names the prophet as the one who suffers for God's word — the inner-being posture of endurance under rejection and persecution as the mark of authentic prophecy.
Verses: Mat 5:12; Mat 23:29/30/31/34/37; Luk 6:23; Luk 11:47/49/50; Luk 13:34; Luk 13:28; 1Th 2:15; Jam 5:10; Rev 11:10; Rev 16:6; Rev 18:20/24; Rom 11:3.
Anchor: **Jam 5:10** ("take the prophets who spoke in the name of the Lord as an example of suffering and patience"); **Mat 23:37** ("O Jerusalem, Jerusalem, the city that kills the prophets and stones those who are sent to it!").

**6044-003:** Term names the prophetic canon — the Law and the Prophets as the scriptural testimony that orients the inner life toward God's purposes.
Verses: Mat 5:17; Mat 5:25; Mat 7:12; Mat 11:13; Mat 22:40; Luk 16:16; Luk 16:29; Rom 1:2; Rom 3:21; 2Pe 3:2; Luk 10:24; Mat 16:14; Mar 6:15; Mar 8:28; Luk 1:70; Luk 9:8/19; Mar 1:2; Mar 11:32; Luk 3:4; Luk 4:17; Luk 4:27; Luk 11:49; Mat 14:5; Mat 21:11/26/46; Mat 26:56; Mat 12:39; Rev 22:9.
Anchor: **Mat 5:17** ("do not think that I have come to abolish the Law or the Prophets; I have not come to abolish them but to fulfill them"); **Rom 1:2** ("which he promised beforehand through his prophets in the holy Scriptures").

Note: 1Pe 1:10 classified primarily under G4395 (prophesying); included in 6044-001 as the prophets' inner searching.

SUMMARY: mti:6044 G4396 profētēs — 87 verses | Relevant: ~74 | Set aside: ~13 (fulfilment formulas) | Groups: 3 (6044-001 through 6044-003) | Anchors: Rev 22:6, 1Cor 14:37, Jam 5:10, Mat 23:37, Mat 5:17, Rom 1:2

---

- Rom 16:26 — "Through the prophetic writings has been made known to all nations, according to the command of the eternal God, to bring about the obedience of faith." The prophetic writings as the vehicle for inner-being transformation — producing the obedience of faith across the nations. **Relevant** — strong verse (faith and obedience as inner-being outcomes of prophetic writing).

The prophetic word as a lamp; the morning star rising in the hearts. **Relevant** — strong verse (heart explicitly named as the destination of prophetic light).

**Group formation:**

Verses: Rom 16:26; 2Pe 1:19.

### mti:6048 G4398 profētis [prophetess] — 2 verses

**Filter decisions:**
- Luk 2:36 — "There was a prophetess, Anna, the daughter of Phanuel, of the tribe of Asher." Anna named as a prophetess — her identity and vocation. **Relevant** (the prophetess role names a specific inner calling and spiritual capacity for receiving and declaring divine truth; the term defines the inner-being orientation of her life).
- Rev 2:20 — "That woman Jezebel, who calls herself a prophetess and is teaching and seducing my servants to practice sexual immorality." A false prophetess — the claimed inner role used to mislead. **Relevant** (the false claim to prophetic inner capacity as the basis for destructive teaching).

**Group formation:**
**6048-001:** Term names the prophetess — whether the authentic inner calling (Anna, devoted to God in prayer and fasting) or the false claim to prophetic authority used for seduction.
Verses: Luk 2:36; Rev 2:20.
Anchor: **Luk 2:36** ("there was a prophetess, Anna... she did not depart from the temple, worshiping with fasting and prayer night and day"); **Rev 2:20** ("Jezebel, who calls herself a prophetess and is teaching and seducing my servants").

SUMMARY: mti:6048 G4398 profētis — 2 verses | Relevant: 2 | Set aside: 0 | Groups: 1 (6048-001) | Anchors: Luk 2:36, Rev 2:20

---

### mti:6046 G5578 pseudoprofētēs [false prophet] — 11 verses

**Reading summary:** "False prophet." Covers: the warning against false prophets who come in sheep's clothing but are inwardly ravenous wolves (Mat 7:15); false prophets arising to lead astray in the last days (Mat 24:11/24; Mar 13:22); woe to those praised as false prophets were (Luk 6:26); Bar-Jesus the Jewish false prophet (Act 13:6); false prophets who arose among the people (2Pe 2:1); the test of spirits against false prophets (1Jo 4:1); the eschatological False Prophet in Revelation (Rev 16:13; 19:20; 20:10).

**Filter decisions:** All 11 verses relevant — the false prophet is an inner-being figure par excellence, characterised by deceptive inner orientation masked by outward appearance.

Key verses:
- Mat 7:15 — "Beware of false prophets, who come to you in sheep's clothing but inwardly are ravenous wolves." The critical word: *inwardly* — the false prophet's inner-being is the opposite of their outer presentation. **Strong** — directly names the inner/outer contrast.
- 1Jo 4:1 — "Do not believe every spirit, but test the spirits to see whether they are from God, for many false prophets have gone out into the world." Testing the inner spirit-source of prophetic claims. **Strong.**
- 2Pe 2:1 — "False prophets also arose among the people... who will secretly bring in destructive heresies, even denying the Master who bought them." The false prophet's inner denial and secret corruption. **Strong.**

**Group formation:**

**6046-001:** Term names the false prophet as an inwardly deceptive figure — whose inner orientation is predatory, self-serving, or demonic, masked by an outward appearance of authenticity.
Verses: Mat 7:15; Mat 24:11; Mat 24:24; Mar 13:22; Luk 6:26; Act 13:6; 2Pe 2:1; 1Jo 4:1.
Anchor: **Mat 7:15** ("false prophets, who come to you in sheep's clothing but inwardly are ravenous wolves"); **1Jo 4:1** ("test the spirits to see whether they are from God, for many false prophets have gone out into the world").

**6046-002:** Term names the eschatological False Prophet — the end-times figure of deception who drives worship of the beast, ultimately destroyed with him.
Verses: Rev 16:13; Rev 19:20; Rev 20:10.
Anchor: **Rev 19:20** ("the false prophet who in its presence had done the signs by which he deceived those who had received the mark of the beast").

SUMMARY: mti:6046 G5578 pseudoprofētēs — 11 verses | Relevant: 11 | Set aside: 0 | Groups: 2 (6046-001, 6046-002) | Anchors: Mat 7:15, 1Jo 4:1, Rev 19:20
